# Intelligence {#intelligence}

[A Brief History of Intelligence: Evolution, AI, and the Five Breakthroughs That Made Our Brains](https://tinyurl.com/2ctrqapu) by Max S. Bennett

## **Adaptability Intelligence** {#adaptability-intelligence}

* [Screw Emotional Intelligence \-- Here’s The Key To The Future Of Work](https://www.fastcompany.com/40522394/screw-emotional-intelligence-heres-the-real-key-to-the-future-of-work) by Natalie Fratto   
  The importance of Adaptability Intelligence

* [5 Habits That Let Emotionally Intelligent People Adapt To Anything](https://www.fastcompany.com/40514381/5-habits-that-help-emotionally-intelligent-people-adapt-to-change) by Harvey Deutschendorf 

* [On Intelligence: How a New Understanding of the Brain Will Lead to the Creation of Truly Intelligent Machines](https://www.amazon.com/Intelligence-Understanding-Creation-Intelligent-Machines-ebook/dp/B003J4VE5Y/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1530304508&sr=8-2&keywords=on+intelligence) by Jeff Hawkins and Sandra Blakeslee 

* [Stealing Fire: : How Silicon Valley, the Navy SEALs, and Maverick Scientists Are Revolutionizing the Way We Live and Work](https://www.amazon.com/Stealing-Fire-Maverick-Scientists-Revolutionizing-ebook/dp/B01GCCT3G6/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1530304435&sr=8-2&keywords=stealing+fire) by Steven Kotler and Jamie Wheal . Cultivating Different Mind States.

———————————————————

## **Emotional Intelligence** {#emotional-intelligence}

* [Emotional Intelligence](https://www.amazon.com/Emotional-Intelligence-Matter-More-Than/dp/055338371X/ref=sr_1_2?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1536067411&sr=1-2&keywords=Emotional+Intelligence+by+Daniel+Goleman) by Daniel Goleman   
  Deepening personal awareness and interpersonal connection produces more sustainable leadership results.

* [Emotional Intelligence 2.0](https://www.amazon.com/Emotional-Intelligence-2-0-Travis-Bradberry/dp/0974320625/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&qid=1525783202&sr=8-1-spons&keywords=emotional+intelligence+2.0&psc=1&linkCode=sl1&tag=readingraphic-20&linkId=4e533a863ce32def64a0db4191304389) by Travis Bradberry, Jean Greaves builds on the Goleman’s framework   
    
* [Working with Emotional Intelligence](https://www.amazon.com/Working-Emotional-Intelligence-Daniel-Goleman/dp/0553378589/ref=sr_1_3?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1534039196&sr=1-3&keywords=Working+with+Emotional+Intelligence) by Daniel Goleman is an anecdotally driven exploration of the concepts

* [Emotional Intelligence has 12 Elements. Which Do You Need to Work On?](https://hbr.org/2017/02/emotional-intelligence-has-12-elements-which-do-you-need-to-work-on) by Daniel Goleman and Richard E. Boyatzis

* [Primal Leadership: Realizing the Power of Emotional Intelligence](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1422168034/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_bibl_vppi_i1) By Daniel Goleman, Richard Boyatzis, Annie McKee  [HBR Paper: Primal Leadership: The Hidden Driver of Great Performance](https://hbr.org/2001/12/primal-leadership-the-hidden-driver-of-great-performance)   
  (annotated by [Larry Boyer](https://twitter.com/larryboyer)) Primal Leadership is my favorite leadership development book. It starts with a discussion of brain science so the reader can understand the physical connection to emotional responses and therefore our leadership skills. Whether you are a fan or skeptic of leadership development books, this is one of the few books out there that can relate to most any view and transform your way of thinking.

* [HBR Articles](https://docs.google.com/document/d/10AKk5God5Jp4TTQzRsvSzLCByHNbgdaiRPmhsXl_9nA/edit#bookmark=id.bxgu4hlxqlt1) on Emotional Intelligence

* Building the Emotional Intelligence of Groups by Vanessa Urch Druskat and Steven Wolff (HBR article)

* [The Emotionally Intelligent Manager’s Guide To Leading Remote Teams](https://www.fastcompany.com/40495919/the-emotionally-intelligent-managers-guide-to-leading-remote-teams) by Suzan Bond (article)

* [Do These 5 Emotionally Intelligent Things Within 5 Minutes Of Meeting Someone](https://www.fastcompany.com/40514381/5-habits-that-help-emotionally-intelligent-people-adapt-to-change) by Harvey Deutschendorf  (article)

* [Emotional Agility: Get Unstuck, Embrace Change, and Thrive in Work and Life](https://www.amazon.com/Emotional-Agility-Unstuck-Embrace-Change/dp/1592409490/ref=tmm_hrd_swatch_0?_encoding=UTF8&qid=1519741661&sr=8-1) by Susan David 

* [The Five Big Personality Traits](https://getpocket.com/a/read/2060151241) By Kendra Cherry, [www.verywellmind.com](http://www.verywellmind.com)

* [Give and Take](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0143124986/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_bibl_vppi_i1) by Adam Grant

* [Insight: The Surprising Truth About How Others See Us, How We See Ourselves, and Why the Answers Matter More Than We Think](https://www.amazon.com/Insight-Surprising-Others-Ourselves-Answers/dp/0525573941/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1546031565&sr=8-1&keywords=insight+by+tasha) by Tasha Eurich

* [Mindwise: Why We Misunderstand What Others Think, Believe, Feel, and Want](https://www.amazon.com/Mindwise-Misunderstand-Others-Think-Believe/dp/030774356X/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1546459226&sr=8-1&keywords=mindwise+nicholas+epley)  by Nicholas Epley. Review: If you wish to know what is on other people's mind, don't guess. Ask them. That is the main message of this book, and it is brought across in a very readable, entertaining and convincing manner. Both scientific observations and anecdotes are presented to demonstrate how we often under-interpret or over-interpret the activities of other people's minds. Our biases are presented in systematic order, showing how our guesses and inferences may go dreadfully wrong. Therefore, although the point may already be familiar to the reader, this book is a very useful reminder and definitely worth reading. Talk to people. And listen to their answers.

* [The Road Back to You: An Enneagram Journey to Self-Discovery](https://www.amazon.com/gp/slredirect/picassoRedirect.html/ref=pa_sp_atf_aps_sr_pg1_1?ie=UTF8&adId=A04814262CWP4MIM55A9Y&url=%2FRoad-Back-You-Enneagram-Self-Discovery%2Fdp%2F0830846190%2Fref%3Dsr_1_1_sspa%3Fcrid%3D3GO1LE7HR56WR%26keywords%3Dthe%2Broad%2Bback%2Bto%2Byou%26qid%3D1575123736%26sprefix%3Dthe%2Broad%2B%252Caps%252C147%26sr%3D8-1-spons%26psc%3D1&qualifier=1575123736&id=5705278610393122&widgetName=sp_atf) by Ian Morgan Cron and Suzanne Stabile 

**Empathy**

* [Empathy exploration](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1YzY26H0CZIFgY6yOZoNFYVZ7RmawUtdDN2COsh9kJmw/edit)

* [The Empathy Effect: Seven Neuroscience-Based Keys for Transforming the Way We Live, Love, Work, and Connect Across Differences](https://www.amazon.com/Empathy-Effect-Neuroscience-Based-Transforming-Differences/dp/1683640284/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1545831739&sr=8-1&keywords=THE+EMPATHY+EFFECT) by Helen Riess and Liz Neporent

## **Decision-Making** {#decision-making}

* [Predictably Irrational](https://www.amazon.com/Predictably-Irrational-Revised-Expanded-Decisions/dp/0061353248/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1527941880&sr=8-1&keywords=Predictability+Irrational) by Dan Ariely [book in pdf](http://radio.shabanali.com/predictable.pdf) (on [Google Drive](https://drive.google.com/open?id=1MYz1J3hKKZ51_Cg0jr3gJQiFzomiuFDe))

* [Nudge: Improving decisions about health, wealth and happiness](https://www.amazon.com/Nudge-Improving-Decisions-Health-Happiness/dp/014311526X/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1527942165&sr=8-1&keywords=Nudge%3A+Improving+decisions+about+health%2C+wealth+and+happiness) by Richard H. Thaler, Cass R. Sunstein 

* [Thinking, Fast And Slow](https://www.amazon.com/Thinking-Fast-Slow-Daniel-Kahneman/dp/0374533555/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1527942150&sr=8-1&keywords=Thinking%2C+Fast+And+Slow+by+Daniel+Kahneman) by Daniel Kahneman 

* [Farsighted: How We Make the Decisions That Matter the Most](https://www.amazon.com/Farsighted-Make-Decisions-That-Matter/dp/1594488215/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Farsighted&qid=1552056263&s=gateway&sr=8-1) by Steven Johnson

* [Decisions, Decisions, Decisions](http://www.npr.org/programs/ted-radio-hour/519264798/decisions-decisions-decisions), TedX Hour

* HBR Collection: [On Making Smart Decisions](https://docs.google.com/document/d/10AKk5God5Jp4TTQzRsvSzLCByHNbgdaiRPmhsXl_9nA/edit#bookmark=id.c8xq5uxzvr1k)

* [The Power of Collective Wisdom and the Trap of Collective Folly](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1576754456/ref=as_li_tf_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=theworldcafe-20&linkCode=as2&camp=1789&creative=9325&creativeASIN=1576754456) by Alan Briskin, Sheryl Ericson, John Ott, and Tom Callanan

* [A Facilitator's Guide to Participatory Decision-Making](https://www.amazon.com/Facilitators-Participatory-Decision-Making-Jossey-bass-Management/dp/1118404955/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1534041438&sr=1-1&keywords=A+Facilitator%27s+Guide+to+Participatory+Decision-Making) by Sam Kaner

* [Superforecasting: The Art and Science of Prediction](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2015%20Reviews/Scoring%20Forecast%20Accuracy.pdf) by Philip Tetlock and Dan Gardner ([review](https://jamesstuber.com/super-forecasting/))

* [Algorithms to Live By: The Computer Science of Human Decisions](https://www.amazon.com/Algorithms-Live-Computer-Science-Decisions/dp/B01D24NAL6/ref=sr_1_3?keywords=algorithm+decision+making&qid=1576175330&s=books&sr=1-3) by Brian Christian, Tom Griffiths, et al. 

* [Fooled by Randomness: The Hidden Role of Chance](https://www.amazon.com/Fooled-Randomness-Hidden-Markets-Incerto/dp/0812975219/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Fooled+By+Randomness&qid=1552056623&s=books&sr=1-1) by Nassim Nicholas Taleb (v1 on [Google Drive](https://drive.google.com/open?id=1yXDyHa-zhrqhKWQ3XyM0DiFKGeoja46x))   
  This book will show you perfectly why life is not reasonable and how it passes in a very non-linear way. This book is about the part of fortunes in our lives and how we perceive it. The writer contends that we severely underestimate the realm of possibilities when we make decisions, and thereby expose ourselves to risks. Most fascinating is the blend of disciplines in this book. Read this book, it might change your thinking and reasoning.

* [Seeking Wisdom](https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Wisdom-Darwin-Munger-3rd/dp/1578644283/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Seeking+Wisdom&qid=1552056559&s=books&sr=1-1) by Peter Bevelin: mental models of Charlie Munger, Warren Buffett

* [Behave: The Biology of Humans at Our Best and Worst](https://www.amazon.com/Behave-Biology-Humans-Best-Worst-ebook/dp/B01IAUGC5S/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=behave+by+robert&qid=1590605790&sr=8-1) by Robert M. Sapolsky

———————————————————

## **Enlightenment and Rationality**  {#enlightenment-and-rationality}

* [The Power of Now: a Guide To Spiritual Enlightenment](https://www.amazon.com/Power-Now-Eckhart-Tolle/dp/0340733500?tag=livelearnev01-20) by Eckhart Tolle 

* [Enlightenment Now](https://www.amazon.com/Enlightenment-Now-Science-Humanism-Progress/dp/0525427570/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1523752190&sr=1-1&keywords=steven+pinker) by Steven Pinker

* [The Four Agreements: A Practical Guide to Personal Freedom](https://www.amazon.com/Four-Agreements-Practical-Personal-Freedom/dp/1878424319/ref=pd_sim_14_4?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=1878424319&pd_rd_r=XQ70WZ816QWJ12DTNS7V&pd_rd_w=yUL63&pd_rd_wg=qrFmi&psc=1&refRID=XQ70WZ816QWJ12DTNS7V) by Don Miguel Ruiz

* [When Breath Becomes Air](https://www.amazon.com/When-Breath-Becomes-Paul-Kalanithi/dp/081298840X/ref=zg_bs_11023_2?_encoding=UTF8&psc=1&refRID=43MWNQHXTH81D0H2QYG1) by Paul Kalanithi

* [The Power of Your Subconscious Mind](https://www.amazon.com/Power-Your-Subconscious-Mind/dp/160459201X/ref=zg_bs_11023_10?_encoding=UTF8&psc=1&refRID=43MWNQHXTH81D0H2QYG1) by Joseph Murphy 

* [Everything Happens for a Reason: And Other Lies I've Loved](https://www.amazon.com/Everything-Happens-Reason-Other-Loved-ebook/dp/B071YY6X9Q/ref=sr_1_1?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1544633655&sr=1-1&keywords=everything+happens+for+a+reason+and+other+lies+i%27ve+loved) by Kate Bowler (Bill Gates [review](https://www.gatesnotes.com/Books/Everything-Happens-for-a-Reason))

* [Stillness Speaks: Whispers of Now](https://tinyurl.com/ytwet66d) by Eckhart Tolle

* [The Enigma of Reason](https://www.amazon.com/Enigma-Reason-Hugo-Mercier/dp/067423782X/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Enigma+of+Reason&qid=1574284268&sr=8-1) by Hugo Mercier, Dan Sperber 


———————————————————

## **Expand Your Brain**  {#expand-your-brain}

Curated by James Altucher, businessinsider.com

* [Mastery](https://www.amazon.com/Unknown-Mastery/dp/B00A6G9CGG/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Mastery+by+Robert+Greene&qid=1575169943&s=books&sr=1-1) by Robert Greene  
  This book is like a curated version of 1,000 biographies all under the guise, "how to become a master at what you love." 

* [Bold: How to Go Big, Create Wealth and Impact the World](https://www.amazon.com/Bold-Create-Wealth-Impact-World/dp/1476709580/ref=sr_1_fkmr0_1?keywords=bold+by+peter+diamond+is+and+steven+kotler&qid=1575169958&s=books&sr=1-1-fkmr0) by Peter Diamondis and Steven Kotler  
  Basically if you want to know the future, read this. Supplement it with "Abundance" by the same two and "Tomorrowland" by Steven Kotler" and even "The Rational Optimist" by Matt Ridley. I feel "Abundance" is like a sequel to "The Rational Optimist". So I'm giving you four books with one recommendation. 

* [Outliers: The Story of Success](https://www.amazon.com/Outliers-Story-Success-Malcolm-Gladwell/dp/0316017930/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Outliers+by+Malcolm+Gladwell&qid=1575169994&s=books&sr=1-1) by Malcolm Gladwell   
  Gladwell is not the first person to come up with the 10,000 hour rule. Nor is he the first person to document what it takes to become the best in the world at something. But his stories are so great as he explains these deep concepts. How did the Beatles become the best? Why are professional hockey players born in January, February and March? 

* [Where Good Ideas Come From: The Natural History of Innovation](https://www.amazon.com/Where-Good-Ideas-Come-Innovation/dp/1594485380/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Where+Good+Ideas+Come+From+by+Steven+Johnson&qid=1575170013&s=books&sr=1-1) by Steven Johnson  
  Also add to this: "How We Got to Now" by Steven Johnson. Don't believe the myth of the lonely genius. Ideas come from a confluence of history, "the adjacent possible" specific geographic locations, etc. The connections Johnson makes are brilliant. For instance, The Gutenberg Press (which, in itself, was invented because of improvements in sewing looms), made everyone realize they had bad vision. So the science of lenses was created. So microscopes were eventually created. So germs were eventually discovered. So modern medical science was discovered. And so on. Johnson is a thinker and a linker and tells a good story.

* [Man's Search For Meaning](https://www.amazon.com/Mans-Search-Meaning-Viktor-Frankl/dp/0807014273/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=man%27s+search+for+meaning+by+viktor+frankl&qid=1575170036&s=books&sr=1-1) by Victor Frankl  
  Don't read it for the Holocaust. Or psychological theory. Read it because when you're about halfway through you will realize your life is no longer the same. And next time you get a chance to whisper in the ear of someone about to kill himself, whisper words from this book. 

* [Born Standing Up: A Comic’s Life](https://www.amazon.com/Born-Standing-Up-Comics-Life/dp/1416553657/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Born+Standing+Up&qid=1575170056&s=books&sr=1-1) by Steve Martin  
  And while you are at it, throw in "Bounce" by Mathew Syed, who was the UK Ping Pong champion when he was younger. I love any book where someone took their passion, documented it, and shared it with us. That's when you can see the subtleties, the hard work, the luck, the talent, the skill, all come together to form a champion. Heck, throw in, "An Astronaut's Guide to Earth" by Commander Chris Hadfield.

* [Zero to One: Notes on Startups, or How to Build the Future](https://www.amazon.com/Zero-One-Notes-Startups-Future/dp/0804139296/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Zero+to+One+by+Peter+Thiel&qid=1575170076&s=books&sr=1-1) by Peter Thiel  
  There's a lot of business books out there. 99% of them are BS. Read this one. So many concepts really changed my attitude about not only business but capitalism.  Thiel, the founder of PayPal, and first investor in Facebook, is brilliant in how he simply shares his theories on building a billion dollar business. I love his story on my podcast what exactly happened in the room when a 24 year old Mark Zuckerberg was offered $250,000,000 and refused it in two minutes. 

* [Quiet: The Power of Introverts in a World That Can't Stop Talking](https://www.amazon.com/Quiet-Power-Introverts-World-Talking/dp/0307352153/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Quiet+by+Susan+Cain&qid=1575170110&s=books&sr=1-1) by Susan Cain  
  Probably half the world is introverts. Maybe more. It's not an easy life to live. I sometimes have that feeling in a room full of people, "uh-oh. I just shut down. I can't talk anymore and there's a lock on my mouth and this crowd threw away the key." Do you ever get that feeling? Please? I hope you do. Let's try to lock eyes at the party.  "Quiet" shows the reader how to unlock the secret powers that probably half the world needs to unlock.  And, please Susan Cain come on my podcast. 

* [Antifragile: Things That Gain from Disorder](https://www.amazon.com/Antifragile-Things-That-Disorder-Incerto/dp/0812979680/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Antifragile+by+Nassim&qid=1575170137&s=books&sr=1-1) by Nassim Taleb   
  And throw in "The Black Swan"   and "Fooled by Randomness."  "Fragile" means if you hit something might break.  "Resilient" means if you hit something, it will stay the same. On my podcast, Nassim discusses "Antifragility" — building a system, even one that works for you on a personal level, where you are if you harm yourself in some way it becomes stronger.  That podcast changed my life. He discusses Antifragility throughout history, up to our current economic situation, and even in our personal situations.

* [Mindset: How You Can Fulfill Your Potential](https://www.amazon.com/Mindset-Psychology-Carol-S-Dweck/dp/0345472322/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533945675&sr=8-1&keywords=mindset+carol+s.+dweck&smid=ATVPDKIKX0DER) by Carol Dweck   \-- related: [Do You Have the Right Mindset for Success?](https://www.fastcompany.com/660047/do-you-have-right-mindset-success)  
  Growth mindset. Again, I am fascinated by the field of mastery.  Not self-improvement (eat well, sleep well, etc) but on how can you continue a path of improvement so that you can really enjoy the subtleties at a very deep level of whatever it is you love.  Carol Dweck, through massive research and storytelling, shows the reader how to continue on the path of improvement and why so many people fall off that path. 

---

# Change {#change}

## **Recommended**

* [Transitions: Making Sense Of Life's Changes](https://www.amazon.com/Transitions-Making-Sense-Lifes-Changes-ebook/dp/B004ZY23TS/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1503964824&sr=8-1&keywords=william+bridges+transitions) by William Bridges  (Author)

* [Immunity to Change: How to Overcome It and Unlock the Potential in Yourself and Your Organization](http://www.amazon.com/Immunity-Change-Potential-Organization-Leadership/dp/1422117367) by Kegan and Lahey. [Synopsis](https://www.extension.harvard.edu/inside-extension/surprising-reason-we-dont-keep-our-resolutions-how-overcome-it) from Harvard program.

* [The Real Reason Why People Won't Change](https://drive.google.com/a/google.com/file/d/0Bw6lqrwRclAkZTduNnNPeXV1c1k/view) HBR Article

* [No One Understands You, And What to Do About it](https://www.amazon.com/One-Understands-You-What-About/dp/1625274122/ref=asap_bc?ie=UTF8) by Heidi Grant Halvorson (Columbia Professor, Thinkers50 and Lead at NeuroLeadership Institute) 

* [Tell Me So I Can Hear You](https://www.amazon.com/Tell-Can-Hear-You-Developmental/dp/1612508812/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1516890927&sr=1-1&keywords=eleanor+drago-severson) by Eleanor Drago-Severson (also a Columbia Professor) 

* [Appreciative Inquiry: A Positive Revolution in Change](https://www.amazon.com/Appreciative-Inquiry-Positive-Revolution-Change/dp/1576753565/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1517685956&sr=8-1&keywords=Appreciative+Inquiry%3A+A+Positive+Revolution+in+Change) by David Cooperrider  [talk](https://appreciativeinquiry.champlain.edu/learn/appreciative-inquiry-introduction/)  and [paper](https://drive.google.com/open?id=1Vw7EoZcQv04mQrLXERZ3uhU_KHwA51M3JrvUdMDxKO4)

* [Train Your Mind, Change Your Brain: How a New Science Reveals Our Extraordinary Potential to Transform Ourselves](https://www.amazon.com/Train-Your-Mind-Change-Brain-ebook/dp/B000WJVMJM/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=developgoodhabits-20&linkId=605d9360b2bd62410228964d43fc3e23) by Sharon Begley 

* [Organize Your Mind, Organize Your Life: Train Your Brain to Get More Done in Less Time](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00693EPX0/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=developgoodhabits-20&linkId=44fb3b1e0562d76cfe4695ba9674ccc1) by Margaret Moore and Paul Hammerness

* [The Evolving Self: Problem and Process in Human Development](https://www.amazon.com/Evolving-Self-Problem-Process-Development/dp/0674272315/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1519338052&sr=8-1&keywords=evolving+self+kegan) by Robert Kegan      
  [Kegan’s Theory of Adult Development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Kegan) in wikipedia and Mediums [part one](https://medium.com/@NataliMorad/how-to-be-an-adult-kegans-theory-of-adult-development-d63f4311b553) and [part two](https://medium.com/@NataliMorad/part-2-how-to-be-an-adult-kegans-theory-of-adult-development-ddf057b4517bhttps://medium.com/@NataliMorad/part-2-how-to-be-an-adult-kegans-theory-of-adult-development-ddf057b4517b)

* [Leadership on the Line](https://www.amazon.com/Leadership-Line-New-Preface-Staying/dp/1633692833/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1519338110&sr=8-2&keywords=heifetz+leadership+on+the+line) by Ronald Heifetz

* [Presence-Based Coaching: Cultivating Self-Generative Leaders Through Mind, Body, and Heart](https://www.amazon.com/Presence-Based-Coaching-Cultivating-Self-Generative-Leaders/dp/0470325097/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1519338155&sr=1-1&keywords=silsbee) by Doug Silsbee

* [The Life-Changing Magic of Tidying Up: The Japanese Art of Decluttering and Organizing](https://www.amazon.com/Life-Changing-Magic-Tidying-Decluttering-Organizing-ebook/dp/B00KK0PICK/ref=sr_1_2?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1529602237&sr=1-2&keywords=the+art+of+tidying+up+marie+kondo)  by Marie Kondo

* [Liminal Thinking: Create the Change You Want by Changing the Way You Think](https://www.amazon.com/Liminal-Thinking-Create-Change-Changing/dp/1933820462/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1513566521&sr=8-1&keywords=liminal+thinking) by Dave Gray

* [Be More Pirate](https://amzn.to/2LgM9Uo) by Sam Conniff Allende. How you show up at work and cause disruption: make good trouble; push back for the good of the org; sometimes status quo needs to be disrupted.

———————————————————

## **Inspiring Change**

Curated by Chip Heath and Dan Heath, jeffbullas.com

* [The 4 Hour Work Week](https://www.amazon.com/4-Hour-Workweek-Escape-Live-Anywhere/dp/0307465357/ref=sr_1_3?keywords=The+4+Hour+Work+Week&qid=1575170378&s=books&sr=1-3) by Tim Ferriss  
  I read this book about 5 years ago when the future promise of the web was starting to become very real as social media took hold. Twitter was just starting and Facebook was getting traction. The book promises to take you from the drudgery of the day job to the dream of doing what you love doing and monetize it on the web.

* [The Element: How Finding Your Passion Changes Everything](https://www.amazon.com/Element-Finding-Passion-Changes-Everything/dp/0143116738/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Element+by+Ken+Robinson&qid=1575170418&s=books&sr=1-1) by Ken Robinson  
  As I have been a teacher in a previous life, it resonated with me. It provides an inspiring insight into how when finding your passion and combining it with your innate abilities and talents can take a life from drudgery to a masterpiece. He calls this intersection “The Element”. Included are examples from famous people that have have found the element such as Paul McCartney, Richard Branson and Arianna Huffington.

* [Made to Stick: Why Some Ideas Survive and Others Die](https://www.amazon.com/Made-Stick-Ideas-Survive-Others/dp/1400064287/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=made+to+stick&qid=1575170488&s=books&sr=1-1) by Chip Heath and Dan Heath  
  Simplicity, unexpectedness, concreteness,credibility, emotions and stories. If you want to improve your communication skills and make your ideas memorable, then this book should not be ignored.

* [On Writing: A Memoir of the Craft](https://www.amazon.com/Writing-10th-Anniversary-Memoir-Craft/dp/1439156816/ref=sr_1_1?crid=Q7QI8WX6G0GY&keywords=stephen+king+on+writing&qid=1575142212&sprefix=stephen+king+on+%2Caps%2C145&sr=8-1) by Stephen King   
  Stephen King is known more for fiction books than non-fiction. This book is part memoir (for the first 100 pages) and then he reveals in the last 200 pages the basic toolkit for becoming a good or even a great writer. His passion for writing is obvious and compelling. His life journey is revealing. Three key messages impressed me…the importance of simplicity, starting and persistence. That is just the start of what you will find between its covers. This book is not just about writing, it is about life. 

* [ReWork](https://www.amazon.com/Rework-Jason-Fried/dp/0307463745/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=ReWork+by+Jason+Fried+and+David+Hansson&qid=1575170558&s=books&sr=1-1) by Jason Fried and David Hansson  
  This book is written by the founders of 37 Signals which is a very successful software development company (ever heard of the software “Basecamp”). What you find is a lot of ideas to rework your business that they have discovered from personal experience. If you are living in the 21st century and want to know how business is being reinvented that works in a knowledge economy then it is worth reading. Short punchy chapters packed full of cool ideas and inspiration.

* [Start with Why: How Great Leaders Inspire Everyone to Take Action](https://www.amazon.com/Start-Why-Leaders-Inspire-Everyone/dp/1591846447/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Start+with+Why+by+Simon+Sinek&qid=1575170572&s=books&sr=1-1) by Simon Sinek  
  Simon Sinek impressed me when I heard him speak. His core message is what makes leaders great and how that leads to companies that succeed and excel. He uses examples (stories) starting with the Wright Brothers, Martin Luther King and Steve Jobs. Get the “Why” right and then the fun starts. It is also about the art of influence.

* [The New Rules of Marketing and PR: How to Use Social Media, Online Video, Mobile Applications, Blogs, Newsjacking, and Viral Marketing to Reach Buyers Directly](https://www.amazon.com/New-Rules-Marketing-Applications-Newsjacking/dp/1119362415/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+New+Rules+of+Marketing+and+PR&qid=1575170617&s=books&sr=1-1) by David Meerman Scott  
  I must confess I read it more than twice and hence it has a lot of coffee stains. What I loved about this book was its revelations on how to communicate and market in a digital world. I was tired of the old ways of marketing and selling and David Meerman Scott opened up my eyes to a new paradigm. It is about being authentic and  talking plainly. It is also social media 101\. This book preceded the launching of my blog but it is woven into its tapestry. It should be sitting in your Kindle book list or parked on your shelf after it has been consumed and underlined.

* [The Millionaire Messenger: Make a Difference and a Fortune Sharing Your Advice](https://www.amazon.com/Millionaire-Messenger-Difference-Fortune-Sharing/dp/1451665997/ref=sr_1_2?keywords=The+Millionaire+Messenger&qid=1575170652&s=books&sr=1-2) by Brendon Burchard  
  Brendon Burchard is like a “mini me” Tony Robbins. Don’t let that fool you. In this book he reveals how to monetise your knowledge ten different ways and have fun while doing so while adding value to people’s lives. He provides a glimpse into what he has learned about presenting, writing a book, creating promotional partners (affiliates), promoting seminars, educating online and much more. If you are an expert or thought leader and you don’t know how to package your ideas and knowledge and sell it, then read this book.

* [The War of Art](https://www.amazon.com/War-Art-Steven-Pressfield-ebook/dp/B007A4SDCG/ref=sr_1_1?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1534009731&sr=1-1&keywords=the+war+of+art+by+steven+pressfield) by Steve Pressfield  
  If you want to learn more about the art, the challenges and the processes of the creative sphere then this book is packed full of insights. If you are an artist writer, musician, business person or you are breathing and have a pulse….doesn’t everything involve being creative?…then read this book. It is about overcoming roadblocks and resistance in life. It is about “doing the work” that is congruent with your purpose and destiny.

* [Permission Marketing: Turning Strangers Into Friends And Friends Into Customers](https://www.amazon.com/Permission-Marketing-Turning-Strangers-Customers-ebook/dp/B000FC0SSC/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Permission+Marketing&qid=1575170736&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Seth Godin  
  Seth Godin is so visible in the marketing world that he is like a global beacon. I read this book while also reading The New Rules of Marketing and PR. This book flips the model of push marketing to attraction marketing. This book was also instrumental in starting my blogging journey. It is about people giving permission for you to sell to them. I thought that was a cool concept.

* [The ONE Thing: The Surprisingly Simple Truth Behind Extraordinary Results](https://www.amazon.com/ONE-Thing-Surprisingly-Extraordinary-Results/dp/1885167776/ref=sr_1_3?keywords=the+one+thing&qid=1575140668&sr=8-3) by Gary Keller, Jay Papasan

———————————————————

## **Procrastination**

* [Solving the Procrastination Puzzle: A Concise Guide to Strategies for Change](https://www.amazon.com/Solving-Procrastination-Puzzle-Concise-Strategies/dp/0399168125) by Timothy A. Pychyl

* [How to Stop Procrastinating: A Simple Guide to Mastering Difficult Tasks and Breaking the Procrastination Habit](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B0742KRKDG/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_bibl_vppi_i6) by S.J. Scott  (Author)

# Negotiation and Influence {#negotiation-and-influence}

## **Negotiation** {#negotiation}

* [Getting More: How You Can Negotiate to Succeed in Work and Life](https://www.amazon.com/Getting-More-Negotiate-Succeed-Work/dp/0307716902/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1495643715&sr=8-1&keywords=stuart+diamond) by Stuart Diamond 

* [Getting to Yes: Negotiating Agreement Without Giving In](https://www.amazon.com/Getting-Yes-Negotiating-Agreement-Without/dp/0143118757/ref=pd_bxgy_14_img_2?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=0143118757&pd_rd_r=VN5Y28XERAYM3DGRH8MY&pd_rd_w=pKlyX&pd_rd_wg=Qwhx8&psc=1&refRID=VN5Y28XERAYM3DGRH8MY) by Roger Fisher 

* [Never Split the Difference: Negotiating As If Your Life Depended On It](https://www.amazon.com/Never-Split-Difference-Negotiating-Depended-ebook/dp/B014DUR7L2)  by Chris Voss,‎ Tahl Raz

* [Women Don’t Ask: Negotiation and the Gender Divide](https://www.amazon.com/Women-Dont-Ask-Negotiation-Gender/dp/069108940X/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1517692299&sr=8-1&keywords=Women+Don%E2%80%99t+Ask%3A+Negotiation+and+the+Gender+Divide) by Linda Babcock and Sara Laschever

* [Beyond Reason: Using Emotions as You Negotiate](https://www.amazon.com/Beyond-Reason-Using-Emotions-Negotiate/dp/0143037781/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1519728413&sr=8-1&keywords=Beyond+Reason) by Roger Fisher,‎ Daniel Shapiro

———————————————————

## **Influence** {#influence}

* [Influencer: The New Science of Leading Change](https://www.amazon.com/Influencer-Science-Leading-Change-Second/dp/0071808868/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1529930511&sr=8-2&keywords=Influencer+Vital+Smarts) by Joseph Grenny, Kerry Patterson, David Maxfield, Ron McMillan, Al Switzler 

* [Elements of Influence: Getting Others to Follow Your Lead](https://www.amazon.com/Elements-Influence-Getting-Others-Follow/dp/0814438938/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1539278577&sr=8-1&keywords=elements+of+influence) by Terry Bacon

* [Influence](https://www.amazon.com/Influence-Psychology-Persuasion-Robert-Cialdini/dp/006124189X/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1531413664&sr=8-1&keywords=Influence%3A+The+Psychology+of+Persuasion+by+Robert+Cialdini): The Psychology of Persuasion by Robert Cialdini 

* [Influence without Authority](https://www.amazon.com/s/ref=nb_sb_noss_2?url=search-alias%3Daps&field-keywords=influence+without+authority) by Allan R. Cohen and David L. Bradford 

* [How to Win Friends and Influence People](https://www.amazon.com/How-Win-Friends-Influence-People/dp/0671027034/ref=sr_1_3?ie=UTF8&qid=1518103585&sr=8-3&keywords=How+to+Win+Friends+and+Influence+People) by Dale Carnegie    
  (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) Everyone wants to feel important. In Win Friends Carnegie shows you how to use that in your favor to make people like you and win people over. It’s a book about how to communicate and interact with people in a meaningful way. It all comes down to showing interest in the people you interact with and the work that they are doing. If you make that connection you will have won a friend.

* [Start with Why: How Great Leaders Inspire Everyone to Take Action](https://www.amazon.com/Start-Why-Leaders-Inspire-Everyone-ebook/dp/B002Q6XUE4/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1518103607&sr=8-1&keywords=Start+with+Why) by Simon Sinek

* [Influencing Others When You Have No Authority](http://www.clearintentions.net/influencing-others-when-you-have-no-authority/) by Clear Intentions International USA, on using the cohen-bradford influence model (web)

* [Becoming a Person of Influence](https://www.amazon.com/Becoming-Person-Influence-Positively-Impact-ebook/dp/B006IEFVJW/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1530304015&sr=8-1&keywords=becoming+a+person+of+influence) by John C. Maxwell 

* [Influence and Persuasion](https://www.amazon.com/Influence-Persuasion-HBR-Emotional-Intelligence/dp/1633693937/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533292530&sr=8-1&keywords=influence+and+persuasion+hbr), HBR and Nick Morgan  
  * Understand the Four Components of Influence by Nick Morgan  
  * Harnessing the Science of Persuasion by Robert Cialdini  
  * Three Things Managers Should Be Doing Every Day by Linda A. Hill and Kent Lineback  
  * Learning Charisma by John Antonakis, Marika Fenley, and Sue Liechti  
  * To Win People Over, Speak to Their Wants and Needs by Nancy Duarte  
  * Storytelling That Moves People, an interview with Robert McKee by Bronwyn Fryer  
  * The Surprising Persuasiveness of a Sticky Note by Kevin Hogan  
  * When to Sell with Facts and Figures, and When to Appeal to Emotions by Michael D. Harris.

## **Conflict** {#conflict}

* [Conflicted: How Productive Disagreements Lead to Better Outcomes](https://tinyurl.com/yz2nl7ot) by Ian Leslie 

* [The Anatomy of Peace: Resolving the Heart of Conflict](https://www.amazon.com/Anatomy-Peace-Resolving-Heart-Conflict/dp/1626564310/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1539131924&sr=8-1&keywords=the+anatomy+of+peace) by The Arbinger Institute

# Wisdom {#wisdom}

* The [Wisdom Page](http://www.wisdompage.com/) and [48 Characteristics of Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/WisdomCharacteristics.html) by Cop Macdonald

* [Goals, Values and Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/GoalsValuesandWisdom.html) by Walter G. Moss

* [Whatever Happened to Wisdom?](http://www.wisdompage.com/wppino.html) by Jerry Ortiz y Pino. Excerpts from one of his columns in the *Santa Fe Reporter*.

* [Robert Kennedy's Call for Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/RobertKennedySpeech.html). Robert F. Kennedy's speech in Indianapolis, April 4, 1968, on the death of Martin Luther King.

* [The Wisdom Imperative](http://www.wisdompage.com/wisdomimperative.html) by [Alan Nordstrom](http://alan-nordstrom.blogspot.com/)**.** What will save us from our vices, follies, and ineptitudes? Nordstrom discusses the *Wisdom Imperative*.

**Other websites**

* [The Wise Path](http://www.thewisepath.org/) website presents [Leland R. Beaumont](http://www.lelandbeaumont.com/)’s perspective on wisdom as the convergence of three developmental paths: emotional, cognitive, and action.

* [Definitions of Wisdom](http://wisdomcenteredlife.org/definitions.aspx) is a section of Richard Trowbridge's [Wisdom-Centered Life website](http://wisdomcenteredlife.org/) that presents many perspectives on the nature of wisdom.

**What is Wisdom?**

* [Future Consciousness: The Path to Purposeful Evolution \- An Introduction](http://www.wisdompage.com/2016%20Articles/Future%20Consciousness%20Article%20Complete%20FinalWFRCited.pdf) by Tom Lombardo. An overview, published in World Future Review, of a future-focused, evolutionary theory of wisdom. Advocating for a future "Age of Wisdom" as the central grand narrative for humanity, the article proposes that wisdom is the highest ideal to pursue in our personal and collective development, the most efficacious means toward human happiness and the good life, the critical goal to strive for within education, and the guiding light for our future evolution.

* [Eight Dimensions of Wise Design that could Change Everything \- A Video Talk by Kiko Suarez](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ITl8MC5RJN8&feature=youtu.be). The world is changing fast and we live in turbulent times, accelerated by the speed of technological change and rampant complexity.Bringing wisdom back to the center of our societal development by focusing on 8 wisdom-centered design principles, could result in a better redefinition of our human condition and structures of living.

* [Introduction to Psychology and Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/2013%20Articles/Introduction%20to%20Psychology%20&%20Wisdom%20Trowbridge.pdf) by Richard Hawley Trowbridge. An informative review of psychological research on wisdom, along with a thought-provoking discussion of contemporary and classical conceptions of wisdom.

* [Wisdom, Leisure, and Choices](http://www.wisdompage.com/2013%20Articles/Wisdom%20Leisure%20and%20Choices%20Moss.pdf) by Walter G. Moss. Another superb article by Walter Moss \- both well written and well researched. Although, given the title of the article, its focus might seem rather narrow, the article contains an excellent general discussion of practical wisdom, prioritizing values, and making wise choices.

* [A Virtue Theory Of Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/2012%20Articles/Virtue_Theory_of_Wisdom_Final_May2013.pdf) by Tom Lombardo. A future-focused comprehensive theory of wisdom based on thirteen key virtues with some thoughts on the development of wisdom through exercising and practicing the key virtues.

* [KNOWLEDGE REFORM.COM: Self-Improvement of Mind Towards Wisdom](http://www.knowledgereform.com/archives/) is a website rich in wisdom-relevant resources. Jason Cooper, the website's creator, presents the visitor with an eclectic mix of essays, book reviews, and videos that present ancient and contemporary views of the subject.

* [The Rosewood Report on Practical Wisdom](http://www.mcps.umn.edu/documents/RosewoodReport.pdf). This is the complete six-part report summarizing discussions in July, 2010 by a small group of philosophers and psychologists about practical wisdom. (A PDF file.)

* [The Prajña Sutra: Aphorisms of Intuition](http://www.wisdompage.com/prajnasutra.pdf). The Sanskrit word prajña means *wisdom* in English. Here, [Subhash Kak](http://www.cs.okstate.edu/~subhashk/) presents his take on Vedic wisdom. (A PDF file.)

* [What Wisdom Requires](http://alan-nordstrom.blogspot.com/2011/03/what-wisdom-requires-there-is-no-more.html). [Alan Nordstrom](http://alan-nordstrom.blogspot.com/) calls on us to "to become more conscious, careful and committed to changing our minds and behaviors as wisdom requires" and shares his thoughts on just what those requirements are.

* [How Do We Define Wisdom?](http://wisdomresearch.org/forums/t/846.aspx#). This is Part 1 of The Rosewood Report concerning discussions in July, 2010 by a small group of philosophers and psychologists about the capacities of practical wisdom.

* [Is Wisdom Just One Thing?](http://wisdomresearch.org/forums/t/851.aspx#). This is Part 2 of The Rosewood Report concerning discussions in July, 2010 by a small group of philosophers and psychologists about the capacities of practical wisdom.

* [Wisdom Facing Forward](http://www.wisdompage.com/WisdomFacingForwardWFSAug2010.pdf). In this powerful and illuminating article in the [World Futurist Society](http://www.wfs.org/)'s journal *The Futurist*, psychologist Tom Lombardo presents a comprehensive picture of what wisdom is, and he explores the ways in which wisdom and awareness of the future connect. (PDF format)

* [Monika Ardelt's Model of Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/Ardelt01.html). Wisdom researcher [Monika Ardelt](http://www.wisdompage.com/WisdomResearchers/MonikaArdelt.html) considers wisdom to be a combination of cognitive, reflective, and affective personality qualities that "cannot exist independently of individuals."

* [The Wise Path](http://www.thewisepath.org/) website presents [Leland R. Beaumont](http://www.lelandbeaumont.com/)'s perspective on wisdom as the convergence of three developmental paths: emotional, cognitive, and action.

* [Where's Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/WheresWisdom.pdf) is an insightful essay by [Leland R. Beaumont](http://www.lelandbeaumont.com/) that, with the aid of helpful graphics, explores both the personal growth process as one heads toward wisdom and the final destination: wisdom itself. (A PDF file)

* [The Philosophical Approach Towards Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/ThePhilosophicalApproach.doc). Here, [Andrew Targowski](http://www.wisdompage.com/TargowskiBio.html), Professor of Business Information Systems at Western Michigan University, looks at both the history of wisdom and its place in our contemporary world. (A .doc file.)

* [Selected WISDOM PAGE Resources for Independent Study](http://www.wisdompage.com/LearnerIntro.html) A carefully selected group of text, audio, and video resources arranged in four tiers representing four different levels of interest, prior knowledge about wisdom, and personal involvement.

* [WISDOM and THE WISDOM PAGE](http://www.wisdompage.com/Video2/WisdomPageIntroVideo.html) is a 9-minute video that introduces the three big questions concerning wisdom: What is wisdom? Why is wisdom important? and How can we develop wisdom? It touches on answers to all three, and invites the viewer to visit The Wisdom Page website and explore the matter more deeply. (Also available on [YouTube](http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RsoICa0mjjA).)

* [How To Achieve Heaven on Earth with Martin Rutte](http://www.omniartsalon.com/oas-251-how-to-achieve-heaven-on-earth-with-martin-rutte/) is a fascinating and informative 44-minute streaming audio conversation between Martin Rutte and Jeffrey Milburn about the heaven-on-earth concept and the [*How to Achieve a Heaven on Earth*](http://www.wisdompage.com/HOE/HeavenOnEarth01.html) book.

* [SOPPHIA — The 7 Dimensions of Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/SOPPHIAessay2.html) Bernard Brookes's "SOPPHIA model organizes the plethora of competencies into 7 Dimensions of Wisdom, and provides a framework that facilitates coaching and self-development efforts."

* [Islamic Wisdom](http://www.islamicwisdom.net/) is a website that presents an Islamic perspective on wisdom. "Our aim is to present the fundamentals of Islamic ideology from the perspectives of philosophy, reason and wisdom."

* [About Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/Rana01.html) is [Rana Ehtisham Rabbani](http://www.humanityworld.com/author.html)'s succinct answer to the "What is wisdom?" question. He elaborates his view at his website, [www.humanityworld.com](http://www.humanityworld.com/).

* [Some links to Traditional Wisdom Literature](http://www.wisdompage.com/introwis05.html) Cultures around the world have valued wisdom, and through their literatures have tried to help people develop it.

* [Some Contemporary Online Wisdom Books and Reviews](http://www.wisdompage.com/introwis06.html) Today's authors present their views on wisdom and wise living. (See also our main [Books and Reviews](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/) section.)

* [Obama, Passion and Wisdom](http://hnn.us/articles/116297.html) is [Walter Moss](http://people.emich.edu/wmoss/)'s preferred title for this essay that explores what wisdom is in the context of politics.

* [Wisdom, Golf, and Obama (Word format)](http://www.wisdompage.com/WisdomGolfandObama.doc) (or [PDF](http://www.wisdompage.com/WisdomGolfandObama.pdf))   Golf and wisdom miles apart? In this short, fun essay [Walter Moss](http://people.emich.edu/wmoss/) makes the connection.

* [Overview of Prior Research on Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/Mick--OverviewofPriorResearch.html) is a brief but informative excerpt from an [article](http://www.wisdompage.com/Mick--WisdomasaCentralLink.pdf) by University of Virginia professor [David Mick](http://www.commerce.virginia.edu/dgm9t).

* [Barry Schwartz Video on Practical Wisdom](http://www.ted.com/talks/barry_schwartz_on_our_loss_of_wisdom.html) This inspiring 20-minute MP4 talk by [Barry Schwartz](http://www.swarthmore.edu/SocSci/bschwar1/) was presented at the 2009 TED (Technology, Entertainment, Design) conference in Long Beach, California.

* [WISDOM: The Highest Aim of Life and Higher Education](http://www.wisdompage.com/rollinstalk.html)   A text (with slides) rendering of Copthorne Macdonald's “Thomas P. Johnson Distinguished Visiting Scholar” address at Rollins College April 5, 2006\.

* [A Video of the Above Address in Flash format](http://www.wisdompage.com/Video/RollinsTalkVideoFLV.html)  

* [Wisdom and Wilderness](http://www.wisdompage.com/meekart.html) by [Joseph W. Meeker](http://www.wisdompage.com/meekbio.html). An excellent article by Dr. Meeker on wisdom and its relationship to wilderness.

* [The "Understanding Wisdom" issue of *Vimukt Shiksha*](http://www.swaraj.org/shikshantar/vimukt_02.html), a publication of India-based [Shikshantar](http://www.swaraj.org/shikshantar/), an organization dedicated to transforming existing models of education and development.

* [Wisdom: A First Approximation](http://www.wisdompage.com/dc-essa.html) by [Don Cochrane](http://www.wisdompage.com/dc-bio.html). University of Saskatchewan professor Don Cochrane's views on the subject.

* [What is Wisdom?](http://www.wisdompage.com/nordstromessay01.html) by [Alan Nordstrom](http://alan-nordstrom.blogspot.com/). In this short but moving essay, Professor Nordstrom tells us that Wisdom is our Way Out from Folly.

* [Playing the Wisdom Game](http://www.wisdompage.com/wisdomgame-illus.html) by [Copthorne Macdonald](http://www.copmacdonald.com/). An essay that appears in the 2006 book [Living a Life of Value](http://www.valuesofthewise.com/Public/Books-Programs/LivingaLifeofValue/index.cfm), here with added illustrations.

* [Introduction](http://www.wisdompage.com/glintro.html) to *Getting a Life* by [Copthorne Macdonald](http://www.copmacdonald.com/). Comments on the nature of Practical Wisdom, as Aristotle called it.

* [Chapter 1](http://www.wisdompage.com/tw-ch01.html) of *Toward Wisdom* by [Copthorne Macdonald](http://www.copmacdonald.com/). More about the nature of wisdom; here primarily Aristotle's other variety of wisdom: Existential/Metaphysical Wisdom.

* [Sophology: The Study of Wisdom](http://www.sophology.org/wisdom2.htm), an essay on the nature and development of wisdom by Glenn Shipley, is part of his [sophology.org](http://www.sophology.org/) website.

* [The Dance of Polarization](http://www.wisdompage.com/abs-essa.html) by [Andrew Bard Schmookler](http://www.wisdompage.com/abs-bio.html). In this essay Schmookler deals with the polarization-integrating aspect of wisdom.

* [What is Wisdom?](http://www.toothycat.net/wiki/wiki.pl?Wisdom) asks [Douglas Reay](http://www.chiark.greenend.org.uk/~douglasr/).  He presents his own and other's thoughts on the subject.

   
**Review of Books on Wisdom from Cop Macdonald** 

* [An Age of Progress?: Clashing Twentieth-Century Global Forces](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/MossReview.html) by Walter G. Moss \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [Beyond Intellect: Journey Into the Wisdom of Your Intuitive Mind](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/VelasquezReview.html) by Susan McNeal Velasquez \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [Creating Change Through Humanism by Roy Speckhardt](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2015%20Reviews/Good%20Without%20God%20Beaumont%20Review.pdf) \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont. Good Without God: This handbook for prospective humanists is an important resource for thoughtful people who are seeking real good. The book tells us what humanism is, why it makes sense, how it addresses real problems, and what we can do to create positive change. 

* [Consciousness: Confessions of a Romantic Reductionist](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Consciousness_Koch_Book_Review_Final%20copy.pdf) by Christof Koch \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo. A valuable, up to date examination of the scientific and philosophical dimensions of understanding consciousness, free will, and the brain. Also, a revealing portrait of how the writer's scientific ideas and research have influenced his life. 

* [Cutting God in Half \- And Putting the Pieces Together Again: A New Approach to Philosophy](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/ReviewofCuttingGodinHalf.html) by Nicolas Maxwell \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [Educating for Wisdom and Compassion: Creating Conditions for Timeless Learning](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/millerbook.html) by John P. Miller \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [The End of Growth: Adapting to Our New Economic Reality](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/The%20End%20of%20Growth.pdf) by Richard Heinberg \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont

* [Ethics and the Golden Rule](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Pure_Gold_Book_Review_May_2013.pdf) by Harry Gensler \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont. An excellent, informative review concerning one of the most universal ethical principles across human cultures. 

* [Ethics and the Quest for Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2016%20Reviews/Ethics%20and%20Wisdom%20Review%20Moss.pdf) by Robert Kane \- Reviewed by Walter G. Moss. Kane's book conveys valuable insights regarding how to live wisely in our modern age. This age he correctly maintains is characterized by uncertainty and pluralism. Does that mean, however, that we are stuck in a relativist universe where we must accept that one view is as good as another? Kane thinks not. He believes that we can still arrive at central, objective truths, both in our private lives and in the public sphere.

* [The Evolution of Future Consiousness and Contemporary Futurist Thought](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/lombardobooks.html) by Tom Lombardo \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [The Evolution of Well-Being and the Good \- Part I: A Review of “In Search of Coherence: Sketching a Theory of Sustainable Well-Being”](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2015%20Reviews/Well%20Being%20Essay%20Wisdom%20and%20the%20Future%20August%202015.pdf) by Timo Hämäläinen \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo. Hämäläinen’s article is an informative and thought provoking review of the numerous global efforts to articulate and measure human well-being and implement social policies to enhance it in the world; it is an excellent review of theories and the pragmatics of well-being. With critical commentary, this review is the first of two parts on contemporary ideas on well-being, the good life, and those psychological and ethical capacities for realizing psychological and social well-being. 

* [The Evolution of Well-Being and the Good: Part II: A Review of “Happiness Donut: A Confucian Critique of Positive Psychology” by Louise Sundararajan](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2016%20Reviews/Donut%20Review%20Final%20Web%20Copy.pdf)\- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo. Louise Sundararajan argues that Martin Seligman’s vision of positive psychology not only has a Western bias regarding what constitutes psychological well-being, but it is inconsistent in its stated understanding of the relationship between facts uncovered in positive psychological research and ethical thinking. A general discussion of the relationship between the psychology of well being and theories of the good life is included in the review. 

* [Evolutionaries: Unlocking the Spiritual and Cultural Potential of Science's Greatest Idea](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/Evolutionaries.html) by Carter Phipps \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo 

* [Flourish: A Visionary New Understanding of Happiness and Well-being](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Flourish%20.pdf) by Martin Seligman \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont

* [From Knowledge to Wisdom,](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/MaxwellReview.pdf) 2nd Edition by Nicholas Maxwell \- Reviewed by Jeff Huggins

* [The Future We Want: Radical Ideas for the New Century by Sarah Leonard and Bhaskar Sunkara (Ed.)](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2016%20Reviews/Beaumont%20Review%20Socialism%202.0.pdf) \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont. Born out of massive political discontent and the Occupy movement, the collection of ten essays in this timely book each characterizes an important social problem before suggesting a solution. In each case the suggested solution is a bold shift toward socialism.

* [A God that Could be Real: Spirituality, Science, and the Future of Our Planet](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2015%20Reviews/Beaumont%20Book%20Review%20April%202015.pdf)by Nancy Abrams \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont

* [Happiness: A Guide to Developing Life's Most Important Skill](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/HappinessSkill.html) by Matthieu Ricard \- Review by Leland R. Beaumont

* [The Happiness Project: Or, Why I Spent a Year Trying to Sing in the Morning, Clean My Closets, Fight Right, Read Aristotle, and Generally Have More Fun](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/Happinessproject.html) by Gretchen Rubin \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo

* [Healing Spaces: The Science of Place and Well-Being](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Healing%20Spaces%20Review.pdf) by Esther M. Sternberg, M.D. Reviewed by Leland Beaumont. Spaces affect healing and well-being. Medical Doctor Esther Sternberg examines the intersection of architecture and neuroscience—how spaces influence our minds and bodies—in this well-written and informative book.

* [How Enlightenment Changes Your Brain: The New Science of Transformation](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2016%20Reviews/Enlightenment%20Review%20Beaumont.pdf) by Andrew Newberg and Mark Robert Waldman \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont. “The authors describe the phenomenon of enlightenment in a wide variety of forms, endeavor to examine the science of enlightenment, and then describe how you can attain enlightenment...the authors argue that ‘The ability to experience enlightenment, big or small, appears to be ‘wired’ into our brain and consciousness.’ “

* [Imagine: How Creativity Works](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/imagine.html) by Jonah Lehrer \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo

* [The Infinite Resource: The Power of Ideas on a Finite Planet](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Commons_Knowledge_Review_May_2013.pdf) by Ramez Naam \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont. If wisdom involves getting the big picture of things, then this book is wise, pulling together environmental, technological, demographic, and economic dimensions of our contemporary global reality. Further, again in resonance with the various capacities of wisdom, the book offers innovative and integrative solutions for our global challenges. Never underestimate the power of the mind. 

* [In Our Image: Humanity's Quest for Divinity via Technology](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/ChowdhuryReview.html) by Debashis Chowdhury \- Reviewed by Copothorne Macdonald

* [Leading with Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/LeadingwithWisdomReview.pdf) \- This book, reviewed here by Walter G. Moss, brings together the perspectives of eight authors on how leaders lead "and how wisdom (connected to spirituality) can result in a more integrated and peaceful practice of leadership."

* [Leaving Truth](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/LeavingTruth.html) by Keith Sewell \- Reviewed by Leland R. Beaumont

* [Making Waves and Riding the Currents: Activism and the Practice of Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/HalpernReview.html) by Charles Halpern \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [The Man Who Planted Trees: Lost Groves, Champion Trees, and an Urgent Plan to Save the Planet](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/The%20Man%20Who%20Planted%20Trees.pdf) by Jim Robbins \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont

* [Matters of Consequence](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/matters_consequnence.html) by Copthorne Macdonald \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo

* [Meaning: The Secret of Being Alive](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/havener1.html) by Cliff Havener \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [Mind and Cosmos: Why the Materialist Neo-Darwinian Conception of Nature is Almost Certainly False](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Nagel%20Book%20Review%20March%202013.pdf) by Thomas Nagel \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo \- A thoughtful and thought-provoking short philosophy book on the challenge of explaining consciousness, rationality, and values within scientific theories of the evolution of the physical world.

* [The Monk and the Philosopher: A Father and Son Discuss the Meaning of Life](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/The%20Monk%20and%20the%20Philosopher.pdf) by Jean-Francois Revel and Matthieu Ricard \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont

* [The Moral Landscape](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Moral%20Landscape%20and%20Flourish.pdf) by Sam Harris and [Flourish](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Moral%20Landscape%20and%20Flourish.pdf) by Martin Seligman: A Comparative Review Reviewed by Tom Lombardo

* [Moral Tribes: Emotion, Reason, and the Gap Between Us and Them by Joshua Greene](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2016%20Reviews/Beaumont%20Review%20Moral%20Tribes.pdf) \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont. This is the best book I have read in many years. It provides a new level of clarity on ethical reasoning and essential issues I have been curious about for a very long time.

* [The Open-Focus Brain: Harnessing the Power of Attention to Heal Mind and Body](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/FehmiBook.html) by Les Fehmi and Jim Robbins \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [The Power of Collective Wisdom and the Trap of Collective Folly](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/The%20power%20of%20collective%20wisdom%20.pdf) by Alan Briskin, Sheryl Erickson, John Ott, and Tom Callanan \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont

* [The Power of Habit: Why We Do What We Do in Life and Business](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/Powerofhabit.html) by Charles Duhigg \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo

* [The Power of Meaning: Crafting a Life That Matters](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2017%20Reviews/Beaumont's%20Book%20Review%20Pillars%20of%20Meaning.pdf) by Emily Esfahani Smith \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont. As more people realize that religious dogma is not the path to meaningful lives we may be cast adrift, or we may seek effective paths toward meaning. Author Emily Esfahani Smith provides useful insights as we seek our own meaningful path through life. 

* [The Power to Transform: Leadership That Brings Learning and Schooling to Life](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/marshallbook.html) by Stephanie Pace Marshall \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [Practical Wisdom](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/MossReviewOfPracticalWisdom.html) by Barry Schwarz and Kenneth Sharpe \- Reviewed by Walter G. Moss Practical wisdom is the variety of wisdom that helps us deal with everyday life. (See also [the Barry Schwarz video](http://www.ted.com/talks/barry_schwartz_on_our_loss_of_wisdom.html) on practical wisdom.) 

* [Preparing for a World that Doesn’t Exist \- Yet](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2016%20Reviews/Smyre%20Book%20Review%20Final%20.pdf) by Rick Smyre and Neil Richardson \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo. For advocates of change and, in particular, wisdom writers who wish to see the future of humanity more centrally guided and informed by wisdom, this book is an important and valuable contribution and resource. For wisdom writers there is often a disconnect between the presentation of elevating ideas and their actual social impact and effective implementation. Smyre and Richardson's book is a guidance system for moving from idea to action and actual social change.

* [Preparing for a World that Doesn’t Exist \- Yet](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2016%20Reviews/Smyre%20Book%20Excerpt%20Final.pdf) (Book Excerpt) by Rick Smyre and Neil Richardson. The Forward and Prologue to the book. 

* [Prosperity Without Growth: Economics for a Finite Planet](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Prosperity%20Without%20Growth.pdf) by Tim Jackson \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont

* [Redirect: The Surprising New Science of Psychological Change](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/redirect.html) by Timothy Wilson \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo

* [Sacred Economics: Money, Gift, and Society in the Age of Transition](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2014%20Reviews/Prosperity%20Lost.pdf) by Charles Eisenstein \- Reviewed by Lee Beaumont. This book is full of good ideas for transforming the obsolete elements of our economic systems into a truly modern economy. Author Charles Eisenstein begins this bold and well written book examining why innovation, labor saving devices, and all of the earth's bounty fail to deliver prosperity to most of the people.

* [Spirit Matters: Global Healing and the Wisdom of the Soul](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/LernerReview.html) by Michael Lerner \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [Superforecasting: The Art and Science of Prediction](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2015%20Reviews/Scoring%20Forecast%20Accuracy.pdf) by Philip Tetlock and Dan Gardner \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont. Summarizing 20 years of research on forecasting accuracy conducted from 1984 through 2004, Philip Tetlock concluded “the average expert was roughly as accurate as a dart-throwing chimpanzee.” This book describes what was learned as Tetlock set out to improve forecasting accuracy with the Good Judgement Project.

* [A Theory of Everything: An Integral Vision for Business, Politics, Science, and Spirituality](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/toerevw.html) by Ken Wilber \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [The Three Levels of Leadership: How to Develop Your Leadership Presence, Knowhow, and Skill](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Handbook_for_Wise_Leadership.pdf) by James Scouller \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont. A well-researched, deeply thought-out and clearly presented handbook for wise leadership. This book presents a robust model of leadership for the good, based on the concept of leadership presence, with self-mastery at its core. 

* [Wellbeing: The Five Essential Elements](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Wellbeing_Review_Lee_Beaumont.pdf) by Tom Rath and Jim Harter \- Reviewed by Lee Beaumont

* [Why Does the World Exist?](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Why_Does_World_Exist_Book_Review_Final_.pdf) by Jim Holt \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo. A clear, informative, and philosophically engaging review and discussion of the ultimate ontological question: "Why is there something rather than nothing?" 

* [The Willpower Instinct: How Self-Control Works, Why it Matters, and What You Can Do to Get More of It.](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/The%20Willpower%20Instinct%20.pdf) by Kelly McGonigal \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont

* [Willpower: Rediscovering the Greatest Human Strength](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/willpower.html) by Roy Baumeister and John Tierney \- Reviewed by Tom Lombardo

* [Wisdom, Consciousness, and the Future](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/WisConFuture.html) by Tom Lombardo \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [Wisdom, Intuition, and Ethics](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012_HTML_Reviews/curnow.html) by Trevor Curnow \- Reviewed by Copthorne Macdonald

* [Wiser: Getting Beyond Groupthink to Make Groups Smarter](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Wiser%20Groups.pdf) by Cass R. Sunstein and Reid Hastie \- Reviewed by Lee Beaumont 

* [The Wisest One in the Room: How You Can Benefit from Social Psychology's Most Powerful Insights](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2016%20Reviews/Beaumont%20Review%20Seeing%20Beyond%20Illusion.pdf) by Thomas Gilovich and Lee Ross \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont. Of the many definitions proposed for wisdom, perhaps the most intriguing is “seeing beyond illusion.” When most people are captivated by illusions, the wisest one in the room sees past them and proposes new solutions. The authors draw on recent research in social psychology, judgement, and decision making to help us become wiser.

* [Whole Earth Discipline: Why Dense Cities, Nuclear Power, Transgenic Crops, Restored Wildlands, and Geoengineering Are Necessary](http://www.wisdompage.com/reviews/2012%20Reviews/Whole%20Earth%20Discipline.pdf) by Stewart Brand \- Reviewed by Leland Beaumont

# Learning {#learning}

## **Best** {#best}

* [The Science of Accelerated Learning: Advanced Strategies for Quicker Comprehension, Greater Retention, and Systematic Expertise](https://www.amazon.com/Science-Accelerated-Learning-Strategies-Comprehension-ebook/dp/B07856MDT3/ref=pd_cp_351_3?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_p=fcaa6d12-8b2b-4ad7-b277-864b2da79f6e&pf_rd_r=BPPX2F346SX1SKB01WRZ&pd_rd_wg=8zp8L&pf_rd_s=desktop-dp-sims&pf_rd_t=40701&pd_rd_w=XhsUX&pf_rd_i=desktop-dp-sims&pd_rd_r=8732f9ac-9c0e-11e8-af6e-0720243a5fcc&pd_rd_i=B07856MDT3&psc=1&refRID=BPPX2F346SX1SKB01WRZ) by Peter Hollins

* [Deliberate Practice](http://www.davidsongifted.org/db/Articles_id_10448.aspx) by Dr K. Anders Ericsson

* [Make It Stick](https://www.amazon.com/Make-Stick-Peter-C-Brown-ebook/dp/B00JQ3FN7M/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1534038790&sr=1-1&keywords=Make+It+Stick) by Peter Brown, Henry Roediger and Mark McDaniel

* [Teaching Smart People How to Learn](https://hbr.org/1991/05/teaching-smart-people-how-to-learn) by Chris Argyris (from Nancy Brodsky)

* [Mindset: How You Can Fulfill Your Potential](https://www.amazon.com/Mindset-Psychology-Carol-S-Dweck/dp/0345472322/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533945675&sr=8-1&keywords=mindset+carol+s.+dweck&smid=ATVPDKIKX0DER) by Carol Dweck   
  related article: [Do You Have the Right Mindset for Success?](https://www.fastcompany.com/660047/do-you-have-right-mindset-success)  
  Growth mindset. Again, I am fascinated by the field of mastery.  Not self-improvement (eat well, sleep well, etc) but on how can you continue a path of improvement so that you can really enjoy the subtleties at a very deep level of whatever it is you love.  Carol Dweck, through massive research and storytelling, shows the reader how to continue on the path of improvement and why so many people fall off that path. 

* [Kolb Learning Model](https://drive.google.com/open?id=1Q8T9ohTSap2AoNo8l-zJFoT-QXwFQP53)

# Communication {#communication}

## **Candor and Sensitive Conversations** {#candor-and-sensitive-conversations}

* [Radical Candor](https://www.amazon.com/Radical-Candor-KIM-SCOTT/dp/1509845364/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1519116068&sr=8-1&keywords=radical+candor) by Kim Scott. Care personally, challenge directly.

Levitt and Stephen J. Dubner  [short version](http://www.businessinsider.com/freakonomics-levitt-dubner-2011-8?op=1)   
  As the Wall Street Journal proclaims, “If Indiana Jones were an economist, he’d be Steven Levitt.” Freakonomics is a groundbreaking collaboration between Levitt and Stephen J. Dubner, an award-winning author and journalist. The two examined the inner workings of a crack gang, the truth about real estate agents and the secrets of the Ku Klux Klan. The result of their work is this book, which powerfully shows how, at its core, economics is the study of incentives. It is how people get what they want or need, especially when other people are trying to get the same thing.

* [The Paradox of Choice: Why More Is Less](https://www.amazon.com/Paradox-Choice-More-Less-Revised-ebook/dp/B000TDGGVU/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1542826026&sr=8-1&keywords=paradox+of+choice+by+barry+schwartz) by Barry Schwartz
