## **Thinking Differently** {#thinking-differently}

Curated in Change the Way You Think by Born Realist, bornrealist.com and Caitlin Schiller, thenextweb.com

* [Fooled by Randomness: The Hidden Role of Chance](https://www.amazon.com/Fooled-Randomness-Hidden-Markets-Incerto/dp/0812975219/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Fooled+by+Randomness%3A+The+Hidden+Role+of+Chance&qid=1575171067&s=books&sr=1-1) by Nassim Nicholas Taleb  
  This book will show you perfectly why life is not reasonable and how it passes in a very non-linear way. This book is about the part of fortunes in our lives and how we perceive it. The writer contends that we severely underestimate the realm of possibilities when we make decisions, and thereby expose ourselves to risks. Most fascinating is the blend of disciplines in this book. Read this book, it might change your thinking and reasoning.  
  We gravely underestimate the impact of luck and random events on our lives, using terms like “skills,” and “determinism,” when “luck” and “randomness” are the elements actually at play. In this book, Nassim Nicholas Taleb cites real-world examples to whip the veil of certainty from our eyes and explains that life is mostly governed by chance. Read this one for an enlightened view on why life is non-linear and not always fair.

* [A Whole New Mind: Why Right-Brainers Will Rule the Future](https://www.amazon.com/Whole-New-Mind-Right-Brainers-Future-ebook/dp/B000PC0SPU/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=A+whole+new+mind%3A+Why+right+brainers+will+rule+the+world&qid=1575171080&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Daniel Pink  
  Being innovative, creative and imaginative are traits that helps us in succeeding while likewise also increasing our personal well-being. Pink recognizes the 6 fundamental human abilities that he sees as essential for both professional achievement and personal satisfaction.

* [Weird Ideas That Work: 11 1/2 Practices for Promoting, Managing, and Sustaining Innovation](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B000FC0WLK/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_hsch_vapi_tkin_p1_i7) by Robert I. Sutton  
  Stanford professor Robert I. Sutton offers understanding on the nature of innovation and experimentation, failures and creative freedom. It will explode all your creativity and will offer approaches to return more advancement to your business through building systems that will help you in managing both disappointment and achievement. Routine work and innovative work are both important to a company’s success. But truly recognizing the differences between the two and understanding where each is most useful? That is invaluable. Stanford professor Robert I. Sutton offers insight on the nature of innovation and experimentation, failure, and creative freedom. It’ll blow up everything you thought you knew about creativity and offers ways to put more innovation back into your business via expectation setting, hiring choices, and strategies for dealing with both failure and success.

* [Drive: The Surprising Truth About What Motivates Us](https://www.amazon.com/Drive-Surprising-Motivates-Takeaways-Analysis/dp/B01AIK0ESE/ref=sr_1_2?keywords=Drive%3A+The+surprising+truth+about+what+motivates+us&qid=1575171186&s=digital-text&sr=1-2) by Daniel Pink  
  The book teaches you about motivation and inspiration. How you can build awareness with your inspiration so as to enhance your efficiency and how you can transform your way of living. This book carries surprising methods for placing these surprising techniques that will change your perspective about life. The ability to motivate is central to leadership. That’s what makes Pink’s book so valuable. Packed with the secrets of motivation, Pink suggests we move away from rewards and punishment, opting for meaningful work, mastery, and autonomy instead.  
  Let’s talk for a second about extrinsic motivation: based primarily on rewards and sanctions that come from outside the self, extrinsic motivation is useful on a short term basis. In the long run, though, it’s passion and dedication that characterizes intrinsic motivation and truly fuels the search for meaning and success. Drive teaches you about extrinsic and intrinsic motivation, what influences each sort, and how you can build awareness of intrinsic motivation to improve your productivity and inspire others in kind:  
  * Autonomy — Our desire to be self directed. It increases engagement over compliance.  
  * Mastery — The urge to get better skills.  
  * Purpose — The desire to do something that has meaning and is important. Businesses that only focus on profits without valuing purpose will end up with poor customer service and unhappy employees

* [Nudge: Improving Decisions About Health, Wealth, and Happiness](https://www.amazon.com/Nudge-Improving-Decisions-Health-Happiness-ebook/dp/B00A5DCALY/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Nudge%3A+Improving+decisions+about+health%2C+wealth+and+happiness&qid=1575171208&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Richard H. Thaler and Cass R. Sunstein  
  Everyday we make decisions on topics ranging from personal investments to schools for our children to the meals we eat. Unfortunately, we often choose poorly. Being human, we as a whole are helpless to different inclinations that can lead us to blunder. In the book author shows how nudges or subtle changes in context make it more difficult to make a poor decision. But it can help us achieve our goals or accomplish our objectives.   
  Look at acid washed jeans, the atom bomb, and Miley Cyrus and it becomes woefully apparent: we as humans make the wrong decisions all the time. We don’t always do what’s best for us. Why? Sometimes we have too little or overly complex information, or we act on gut feelings rather than reasoned plans. Sometimes we succumb to temptation, and sometimes we’re manipulated by external forces. Thaler, leading behavioral economist and advisor to Barack Obama, shows how nudges, or subtle changes in context that make it more difficult to make a poor decision, can help us achieve our goals.

* [Mindset: How You Can Fulfill Your Potential](https://www.amazon.com/Mindset-Psychology-Carol-S-Dweck/dp/0345472322/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533945675&sr=8-1&keywords=mindset+carol+s.+dweck&smid=ATVPDKIKX0DER)  
  As little children we adopt a mindset, fixed or growth. Shockingly enough, this one selection defines how we’ll feel, what we believe ourselves capable of achieving, and what we’ll risk for the rest of our lives. Dweck, professor of psychology at Stanford, teaches us about how to identify our mindset, confront our own attitudes and ideas, and develop a growth mindset to realize our potential to the fullest. Read it to have your ideas about who you are and your own potential changed forever.  
  It is not just our abilities and talent that bring us success. However we approach them with a settled or development attitude. The author teaches us about how to distinguish our mindset, confront our own attitudes and ideas and develop a growth mindset to realize our potential to the fullest. Read it to have your thoughts regarding your identity and your own potential changed until the end of time. Related article: [Do You Have the Right Mindset for Success?](https://www.fastcompany.com/660047/do-you-have-right-mindset-success)

* [Thinking, Fast And Slow](https://www.amazon.com/Thinking-Fast-Slow-Daniel-Kahneman-ebook/dp/B00555X8OA/ref=sr_1_2?keywords=Thinking%2C+Fast+And+Slow&qid=1575171249&s=digital-text&sr=1-2) by Daniel Kahneman   
  This book will shake your head in denial, disbelief, and surprise. Your mind will feel like it is going to explode from all the fascinating revelations you discover and you will gain a deeper understanding about how you make decisions and react to certain things in your life.

* [The Power of Now: A Guide to Spiritual Enlightenment](https://www.amazon.com/Power-Now-Guide-Spiritual-Enlightenment-ebook/dp/B002361MLA/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Power+of+Now%3A+A+Guide+to+Spiritual+Enlightenment&qid=1575171269&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Eckhart Tolle  
  The core message of the book is simple and powerful.The best approach to genuine satisfaction is through figuring out how to live in the now, at this time we are encountering, without remembering the past or hustling to what’s to come. The creator encourages us to see how our considerations and feelings act as a burden and what to do about it.

* [Think Like a Freak: The Authors of Freakonomics Offer to Retrain Your Brain](https://www.amazon.com/Think-Like-Freak-Authors-Freakonomics-ebook/dp/B00BATINVS/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Think+like+a+freak&qid=1575171286&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by S. Levitt and Stephen Dubner  
  It is easier to fall in line with what your family and friends think than to find new family and friends\! Yet, running with the crowd implies we rush to grasp existing conditions, ease back to alter our opinions, and glad to appoint our reasoning. This book will change your reasoning style and will make you to think beyond.

* [Flourish: A Visionary New Understanding of Happiness and Well-being](https://www.amazon.com/Flourish-Visionary-Understanding-Happiness-Well-being-ebook/dp/B0043RSK9O/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Flourish%3A+A+Visionary+New+Understanding+of+Happiness+and+Well+being&qid=1575171330&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Martin Seligman  
  This book outlines four core components of well-being: positive emotion, engagement with what one is doing, a sense of accomplishment, and good relationships. It is one of the wealthiest assets on your voyage to carrying on with an existence that makes you more joyful.

* [The Wisdom of Crowds](https://www.amazon.com/Wisdom-Crowds-James-Surowiecki/dp/0385721706/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1527942012&sr=1-1&keywords=The+Wisdom+of+Crowds) by James Surowiecki   
  Sure, groupthink can be dangerous, but under the right circumstances crowds can make surprisingly intelligent decisions and even produce better results than the experts or the smartest individuals in those groups. If the group is full of independent thinkers who have no problem pooling intelligence for the common good, you’ve reached the apogee of collective brilliance.  
  In this book, James Surowiecki summons examples from popular culture, psychology, and biology, and more to illustrate this idea’s implications on how we vote, decide, do business, and move through the world.

* [Made to Stick: Why Some Ideas Survive and Others Die](https://www.amazon.com/Made-Stick-Ideas-Survive-Others/dp/1400064287/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=made+to+stick&qid=1575170488&s=books&sr=1-1) by Chip Heath and Dan Heath  
  Successful stories, advertising campaigns, and ideas with staying power share the same recognizable characteristics: they’re simple, unexpected, concrete, credible, and emotional — and they tell a unified story.  
  In this book, Chip & Dan Heath explore why some ideas stick and others don’t, and how you can make yours more velcro than slip ‘n slide.

* [A Whole New Mind: Why Right Brainers Will Rule the Future](https://www.amazon.com/Whole-New-Mind-Right-Brainers-Future-ebook/dp/B000PC0SPU/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1546458789&sr=8-1&keywords=a+whole+new+mind%3A+why+rightbrainers+will+rule+the+future)   
  Right brain aptitudes have been historically undervalued and dismissed, but as we move from the Information Age into the Conceptual Age, they’re becoming the future’s superpowers. What business is increasingly discovering is that while analytical, left-brain thinking is still important, it isn’t insufficient on its own. Being innovative, creative and empathetic are traits that help us succeed professionally, while also increasing our personal well-being. In this book, bestselling author Daniel Pink takes you on a journey that details the capacities of the two hemispheres and why appreciation for the right side, with all its inveterate skills in design, empathy, and humor, is growing.According to Pink, the keys to success are in developing and cultivating six senses: design, story, symphony, empathy, play, and meaning. 

* [Quiet: The Power of Introverts in a World That Can't Stop Talking](https://www.amazon.com/Quiet-Power-Introverts-World-Talking/dp/0307352153/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Quiet+by+Susan+Cain&qid=1575170110&s=books&sr=1-1) by Susan Cain  
  Both introverts and extroverts have qualities that can be extremely valuable to the people in their environments, but these personalities need different spaces and treatments to bloom to their full potential. In Quiet, writer and researcher Susan Cain reveals the differences between introverts and extroverts, how the “extroversion ideal” of the last 150 years has transformed the workplace into an extrovert’s dream, and how the talents of the two personality types can be combined for a stunning degree of success. Read this one to get in touch with your inner introvert and learn how to honor it in others.

* [The Righteous Mind: Why Good People Are Divided by Politics and Religion](https://www.amazon.com/Righteous-Mind-Divided-Politics-Religion/dp/0307455777/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533944971&sr=8-1&keywords=The+Righteous+Mind+by+Jonathan+Haidt) by Jonathan Haidt    
  Where does moral judgment come from? If you answered something like “firm rationale,” you’re wrong. Moral judgment actually springs from our ephemeral friend, intuition. Intuition works rather like a lawyer, justifying moral judgments to others and ourselves, supporting our reputation and self interest.  
  The Righteous Mind exposes how it is emotion and intuition, not reason, that drives moral judgment, showing us how understanding the moral foundations on which our interests are based can benefit us in decision making.

* [Tribes: We Need You to Lead Us](https://www.amazon.com/Tribes-We-Need-You-Lead/dp/B001IMTKUK/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Tribes%3A+We+Need+You+to+Lead+Us+by+Seth+Godin&qid=1575123343&sr=8-1) by Seth Godin   
  (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) Start by reading Tribes and then continue on reading everything Godin has written. From his blog to his books and everything in between, Godin is sharing a winning formula for stepping outside of the status quo to do meaningful work. It’s this kind of work that will inspire others to follow, help you get noticed, and leave a legacy long after you’re gone.

* [What Got You Here Won’t Get You There](https://www.amazon.com/What-Got-Here-Wont-There/dp/1401301304/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1519727854&sr=8-1&keywords=What+Got+You+Here+Won%E2%80%99t+Get+You+There+by+Marshall+Goldsmith) by Marshall Goldsmith  
  One review: The title of this book seems misleading. Most of the audience this book is marketed to are early-to-mid-career professionals who are seeking advice on breaking into the C-suite. This book is actually aimed at people who are already at the height of their careers and is a study of how they can reinvent themselves to ensure the continued success of their companies.

———————————————————

## **Consciousness** {#consciousness}

By Adrian Owen, theguardian.com

* [Rethinking Consciousness: A Scientific Theory of Subjective Experience](https://tinyurl.com/yyus3lpg) by Michael S A Graziano 

* [Consciousness Explained](https://www.amazon.com/Consciousness-Explained-Daniel-C-Dennett-ebook/dp/B01N807LD2/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Consciousness+Explained+by+Daniel+Dennett&qid=1575171886&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Daniel Dennett  
  Probably the best introduction to the central ideas and concepts that have preoccupied all great consciousness thinkers throughout history. It may be a little challenging for a general audience, but Dennett masterfully combines ancient philosophical concepts with more familiar modern analogies (such as “the brain as a computer”) in a book that continues to influence contemporary thought on the human condition more than a quarter of a century after its publication.

* [Other Minds: The Octopus, the Sea and the Deep Origins of Consciousness](https://www.amazon.com/Other-Minds-Octopus-Origins-Consciousness/dp/B06WW5K91W/ref=sr_1_2?keywords=Other+Minds%3A+The+Octopus%2C+the+Sea+and+the+Deep+Origins+of+Consciousness&qid=1575171902&s=digital-text&sr=1-2) by Peter Godfrey-Smith  
  Written by a philosopher, yet borrowing heavily from evolutionary biology, this unique and fascinating book – which was shortlisted for this year’s Royal Society science book prize – asks us to rethink intelligence and how we conceptualise “other minds” – notably, that of the octopus. While the octopus evolved independently of humans, it has a similar number of neurons and exhibits highly intelligent patterns of behaviour that allow it to do things like opening screwtop jars from the inside. Yet unlike humans, more than half of an octopus’s neurons are in its arms, suggesting that in searching for intelligent life, we need look beyond those whose form resembles our own.

* [The Diving Bell and the Butterfly: A Memoir of Life in Death](https://www.amazon.com/Diving-Bell-Butterfly-Memoir-Death-ebook/dp/B0015IPEUM/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Diving+Bell+and+the+Butterfly&qid=1575171918&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Jean-Dominique Bauby   
  Not strictly a book about consciousness, I include Bauby’s memoir because it demonstrates the tremendous power of mind over body and is so beautifully written – everybody should read it at least once. A massive stroke left the author permanently paralysed except for the ability to blink his left eye. With the help of an assistant and a writing board, Bauby wrote the book with 200,000 blinks. Bauby recounts: “My mind takes flight like a butterfly. There is so much to do … You can visit the woman you love, slide down beside her and stroke her still-sleeping face. You can build castles in Spain, steal the Golden Fleece, discover Atlantis, realise your childhood dreams and adult ambitions.” This is Bauby’s “butterfly”: the mind unbound. But Bauby – who died in 1997 – was also locked inside the “diving bell”, a sinking iron chamber from which there is no escape.

* [The Centre Cannot Hold: My Journey Through Madness](https://www.amazon.com/Center-Cannot-Hold-Journey-Through-ebook/dp/B000WHVRZS/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Centre+Cannot+Hold%3A&qid=1575171945&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Elyn R Saks  
  This brutally honest memoir provides a rather special perspective on the nature of “other minds”, in this case that of a successful lawyer living with schizophrenia. Saks has struggled with schizophrenia for most of her life, from her early teenage years when she heard voices urging her to harm herself and others to the full-blown psychotic episodes and suicidal fantasies that she continued to battle as a law professor. Schizophrenia certainly changes one’s conscious experience of the world and this is a fascinating and moving account of what it’s like to live in that alternate universe.

* [The Origin of Consciousness in the Breakdown of the Bicameral Mind](https://www.amazon.com/Origin-Consciousness-Breakdown-Bicameral-Mind-ebook/dp/B009MBTRHA/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Origin+of+Consciousness+in+the+Breakdown&qid=1575171961&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Julian Jaynes  
  Jaynes’s daring and brilliant theory about the evolution of human consciousness is that ancient people could not “think” as we do today and were therefore “unconscious”, going about their business as automatons responding to voices in their heads, which they assumed were those of gods. Consciousness as we experience it only began to emerge around 3,000 years ago, when a series of natural disasters and the widespread use of writing forced humans to change. You may not be convinced by all of his arguments, but you’ll like this book a lot. “Either a work of unparalleled genius, or completely out-to-lunch loopy,” wrote one reviewer. That just about sums it up for me too. Jaynes’s bicameral mind heavily influenced the writers of HBO’s update of Westworld and is namechecked several times by lead actor Anthony Hopkins. Respect\!

* [The Astonishing Hypothesis: The Scientific Search for the Soul](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0684801582/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_bibl_vppi_i1) by Francis Crick  
  Nobel laureate Francis Crick was, of course, one of the discoverers of the structure of DNA and was not the first great mind to be distracted by solving the enigma of consciousness in his later years. Perhaps a little too focused on the scientific details for a novice in this area, the book nevertheless deserves a place here because it was one of the first to argue that consciousness is not solely a matter for philosophical introspection, but a subject worthy of serious neuroscientific investigation. 

* [Phi: A Voyage from the Brain to the Soul](https://www.amazon.com/Phi-Voyage-Brain-Giulio-Tononi/dp/030790721X/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Phi%3A+A+Voyage+from+the+Brain+to+the+Soul&qid=1575172048&s=books&sr=1-1) by Giulio Tononi  
  Tononi considers a historically impossible scenario in which Francis Crick, Charles Darwin and Alan Turing each take Galileo on separate trips to discuss different perspectives on consciousness. Crick discusses consciousness and the brain, Darwin the evolution of consciousness and Turing the integration of information. It is beautifully illustrated and blends neuroscience, art and the imagination in a truly unique way.

* [Making Up the Mind: How the Brain Creates Our Mental World](https://www.amazon.com/Making-Mind-Brain-Creates-Mental/dp/1405160225/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Making+Up+the+Mind%3A+How+the+Brain+Creates+Our+Mental+World&qid=1575172063&s=books&sr=1-1) by Chris Frith  
  Illusions, rubber hands, mirror neurons, self-tickling … what more could you want in a book that explains how your brain gives rise to your whole sense of being something in the world? This is a book about how our brains build models based on prediction that generate our experience of the physical world around us. Highly accessible, witty and erudite, this book is the best of its kind. A series of neurological case histories, delivered Oliver Sacks–style, involving phantom limbs, blindsight and other wonders of modern neuroscience. This is not especially a book about consciousness, but many of the patients described have learned to live with profound alterations in the way their brains understand the world. The underlying sentiment is profoundly neuroscientific; that is, that the brain gives rise to all our subjective experiences, however bizarre they may be.

* [The Head Trip: Adventures on the Wheel of Consciousness](https://www.amazon.com/Head-Trip-Adventures-Wheel-Consciousness/dp/1400064848/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Head+Trip%3A+Adventures+on+the+Wheel+of+Consciousness&qid=1575172082&s=books&sr=1-1) by Jeff Warren  
  Finally, if you want to answer some basic questions about your own brain, follow Canadian journalist Warren’s lead and try to alter your own state of consciousness through lucid dreaming, meditation and various other approaches that don’t require drugs. Although the content of the book is more empirical than scientific, a mix of interviews, personal anecdotes and self-deprecating humour provides a thoroughly entertaining take on how to explore consciousness in the comfort of your own home.

  ———————————————————

## **Creativity** {#creativity}

* [Creativity: Flow and the Psychology of Discovery and Invention](https://www.amazon.com/Creativity-Flow-Psychology-Discovery-Invention/dp/0062283251/ref=pd_bxgy_14_img_2?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=0062283251&pd_rd_r=Y38M3MSB6HMQF51TRVHK&pd_rd_w=KP2gx&pd_rd_wg=SohQ7&psc=1&refRID=Y38M3MSB6HMQF51TRVHK) by Mihaly Csikszentmihalyi  

* [Thinkertoys: A Handbook of Creative-Thinking Techniques](https://www.amazon.com/Thinkertoys-Creative-Thinking-Techniques-Michael-Michalko-ebook/dp/B004CFAWU2/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=developgoodhabits-20&linkId=0e1919dc0892941443359174c041e1c9) by [Michael Michalko](https://www.amazon.com/Michael-Michalko/e/B001JRWY3E/ref=dp_byline_cont_ebooks_1)

* [The Innovator's Mindset: Empower Learning, Unleash Talent, and Lead a Culture of Creativity](https://www.amazon.com/Innovators-Mindset-Empower-Learning-Creativity-ebook/dp/B016YTBZKO/ref=sr_1_fkmr0_1?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1523125388&sr=1-1-fkmr0&keywords=The+Innovator%27s+Mindset%3A+Empower+Learning%2C+Unleash+Talent%2C+and+Lead+a+Culture+of+Creativity%2C+by+George+Couros%2C+Entrepreneurial+Mindset+in+the+Classroom) by George Couros, Entrepreneurial Mindset in the Classroom

* [Weird Ideas That Work: How to Build a Creative Company](https://www.amazon.com/Weird-Ideas-That-Work-Creative/dp/0743227883/ref=sr_1_1?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1523125501&sr=8-1&keywords=Weird+Ideas+That+Work%3A+How+to+Build+a+Creative+Company) by Robert I. Sutton 

* [The Art of Possibility](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0142001104/ref=as_li_tf_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=theworldcafe-20&linkCode=as2&camp=1789&creative=9325&creativeASIN=0142001104) by Benjamin Zander and Rosamund Stone Zander  
  Presenting twelve breakthrough practices for bringing creativity into all human endeavors.

* [Creativity, Inc](https://www.amazon.com/Creativity-Inc-Overcoming-Unseen-Inspiration-ebook/dp/B00FUZQYBO/ref=sr_1_1?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1523125474&sr=1-1&keywords=creativity+inc) by Ed Catmull

* [The Science of Serendipity: How to Unlock the Promise of Innovation Paperback](https://www.amazon.com/Science-Serendipity-Unlock-Promise-Innovation/dp/111847810X/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=the+science+of+serendipity&qid=1558632793&s=gateway&sr=8-1) by Matt Kingdon

## **Self Discipline**  {#self-discipline}

* [The Practicing Mind: Developing Focus and Discipline in Your Life — Master Any Skill or Challenge by Learning to Love the Process](https://www.amazon.com/Just-Listen-Discover-Getting-Absolutely/dp/0814436471/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1500142190&sr=8-1&keywords=just+listen+book)   
  *  If an activity doesn't enrich you, than don't do it   
  * All things of lasting and deep value require time and nurturing and come to us only through our own effort.   
  * Based on Zen and on being process oriented. The message it's trying to give out is: to stay in the present moment. The practicing mind got it's title I assume when we are focused on the actual process instead of the overarching goal.   
  * Do, Observe and Correct. It has some roots in eastern philosophy, meditation, zen or the likes but for me it's CBT-ish. Tackling and solving problems with emotional indifference especially at times when you're just plain irrational.  
  * Great for things like weight loss

* [Discipline Your Mind: Control Your Thoughts, Boost Willpower, Develop Mental Toughness](https://www.amazon.com/Discipline-Your-Mind-Willpower-Toughness-ebook/dp/B071ZB72CB/ref=sr_1_15?ie=UTF8&qid=1502368270&sr=8-15&keywords=discipline) by Zoe McKey  
  * Focus on your Comparative Advantage, not necessarily what you are best at  
  * Focus on Results, not time spent  
  * Think before you Read or Write. The Why.  
  * Plan ahead but be ready to Change during the day  
  * Be open to others ideas in your meetings  
  * Keep your life and work short and simple  
  * description of the differences among career aims / objectives / targets \- by separating into distinct time horizons and the recognition that only a subset of shorter timelines contribute to longer term goals, Pozen succinctly demonstrates his style for prioritization.

* [No Excuses\!: The Power of Self-Discipline](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1593156324/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=mannyb-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=1593156324&linkId=6c03bdf427e728c3c1386208b691bcb7) by Brian Tracy

* [4 Essential Keys to Effective Communication in Love, Life, Work--Anywhere\!: A How-To Guide for Practicing the Empathic](https://www.amazon.com/Essential-Keys-Effective-Communication-Work-Anywhere-ebook/dp/B071DFFYYD/ref=sr_1_3_sspa?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1546461536&sr=1-3-spons&keywords=empathy&psc=1)  by Bento C. Leal III

# **Business** {#business}

## **Startups** {#startups}

* [The Hard Thing About Hard Things: Building a Business When There Are No Easy Answers](https://www.amazon.com/Hard-Thing-About-Things-Building-ebook/dp/B00DQ845EA/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533944092&sr=8-1&keywords=The+Hard+Thing+about+Hard+Things) by Ben Horowitz.   The rough side of Entrepreneurship.

* [Founding Brothers: The Revolutionary Generation](https://www.amazon.com/Founding-Brothers-Revolutionary-Joseph-Ellis/dp/0375705244/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533944028&sr=8-1&keywords=founding+brothers+by+joseph+j.+ellis) by Joseph J. Ellis

* [The Lean Startup](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0307887898/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=mannyb-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=0307887898&linkId=8c02326b6ae369cf07665d317af1b9f5) by Eric Ries

* [Do More Faster](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0470929839/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=mannyb-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=0470929839&linkId=a88bd91a827f025c8f11433ab79b0d07) by Brad Feld

* [Zero to One](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0804139296/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=mannyb-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=0804139296&linkId=8e71ec71305ddb3bf10e1aae2910fb2d) by Peter Theil

  (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) As CEO of Zappo, Tony Hsieh built a massively successful business by doing what everyone else talks about: putting the customer first and hiring the right people. Serving customers and company culture were the main focus. As a result employees and customers were happy and satisfied. Hsieh was able to dismantle traditional corporate leadership and deliver happiness and loads of profit along the way

## **Innovation** {#innovation}

* [The Innovator's Mindset: Empower Learning, Unleash Talent, and Lead a Culture of Creativity](https://www.amazon.com/Innovators-Mindset-Empower-Learning-Creativity-ebook/dp/B016YTBZKO) by George Couros, Entrepreneurial Mindset in the Classroom

* [The Innovator's Dilemma: The Revolutionary Book That Will Change the Way You Do Business](https://www.amazon.com/Innovators-Dilemma-Revolutionary-Change-Business/dp/0062060244/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1534009550&sr=8-2&keywords=The+Innovator%E2%80%99s+Dilemma+by+Clayton+Christensen) by Clayton Christensen

* (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) Here Harvard professor and businessman Clayton Christensen lays out the path to “disruptive innovation.” This, as described by Christensen, requires rejecting the needs of the customer right now in favor of adopting new methods and technologies that will meet their needs in the future. Early adopters and innovators get ahead; all of the others fall behind.

* [Loonshots: How to Nurture the Crazy Ideas That Win Wars, Cure Diseases, and Transform Industries](https://www.amazon.com/Loonshots-Nurture-Diseases-Transform-Industries/dp/B07PC2KZBZ/ref=sr_1_1?crid=3UBOM1LJCZ0OL&keywords=Loonshots%2C+Safi+Bahcall&qid=1569267684&sprefix=propacking+%2Caps%2C139&sr=8-1) by Safi Bahcall

* [Progress: Ten Reasons to Look Forward to the Future](https://www.amazon.com/Progress-Reasons-Look-Forward-Future/dp/1786070650/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Progress+by+Johan+Norberg&qid=1575172554&s=books&sr=1-1) by Johan Norberg

P. Seligman  

* [Solve for Happy: Engineer Your Path to Joy](https://www.amazon.com/Solve-Happy-Engineer-Your-Path/dp/1501157558/ref=sr_1_1?crid=2ZALK3RZD5CBG&keywords=mo+gawdat&qid=1550686000&s=gateway&sprefix=mo+g%2Caps%2C139&sr=8-1) by Mo Gawdat 

* [Meditations](https://www.amazon.com/gp/slredirect/picassoRedirect.html/ref=pa_sp_atf_stripbooks_sr_pg1_1?ie=UTF8&adId=A07971392UXJZ81X5P83M&url=%2FMeditations-Marcus-Aurelius%2Fdp%2F1503280462%2Fref%3Dsr_1_1_sspa%3Fcrid%3DMIRD4JDIULFE%26keywords%3Dmeditations%2Bmarcus%2Baurelius%26qid%3D1575168404%26s%3Dbooks%26sprefix%3Dmeditati%252Cstripbooks%252C146%26sr%3D1-1-spons%26psc%3D1&qualifier=1575168403&id=4098469783606766&widgetName=sp_atf) by Marcus Aurelius (Gregory Hays translation)  
  (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) Although Aurelius was writing for himself, the surviving text is a road map to living a better life. By removing the excess, Aurelius shows us all how to rise above distractions to maintain our principles. Rooted in Stoic philosophy, Meditations is practical advice for controlling your thoughts, emotions, and actions to remove stress from your life.

* [The Power of One](https://www.amazon.com/Power-One-Novel-Bryce-Courtenay/dp/034541005X/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1534009157&sr=8-1&keywords=The+Power+of+One+by+Bryce+Courtenay) by Bryce Courtenay

* [The Alchemist](https://www.amazon.com/Alchemist-Paulo-Coelho/dp/0062315005/ref=sr_1_1?crid=1PU5OM8QDL8Y8&keywords=alchemist+book&qid=1575168377&s=books&sprefix=alchemi%2Cstripbooks%2C166&sr=1-1) by Paulo Coelho  
  (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) Life is a journey. Each one of us should be trying to follow our own personal legend (that is, what you have always wanted to accomplish). The tale of Santiago, a shepherd boy, reveals what happens when we pursue our own legend: “the universe conspires in helping you to achieve it.”

* [Man’s Search for Meaning](https://www.amazon.com/Mans-Search-Meaning-Viktor-Frankl/dp/080701429X/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Man%E2%80%99s+Search+for+Meaning+By+Viktor+E.+Frankl&qid=1556501578&s=gateway&sr=8-1) By Viktor E. Frankl  
  (annotated by [Dr. Woody Woodward](https://twitter.com/drwoody)) Any aspiring leader should start by tackling the basics of human motivation. Man’s Search for Meaning illustrates the power of one of our primary motivators: the need for purpose. The book chronicles Frankl’s experiences and observations during his imprisonment at Auschwitz, showing how purpose, attitude and mindset can play such a critical role in overcoming the toughest of circumstances. A must read\!

**Managing your negative thoughts**

* [Positive Intelligence](https://amzn.to/2Lveqab) by Shirzad Chamine: By a former CEO of CTI, a deeper dive into the Saboteur (and accomplices) and your inner leader(s) (not necessarily your "Captain" and crew).

* [Taming Your Gremlin: A Surprisingly Simple Method for Getting Out of Your Own Way](https://www.amazon.com/Taming-Your-Gremlin-Surprisingly-Getting/dp/0060520221/ref=sr_1_1?crid=1EOKYNZERFM6Z&keywords=taming+your+gremlin&qid=1575593898&sprefix=10%25%2Caps%2C156&sr=8-1) by Rick Carson

* [The Big Leap: Conquer Your Hidden Fear and Take Life to the Next Level](https://www.amazon.com/Big-Leap-Conquer-Hidden-Level/dp/0061735361/ref=sr_1_1?crid=1EOKYNZERFM6Z&keywords=the+big+leap&qid=1575594261&sprefix=10%25%2Caps%2C156&sr=8-1) by Gay Hendricks

* [Meet Your Inside Team: How to Turn Internal Conflict into Clarity and Move Forward with Your Life](https://www.amazon.com/Meet-Your-Inside-Team-Internal/dp/0692155198/ref=sr_1_1?crid=1EOKYNZERFM6Z&keywords=Meet+Your+Inside+Team%3A+How+to+Turn+Internal+Conflict+into+Clarity&qid=1575594640&sprefix=10%25%2Caps%2C156&sr=8-1) by Cynthia Loy Darst

## **Vulnerability** {#vulnerability}

* [The Power of Vulnerability](https://www.amazon.com/Power-Vulnerability-Create-Leaders-Shifting/dp/1626344736) by Barry Kaplan and Jeffrey Manchester  
  The fear will tug at your sleeves and attempt to pull you back into a spiral of second guessing. Don’t try to suppress that anxiety. Acknowledge it, be thankful that the presence of the emotion keeps you grounded, and then move through it.

* [Daring Greatly](https://www.amazon.com/Daring-Greatly-Courage-Vulnerable-Transforms/dp/1592408419) by Brené Brown  
  Vulnerability is not weakness, and the uncertainty, risk, and emotional exposure we face every day are not optional. Our only choice is a question of engagement. Our willingness to own and engage with our vulnerability determines the depth of our courage and the clarity of our purpose; the level to which we protect ourselves from being vulnerable is a measure of our fear and disconnection. If you engage with your discomfort at the idea of changing your habits – you’ll never find a way to break with the old.  (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) Being vulnerable doesn’t have to be a weakness. Fear and shame shouldn’t prevent us from daring to do big things. Instead, Brown tells us that it’s most important to show up; to try and to fail. Because coming up short is better than never having tried at all.

* [The Gifts of Imperfection](https://www.amazon.com/Gifts-Imperfection-Think-Supposed-Embrace/dp/159285849X/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1529604096&sr=8-2&keywords=gifts+of+imperfection) by Brené Brown  
  When our embarrassments and fears lie, we often listen to them anyway. They thwart our gratitude, acceptance, and compassion—our goodness. They insist, “I am not worthy.” But we *are* worthy—of self-discovery, personal growth, and boundless love. Key lessons:  
  * Gut feelings and grounded reasoning aren’t opposing forces, just a mix.  
  * Comparison breeds conformity. The more you compete, the more boring you’ll get.  
  * The opposite of play isn’t work, it’s depression.

* [When I say no I feel guilty](https://www.amazon.com/When-Say-No-Feel-Guilty-ebook/dp/B004IK8Q22/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533944531&sr=8-1&keywords=When+I+say+no+I+feel+guilty+by+Manuel+J.+Smith) by Manuel J. Smith  
  Beware of those who try to impose their standards of “right” and “wrong” to manipulate you. Smith lists your 10 “assertive rights,” the most important being the right to be the ultimate judge of your own behavior. He details several verbal techniques you can use to block manipulation, and encourage productive communication and negotiation. He supports each tactic with sample dialogues from real-life situations. In summary:  
  * How other people may attempt to manipulate your behavior to get you to do what they want;  
  * What your basic “assertive rights” are; and  
  * How to thwart others’ manipulative behavior and promote productive communication at work and at home.

* [Hello, Fears: Crush Your Comfort Zone and Become Who You're Meant to Be](https://www.amazon.com/Hello-Fears-Crush-Comfort-Become-ebook/dp/B086D6ZY7R/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=hello+fears&qid=1590604948&sr=8-1) by Michelle Poler

\*———————————————————

## **Confidence**  {#confidence}

* [The War of Art](https://www.amazon.com/War-Art-Steven-Pressfield-ebook/dp/B007A4SDCG/ref=sr_1_1?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1534009731&sr=1-1&keywords=the+war+of+art+by+steven+pressfield) by Steve Pressfield  
  (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) Anything you create is going to require one heck of a battle: that’s the war of art. Every single person in the world who has written a book, published an article, started a business, or made “art” has been scared out of their mind. Procrastination, fear, and self-doubt strike everyone. The only way to beat them is to make stuff and share it with the world.

* [Managing the Mental Game](https://www.amazon.com/Managing-Mental-Game-Effectively-Uncertainty/dp/0990670341/ref=cm_cr_arp_d_product_top?ie=UTF8) by Jeff Boss  
  Using a blend of mental-training methodologies, former Navy SEAL Jeff Boss shows readers how to build self-confidence and fortitude, enabling them to reach new levels of success. Managing the Mental Game contains useful exercises on learning how to manage chaos and pressure in order to stay clear headed and calm in uncertain and difficult situations. Boss’s advice helps you understand that stress is a mental game that can be overcome, often by avoiding mental pitfalls and learning to replace negative thoughts with positive ones.

* [Feel the Fear and Do It Anyway: Dynamic techniques for turning Fear, Indecision and Anger into Power, Action and Love](https://www.amazon.com/Feel-Fear-Anyway%C2%AE-techniques-Indecision-ebook/dp/B008OXEROK/ref=sr_1_1?crid=UPSLE7EF69FO&keywords=feel+the+fear+and+do+it+anyway&qid=1575583711&s=digital-text&sprefix=Feel+the+Fea%2Cdigital-text%2C171&sr=1-1) by Susan Jeffers

# Leadership and Management  {#leadership-and-management}

## **General Leadership**  {#general-leadership}

* [Leadership](https://www.amazon.com/dp/B007MFECFU/?coliid=I4AF2319XRFHV&colid=E2P2OAQS8S5Y&psc=0) by James MacGregor Burns   
  Pulitzer Prize–winning historian examines transformational leaders from Moses to Machiavelli to Martin Luther King Jr. Burns examines the qualities that make certain leaders—in America and elsewhere—succeed as transformative figures. Through insightful anecdotes and historical analysis, Burns scrutinizes the charisma, vision, and persuasive power of individuals able to imbue followers with a common sense of purpose, from the founding fathers to FDR, Gandhi to Napoleon. 

* [The Only Leaders Worth Following: Why Some Leaders Succeed, Others Fail, and How the Quality of Our Lives Hangs in the Balance](https://tinyurl.com/y3n3svck) by Tim Spiker

* [Leadership and the New Science](https://www.amazon.com/Leadership-New-Science-Margaret-Wheatley/dp/1576750558?crid=2Q3QSYUDQOX0O&keywords=margaret+wheatley&qid=1540815014&sprefix=samsung+ssd%2Caps%2C244&sr=8-9&ref=sr_1_9) by Margaret J. Wheatley    From ORSC Training. Discusses the Ground Conditions for change.

* [Leadership Is an Art](https://www.amazon.com/Leadership-Art-Max-Depree-ebook/dp/B0053CT29A/ref=sr_1_2?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1542828287&sr=1-2&keywords=leadership+is+an+art+by+max+depree) by Max Depree

* [Scaling Leadership: Building Organizational Capability and Capacity to Create Outcomes that Matter Most](https://www.amazon.com/Scaling-Leadership-Building-Organizational-Capability/dp/B07NJ272YS/ref=sr_1_3?keywords=bob+anderson+leadership&qid=1568402079&sr=8-3) by Robert J. Anderson, William A. Adams, et al. (the Leadership Circle founders)

* [The 15 Commitments of Conscious Leadership: A New Paradigm for Sustainable Success](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00R3MHWUE/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_hsch_vapi_tkin_p1_i0) by Jim Dethmer  (Author), Diana Chapman, Kaley Klemp 

* [The Leadership Shadow: How to Recognize and Avoid Derailment, Hubris and Overdrive](https://www.amazon.com/Leadership-Shadow-Recognize-Derailment-Overdrive-ebook/dp/B00LZTVRLQ/ref=sr_1_2?keywords=The+leadership+shadow+by+Erik+de+Haan&qid=1575173564&s=books&sr=1-2) by Erik de Haan   
  Good book on blind spots for leaders

### Leadership Development

* [Self as instrument](http://leadershipdiamond.blogspot.com/2010/09/self-as-instrument.html)

* [Social: Why Our Brains Are Wired to Connect](https://www.amazon.com/Social-Why-Brains-Wired-Connect/dp/0307889106/ref=asap_bc?ie=UTF8) by Matthew Lieberman: importance of social connections

* [Changing on the Job: Developing Leaders for a Complex World](https://www.amazon.com/Changing-Job-Developing-Leaders-Complex/dp/0804786968/ref=sr_1_3?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1517684657&sr=1-3&keywords=changing+on+the+job) by Jennifer Garvey Berger  

* [Principles](https://www.amazon.com/Principles-Life-and-Work/dp/B074B2CZJG/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1517684733&sr=1-1-spons&keywords=Principles+by+Ray+Dalio) by Ray Dalio (via Amazon recommendations)

* [Reinventing Organizations](https://www.amazon.com/Reinventing-Organizations-Illustrated-Invitation-Conversation/dp/2960133552/ref=sr_1_fkmr0_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1517684755&sr=1-1-fkmr0&keywords=Stages+of+Org+Development+by+Laloux+and+Wilber) by Laloux and Wilber

* [Conscious Business: How to Build Value through Values](https://www.amazon.com/Conscious-Business-Build-through-Values/dp/1622032020/ref=sr_1_3?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1517684841&sr=1-3) by Fred Kofman and Ken Wilber

* Websites:  
  * [Growth Edge Coaching](https://www.growthedgecoaching.com/) website from GSL offsite  
  * [Cultivating Leadership](https://www.cultivatingleadership.co.nz/) website from GSL offsite

* [How Leaders Improve: A Playbook for Leaders Who Want to Get Better Now](https://www.amazon.com/How-Leaders-Improve-Playbook-Better-ebook-dp-B0779LVW6N/dp/B0779LVW6N/ref=mt_kindle?_encoding=UTF8&me=&qid=) by J. Gates, J. Graddy, S. Lindekens 

* [Immunity to Change](https://www.amazon.com/Immunity-Change-Potential-Organization-Leadership/dp/1422117367/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1517685185&sr=1-1&keywords=Immunity+to+Change) by Kegan and Lisa Layhe; Talks and Kegan and Lahey and [talks](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6reQY1MIBA8) [interview](https://www.forbes.com/sites/berlinschoolofcreativeleadership/2016/04/23/5-questions-with-robert-kegan-lisa-lahey-and-andy-fleming-on-ddos/#6afc09367eed). [Synopsis](https://www.extension.harvard.edu/inside-extension/surprising-reason-we-dont-keep-our-resolutions-how-overcome-it) from Harvard program.

* [Being Wrong: Adventures in the Margin of Error](https://www.amazon.com/Being-Wrong-Adventures-Margin-Error/dp/0061176052/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1517685077&sr=1-1&keywords=on+being+wrong) by Kathryn Schulz  and [podcast](https://longform.org/podcast)

* [Conscious Leadership](https://www.amazon.com/Conscious-Leadership-Steven-Bowman/dp/1939261295/ref=sr_1_3?crid=HJ9E7KGFL74Z&keywords=conscious+leadership&qid=1550090587&s=gateway&sprefix=learned+opti%2Caps%2C139&sr=8-3) by Steven Bowman, Chutisa Bowman, Gary Douglas 

* [The Starfish and the Spider: The Unstoppable Power of Leaderless Organizations](https://www.amazon.com/Starfish-Spider-Unstoppable-Leaderless-Organizations/dp/1591841437/ref=sr_1_1?crid=29R879WV01WD0&keywords=spider+starfish&qid=1555605442&s=gateway&sprefix=celeste+ng%2Caps%2C200&sr=8-1) by Ori Brafman and Rod A. Beckstrom

* [An Everyone Culture: Becoming a Deliberately Developmental Organization](https://www.amazon.com/dp/B01BO2ITX2/?ref=idea_lv_dp_ov_d) by Robert Kegan (hardcopy)

* [What Got You Here Won't Get You There: How Successful People Become Even More Successful](https://www.amazon.com/What-Got-Here-Wont-There/dp/1401301304/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=What+Got+You+Here+Won%27t+Get+You+There&qid=1575161831&sr=8-1) by Marshall Goldsmith and Mark Reiter

* [Authentic Leadership: Rediscovering the Secrets to Creating Lasting Value](https://www.amazon.com/Authentic-Leadership-Rediscovering-Secrets-Creating/dp/0787975281/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1517780248&sr=8-1&keywords=Authentic+Leadership%3A+Rediscovering+the+Secrets+to+Creating+Lasting+Value) by Bill George

* #### [The Effective Executive: The Definitive Guide to Getting the Right Things Done](https://www.amazon.com/Effective-Executive-Definitive-Harperbusiness-Essentials/dp/0060833459/ref=sr_1_1?crid=1EOKYNZERFM6Z&keywords=The+Effective+Executive%3A+The+Definitive+Guide+to+Getting+the+Right+Things+Done&qid=1575161650&sprefix=10%25%2Caps%2C156&sr=8-1) by Peter Drucker

* [The SPEED of TRUST: The One Thing That Changes Everything](https://www.amazon.com/SPEED-TRUST-Thing-Changes-Everything/dp/1416549005/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Speed+of+Trust&qid=1575161730&sr=8-1) by Stephen Covey

* [The Power of Vulnerability: Teachings of Authenticity, Connection, and Courage](https://www.amazon.com/Power-Vulnerability-Teachings-Authenticity-Connection/dp/B00D1Z9RFU/ref=sr_1_1?crid=WU54S3IBCGUO&keywords=power+of+vulnerability+brene+brown+book&qid=1575161923&sprefix=power+of+vuln%2Caps%2C148&sr=8-1) by Brené Brown 

* [The Leadership Pipeline: How to Build the Leadership Powered Company](https://www.amazon.com/Leadership-Pipeline-Build-Powered-Company/dp/0470894563/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Leadership+Pipeline&qid=1575162762&sr=8-1) by Ram Charan, Stephen Drotter

* [https://hbr.org/2005/12/how-to-build-your-network](https://hbr.org/2005/12/how-to-build-your-network)

* [That Discomfort You’re Feeling Is Grief](https://hbr.org/2020/03/that-discomfort-youre-feeling-is-grief)

* [It's the Manager: Gallup finds the quality of managers and team leaders is the single biggest factor in your organization's long-term success](https://www.amazon.com/Its-Manager-managers-organizations-long-term/dp/1595622241) by Jim Clifton, Jim Harter

### Scaling {#scaling}

* [Scaling Up Excellence: Getting to More Without Settling for Less](https://www.amazon.com/Scaling-Up-Excellence-Getting-Settling/dp/0385347022/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1534038442&sr=1-1&keywords=Scaling+Up+Excellence) by Bob Sutton and Huggy Rao  

* [The Art of Scalability: Scalable Web Architecture, Processes, and Organizations for the Modern Enterprise](https://www.amazon.com/Art-Scalability-Architecture-Organizations-Enterprise/dp/0134032802/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=THE+ART+OF+SCALABILITY&qid=1575162631&sr=8-1) by Martin L. Abbott and Michael T. Fisher 

* [Scaling Leadership: Building Organizational Capability and Capacity to Create Outcomes that Matter Most](https://www.amazon.com/Scaling-Leadership-Building-Organizational-Capability/dp/B07NJ272YS/ref=sr_1_3?keywords=bob+anderson+leadership&qid=1568402079&sr=8-3) by Robert J. Anderson, William A. Adams, et al. (the Leadership Circle founders) 

* [Scaling Up: How a Few Companies Make It...and Why the Rest Don't](http://www.amazon.com/Scaling-Up-Companies-Rockefeller-Habits/dp/0986019526/ref=asap_bc?ie=UTF8) by Verne Harnish 

### From Deep Patel, entrepreneur.com

* [Managing the Mental Game](https://www.amazon.com/Managing-Mental-Game-Effectively-Uncertainty/dp/0990670341/ref=cm_cr_arp_d_product_top?ie=UTF8) by Jeff Boss  
  Using a blend of mental-training methodologies, former Navy SEAL Jeff Boss shows readers how to build self-confidence and fortitude, enabling them to reach new levels of success. Managing the Mental Game contains useful exercises on learning how to manage chaos and pressure in order to stay clear headed and calm in uncertain and difficult situations. Boss’s advice helps you understand that stress is a mental game that can be overcome, often by avoiding mental pitfalls and learning to replace negative thoughts with positive ones.  
  Related: Top 10 Online Book Clubs For Entrepreneurial Inspiration

* [Start With Why: How Great Leaders Inspire Everyone to Take Action](https://www.amazon.com/Start-Why-Leaders-Inspire-Everyone-ebook/dp/B002Q6XUE4/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1533945387&sr=8-2&keywords=Start+With+Why+by+Simon+Sinek) by Simon Sinek  
  This book centers on an important business truth: People don’t buy what you do, they buy why you do it. Simon Sinek explains this concept in Start With Why by delving into a few basic questions. One key question he poses is why some people and organizations are more innovative, influential and profitable than others. He also asks why so few are able to repeat their success. If you are struggling to create a long-term vision and guiding principles as you navigate business and life, this book can give you the inspiration to begin moving in the right direction.

* [The Go-Giver: A Little Story About a Powerful Business Idea](https://www.amazon.com/Go-Giver-Expanded-Little-Powerful-Business/dp/1591848288/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Go-Giver+Leader+by+Bob+Burg+and+John+David+Mann&qid=1575168133&s=books&sr=1-1) by Bob Burg and John David Mann  
  Great leaders don’t try to act like “leaders.” Instead, they strive to be more human. They focus on the concept that “if you give, you shall receive.” Burg and Mann tell a compelling tale of an ambitious young executive trying to lead a struggling small business to make a crucial decision. The Go-Giver Leader promotes a mindset of higher consciousness. It expands on the idea that your influence is determined by whether you place others’ interests first. Leaders who do this will create prosperity for their communities and society, as well as for their companies and employees.

* [The Dip: A Little Book That Teaches You When to Quit (and When to Stick)](https://www.amazon.com/Dip-Little-Book-Teaches-Stick/dp/1591841666/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Dip+by+Seth+Godin&qid=1575168104&s=books&sr=1-1) by Seth Godin  
  The Dip proves that winners do quit, and quitters do win. Seth Godin shows that winners quit quickly and often, until they commit to beating the right “dip.” Winners are those who know that the bigger the barrier, the bigger the reward for getting past it. If you can beat the dip, you’ll earn profits, glory and long-term security. What this book will do is help you determine if you’re in a dip that’s worthy of your time, effort and talents.

* [Freakonomics](https://www.amazon.com/Freakonomics-Rev-Ed-Economist-Everything-ebook/dp/B000MAH66Y/ref=sr_1_1?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1534010308&sr=1-1&keywords=freakonomics+book) by Steven D. Levitt and Stephen J. Dubner  [short version](http://www.businessinsider.com/freakonomics-levitt-dubner-2011-8?op=1)  
  As the Wall Street Journal proclaims, “If Indiana Jones were an economist, he’d be Steven Levitt.” Freakonomics is a groundbreaking collaboration between Levitt and Stephen J. Dubner, an award-winning author and journalist. The two examined the inner workings of a crack gang, the truth about real estate agents and the secrets of the Ku Klux Klan. The result of their work is this book, which powerfully shows how, at its core, economics is the study of incentives. It is how people get what they want or need, especially when other people are trying to get the same thing.

* [Essentialism: The Disciplined Pursuit of Less](https://www.amazon.com/Essentialism-Disciplined-Pursuit-Less/dp/B00IWYP5NI/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Essentialism+by+Greg+McKeown&qid=1575168072&s=books&sr=1-1) by Greg McKeown  
  Instead of trying to manage your time more efficiently, Essentialism helps you focus on getting the right things done. This isn’t about time management or productivity improvement. Greg McKeown teaches a systematic discipline for discerning what is absolutely essential and eliminating everything else. By pursuing “less,” we are empowered to prioritize what is truly important in our lives, and thus are able to give the highest possible contribution toward those things.

* [Drive: The Surprising Truth About What Motivates Us](https://www.amazon.com/Drive-Surprising-Truth-About-Motivates/dp/1594484805/ref=pd_sim_14_3?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=1594484805&pd_rd_r=YCBE110RHN5TGQHC6855&pd_rd_w=AZsEs&pd_rd_wg=J6WD8&psc=1&refRID=YCBE110RHN5TGQHC6855) by Daniel Pink  
  We all have an innate desire to be in control of our lives and create new things. These two desires are what truly drive us. The “carrot and stick” approach that most corporations use to motivate people doesn’t deliver high performance or results because it ignores the most important element: intrinsic (or internal) motivation. Daniel H. Pink asserts in Drive that the secret to prompting higher achieving workers is to tap into their internal motivation. Doing so will increase satisfaction at work, at school and at home, and also empower us to better ourselves and our world.

* [Getting Things Done: The Art of Stress-Free Productivity](https://www.amazon.com/Getting-Things-Done-Stress-Free-Productivity/dp/0143126563/ref=sr_1_3?keywords=getting+things+done&qid=1575167862&s=books&sr=1-3) by David Allen and James Fallows  
  Since Getting Things Done was first published 15 years ago, “GTD” has become shorthand for an entire method of approaching professional and personal tasks. This updated version includes new material that adds fresh perspectives to David Allen’s classic text on how to attain maximum efficiency. Allen offers important tools and strategies on how to focus our energy and manage workflows, including how to get through work tasks quickly, delegate when appropriate and defer when necessary,

* [Give and Take](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0143124986/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_bibl_vppi_i1) by Adam Grant  
  Success is not just about hard work, talent and luck. Our ability to achieve is increasingly dependent on how well we interact with others. Adam Grant's book shows that most people operate as takers, matchers or givers. Whereas takers strive to get as much as possible from others and matchers aim to trade evenly, givers are a rare breed who contribute to others without expecting anything in return. When used correctly, giving can attain extraordinary results.

* [What They Don't Teach You at Harvard Business School](https://www.amazon.com/gp/slredirect/picassoRedirect.html/ref=pa_sp_atf_stripbooks_sr_pg1_1?ie=UTF8&adId=A05586932FRVVKK4V7VEL&url=%2FWhat-They-Teach-Business-School-ebook%2Fdp%2FB071VKW8PZ%2Fref%3Dsr_1_1_sspa%3Fkeywords%3DWhat%2BThey%2BDon%2527t%2BTeach%2BYou%2Bat%2BHarvard%2BBusiness%2BSchool%26qid%3D1575167955%26s%3Dbooks%26sr%3D1-1-spons%26psc%3D1&qualifier=1575167955&id=6051999283402436&widgetName=sp_atf) by Mark H. McCormack  
  Like a wise mentor, this book offers real-world guidance and concise information that you won’t learn elsewhere. What They Don’t Teach You at Harvard Business School is a complement to a traditional business background, offered by a seasoned luminary in the field. Mark H. McCormack teaches you how to use his “applied people sense” in sales, negotiation, executive time management and reading yourself and others.

### Leadership: Curated Readings {#leadership:-curated-readings}

* [Strengths Based Leadership: Great Leaders, Teams, and Why People Follow](https://www.amazon.com/Strengths-Based-Leadership-Leaders-People/dp/1595620257/ref=sr_1_3?ie=UTF8&qid=1533945233&sr=8-3&keywords=Strengths+Based+Leadership+by+Tom+Rath) by Tom Rath and Barry Conchie  
  (annotated by [Geoffrey James](https://www.inc.com/geoffrey-james/the-12-leadership-books-every-boss-should-read.html)) While I don't know whether the research behind this book (and the online survey it promotes) has been replicated or substantiated, this book's intent to be data-driven rather than opinion-driven is to be applauded.

* [Team of Rivals: The Political Genius of Abraham Lincoln](https://www.amazon.com/Team-Rivals-Political-Abraham-Lincoln/dp/0743270754/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533945983&sr=8-1&keywords=Team+of+Rivals+by+Doris+Kearns+Goodwin) by Doris Kearns Goodwin  
  (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) If Abe Lincoln can unite his cabinet and the country around abolishing slavery amidst war, you can probably reconcile conflicting personalities in your company. Meshing people of divergent ideologies into a team or group is an admirable leadership trait. In Team of Rivals Kearns Goodwin recounts the story of how Lincoln surrounded himself with the best people, despite their differences. He was humble and unafraid to be challenged: two traits that will serve every leader.

* [Endurance: Shackleton’s Incredible Voyage](https://www.amazon.com/Endurance-Shackletons-Incredible-Alfred-Lansing/dp/0465062881/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533946019&sr=8-1&keywords=Endurance+by+Alfred+Lansing) by Alfred Lansing  
  (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) In 1914, explorer Edward Shackleton undertook an expedition to the South Pole. Although the mission was a failure, the resulting story of survival in the ice-bound Antarctic seas serves as a guidepost for leaders confronted with adversity.

* [Multipliers: How the Best Leaders Make Everyone Smarter](https://www.amazon.com/Multipliers-Best-Leaders-Everyone-Smarter-ebook/dp/B003M69A4Q/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1530305241&sr=8-2&keywords=multipliers) by Liz Wiseman and Greg McKeown 

* [The 21 Irrefutable Laws of Leadership](https://www.amazon.com/21-Irrefutable-Laws-Leadership-Anniversary/dp/0785288376/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1533945767&sr=8-2&keywords=The+21+Irrefutable+Laws+of+Leadership) by John C. Maxwell   
  (annotated by [Geoffrey James](https://www.inc.com/geoffrey-james/the-12-leadership-books-every-boss-should-read.html)) I don't know about you, but I'm getting pretty tired of the "xxx principles" format. Nevertheless, this is a classic of that genre and contains a wealth of accessible, easily understood advice.

* [Leadership and Self-Deception: Getting Out of the Box](https://www.amazon.com/Leadership-Self-Deception-Getting-Out-Box/dp/1576759776/ref=sr_1_3?ie=UTF8&qid=1533945786&sr=8-3&keywords=Leadership+and+Self-Deception+by+The+Arbinger+Institute) by The Arbinger Institute  
  (annotated by [Geoffrey James](https://www.inc.com/geoffrey-james/the-12-leadership-books-every-boss-should-read.html)) Many bosses suffer from confirmation bias, where every fact and event is framed so that it reinforces the boss's preconceived notions. I've watched huge companies topple as the result of self-deception; this book makes you painfully aware of your own tendency toward it.

* [Mastering Leadership: An Integrated Framework for Breakthrough Performance and Extraordinary Business Results](https://www.amazon.com/Mastering-Leadership-Breakthrough-Performance-Extraordinary-ebook/dp/B015EN6NXK/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1534008785&sr=8-1&keywords=Mastering+Leadership%3A+An+Integrated+Framework+for+Breakthrough+Performance+and+Extraordinary+Business+Results) By Robert J. Anderson and William A. Adams  
  (annotated by [Bill Gardner](https://twitter.com/LeadingThots)) Before Mastering Leadership was published last year, I would have mentioned several, but it transcends all my previous favorites. It’s comprehensive enough to actually include everything from every previous model, yet presented in an easy to understand manner. The writing holds the reader’s attention with stories and concrete examples. For new, aspiring or long-tenured leaders, this book is a must.

* [Originals: How Non-Conformists Move the World](https://www.amazon.com/Originals-How-Non-Conformists-Move-World/dp/014312885X/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1534008825&sr=8-1&keywords=Originals%3A+How+Non-Conformists+Move+the+World) By Adam Grant  
  (annotated by [Taylor Jacobson](http://twitter.com/TaylorJacobson)) Adam Grant, a professor at the Wharton School of Business, tackles several invaluable leadership questions in his new book Originals: “Who does original work?” “What are the conditions that help individuals and companies innovate?” “What conditions must be present for original ideas to take root?” Grant provides research-backed ideas on how each of us can be more original.

* [The Truth About Leadership](https://www.amazon.com/Truth-about-Leadership-Heart-Matter/dp/0470633549/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1534009263&sr=8-1&keywords=The+Truth+About+Leadership+by+James+M.+Kouzes+and+Barry+Z.+Posner) by James M. Kouzes and Barry Z. Posner  
  (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) There are some things that will always play a role in effective leadership. Trust, credibility, and ethics are among those things. Kouzes and Posner reveal 30 years of research that support these and other core principles.

* [Start with Why: How Great Leaders Inspire Everyone to Take Action](https://www.amazon.com/Start-Why-Leaders-Inspire-Everyone/dp/1591846447/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1508439853&sr=8-1&keywords=start+with+why) by Simon Sinek

* [Leading with Kindness: How Good People Consistently Get Superior Results](https://www.amazon.com/dp/0814401562/_encoding=UTF8?coliid=I3CGTYNPDB2ZK2&colid=E2P2OAQS8S5Y) by William F. Baker and Michael O'Malley 

* [The Extraordinary Leader: Turning Good Managers into Great Leaders](https://www.amazon.com/Extraordinary-Leader-Turning-Managers-Leaders/dp/0071628088/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1534039020&sr=1-1&keywords=The+Extraordinary+Leader) by John Zenger, Joseph Folkman

* [Simple Habits for Complex Times](https://www.amazon.com/Simple-Habits-Complex-Times-Practices/dp/0804799431/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1517743225&sr=8-1&keywords=Simple+Habits+for+Complex+Times) \- Garvey Berger / Johnston (leadership practices navigating complexity)

* [Six Simple Rules: How to Manage Complexity without Getting Complicated](https://www.amazon.com/Six-Simple-Rules-Complexity-Complicated/dp/1422190552/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=6+simple+rules&qid=1583173468&sr=8-1) by Yves Morieux and Peter Tollman   [TED talk](https://www.ted.com/talks/yves_morieux_as_work_gets_more_complex_6_rules_to_simplify?language=en)

* [Leadership Without Easy Answers](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B002OEBO82/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_hsch_vapi_tkin_p1_i2) by Ronald A. Heifetz

* [Leadership Can Be Taught: A Bold Approach for a Complex World](https://www.amazon.com/Leadership-Can-Be-Taught-Approach/dp/1591393094/ref=pd_ybh_a_1?_encoding=UTF8&psc=1&refRID=ZN2W7CRKJ32K9JP694BS) by Sharon Daloz Parks (Heifetz disciple)

* [The Practice of Adaptive Leadership](https://www.amazon.com/Practice-Adaptive-Leadership-Changing-Organization/dp/1422105768/ref=sr_1_2?keywords=Ronald+Heifetz&qid=1556205837&s=gateway&sr=8-2) by Ronald Heifetz

* [Conscious Business: How to Build Value Through Values](https://www.amazon.com/Conscious-Business-Build-Through-Values-ebook/dp/B0034184XM/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=fred+kofman&qid=1564162254&s=gateway&sr=8-1) by Fred Kofman , Ken Wilber, et al.

* [The Meaning Revolution: The Power of Transcendent Leadership](https://www.amazon.com/Meaning-Revolution-Power-Transcendent-Leadership-ebook/dp/B073P9NQ4V/ref=sr_1_2?keywords=fred+kofman&qid=1564162254&s=gateway&sr=8-2) by Fred Kofman and Reid Hoffman

———————————————————

## **Female Leadership and Equality** {#female-leadership-and-equality}

* [The Next Generation of Women Leaders: What You Need to Lead but Won’t Learn in Business School](https://www.amazon.com/Next-Generation-Women-Leaders-Business-ebook/dp/B003C80QBA/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1534009015&sr=8-1&keywords=The+Next+Generation+of+Women+Leaders%3A+What+You+Need+to+Lead+but+Won%E2%80%99t+Learn+in+Business+School) By Selena Rezvani.    
  (annotated by [Barbara Safani](http://twitter.com/barbarasafani)) Rezvani interviews women executives in various industries, roles and job functions to uncover how women navigate the leadership maze. The book is a valuable resource with tools and information to help young women shape their careers and negotiate the workplace as a woman. Even though it’s geared toward women, many of the stories about finding mentors will resonate with men as well.

* [The Cyber Effect: An Expert in Cyberpsychology Explains How Technology Is Shaping Our Children, Our Behavior, and Our Values--and What We Can Do About It](https://www.amazon.com/Cyber-Effect-Cyberpsychology-Technology-Values/dp/0812987470/ref=asap_bc?ie=UTF8) by Mary Aiken, PhD.   
  CSI:Cyber the TV show is based on her

* [Reclaiming Conversation](https://www.amazon.com/Reclaiming-Conversation-Power-Talk-Digital/dp/0143109790/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1527525241&sr=1-1&keywords=sherry+turkle) by Sherry Turkle.   
  A flight from conversation undermines our relationships, creativity, and productivity—and why reclaiming face-to-face conversation can help us regain lost ground.

* [Weapons of Math Destruction: How Big Data Increases Inequality and Threatens Democracy](https://www.amazon.com/Weapons-Math-Destruction-Increases-Inequality/dp/0553418831/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1527525268&sr=1-1&keywords=weapons+of+math+destruction+cathy+o%27neil) by Cathy O'Neil.   
  By tracking how algorithms shape people's lives at every stage, O'Neil makes a compelling case that our bot overlords are using data to discriminate unfairly and foreclose democratic choices. If you work with data, or just produce reams of it online, this is a must-read.

———————————————————

## **Managing** {#managing}

* [The Manager's Path: A Guide for Tech Leaders Navigating Growth and Change](https://www.amazon.com/Managers-Path-Leaders-Navigating-Growth/dp/1491973897/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1519115869&sr=8-1&keywords=%22The+Manager%27s+Path%22+by+Camlile+Fournier..direct/es) by Camille Fournier  

* [Debugging Teams: Better Productivity through Collaboration](https://www.amazon.com/Debugging-Teams-Productivity-through-Collaboration/dp/1491932058/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1519116009&sr=8-1&keywords=Brian+W.+Fitzpatrick) by Brian W. Fitzpatrick and Ben Collins-Sussman  
  ([free version](https://bit.ly/v-books))

* [Google’s Project Oxygen: Do Manager’s Matter?](https://store.hbr.org/product/google-s-project-oxygen-do-managers-matter/313110?sku=313110-PDF-ENG)

* [High Output Management](https://www.amazon.com/High-Output-Management-Andrew-Grove/dp/0679762884/ref=sr_1_2?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1518215877&sr=1-2&keywords=High+Output+Management+by+Andrew+Grove) by Andrew Grove

* [Radical Candor](https://www.amazon.com/Radical-Candor-KIM-SCOTT/dp/1509845364/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1519116068&sr=8-1&keywords=radical+candor) by Kim Scott   Care personally, challenge directly.  
  "Radical Candor is a simple idea: to be a good boss, you have to Care Personally at the same time that you Challenge Directly. When you challenge without caring it’s obnoxious aggression; when you care without challenging it’s ruinous empathy. When you do neither it’s manipulative insincerity. This simple framework can help you build better relationships at work, and fulfill your three key responsibilities as a leader: creating a culture of feedback (praise and criticism), building a cohesive team, and achieving results you’re all proud of."

* [Managing Humans](https://www.amazon.com/Managing-Humans-Humorous-Software-Engineering/dp/1484221575/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1520460100&sr=8-1&keywords=Managing+Humans+by+Michael+Lopp) by Michael Lopp  
  "Whether you're an aspiring manager, a current manager, or just wondering what the heck a manager does all day, there is a story in this book that will speak to you―and help you survive and prosper amid the general craziness of dysfunctional bright people caught up in the chase of riches and power. Scattered in repose among these manic misfits are managers, an even stranger breed of people who, through a mystical organizational ritual, have been given power over the futures and the bank accounts of many others."

* [An Everyone Culture](https://www.amazon.com/Everyone-Culture-Deliberately-Developmental-Organization/dp/1625278624/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1520460169&sr=8-1&keywords=An+Everyone+Culture+by+Robert+Kegan+%26+Lisa+Laskow+Lahey) by Robert Kegan & Lisa Laskow Lahey  
  "In most organizations nearly everyone is doing a second job no one is paying them for—namely, covering their weaknesses, trying to look their best, and managing other people’s impressions of them. There may be no greater waste of a company’s resources. The ultimate cost: neither the organization nor its people are able to realize their full potential.

* [The Situational Leader](https://www.amazon.com/Situational-Leader-Dr-Paul-Hersey/dp/0446513423/ref=cm_cr_arp_d_product_top?ie=UTF8) by Dr. Paul Hersey  
  The original book on [Situational Leadership](http://situational.com/the-cls-difference/situational-leadership-what-we-do/)

* [The New One Minute Manager](https://www.amazon.com/gp/slredirect/picassoRedirect.html/ref=pa_sp_atf_aps_sr_pg1_1?ie=UTF8&adId=A03466362WGXJYWP33KVE&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2FNew-One-Minute-Manager%2Fdp%2F0062367544%2Fref%3Dsr_1_1_sspa%3Fie%3DUTF8%26qid%3D1533945115%26sr%3D8-1-spons%26keywords%3DThe%2BNew%2BOne%2BMinute%2BManager%26psc%3D1&qualifier=1533945115&id=320764652163590&widgetName=sp_atf) by Kenneth H. Blanchard and Spencer Johnson  
  (annotated by [Geoffrey James](https://www.inc.com/geoffrey-james/the-12-leadership-books-every-boss-should-read.html)) This classic not only provides the basics of managing people, but emphasizes that it's not really all that complicated to get people to do what you need them to do.

* [First, Break All the Rules](https://www.amazon.com/First-Break-All-Rules-Differently/dp/1595621113/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533945133&sr=8-1&keywords=First%2C+Break+All+the+Rules) by Marcus Buckingham and Curt Coffman  
  (annotated by [Geoffrey James](https://www.inc.com/geoffrey-james/the-12-leadership-books-every-boss-should-read.html)) Based on an extensive study of managers in different companies, this book pretends to be iconoclastic (hence the title), but is actually a clear manifesto of what has now become standard management practice.

* [Good to Great: Why Some Companies Make the Leap and Others Don't](https://www.amazon.com/Good-Great-Some-Companies-Others/dp/0066620996/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533946189&sr=8-1&keywords=Good+to+Great) by Jim Collins   
  (annotated by [Joe Vennare](http://www.lifehack.org/articles/productivity/15-best-leadership-books-every-young-leader-needs-read.html)) Some companies succeed, but most fail. Jim Collins evaluated thousands of articles and interview transcripts to figure out why exactly that is. Then he packaged it all into this book to show you what traits you’ll need to build a great company. (annotated by [Geoffrey James](https://www.inc.com/geoffrey-james/the-12-leadership-books-every-boss-should-read.html)) Probably the best of the "case study" style of management book. While I often question whether case studies are applicable to real-life situations, Collins is a genius at finding commonalities that make successful companies more successful.

* [Conversational Intelligence: How Great Leaders Build Trust and Get Extraordinary Results](https://www.amazon.com/Conversational-Intelligence-Leaders-Extraordinary-Results-ebook/dp/B01M646LY7/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533946302&sr=8-1&keywords=Conversational+Intelligence%3A+How+Great+Leaders+Build+Trust+and+Get+Extraordinary+Results) by Judith Glaser  
  (annotated by [Janet Zaretsky](https://twitter.com/thezenithbiz)) Judith is a master of training great leaders to build trust. If you want your people to produce great results, you must have their trust. She has led numerous successful initiatives in companies where leadership was the key to altering the company’s future. This book gives practical tools to develop oneself in empowering conversations and developing our own and others leadership.

* [First 90 Days](https://www.amazon.com/First-Days-Updated-Expanded-Strategies-ebook/dp/B00B6U63ZE/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1520460071&sr=8-1&keywords=First+90+Days+by+Michael+D.+Watkins) by Michael D. Watkins  
  Offers proven strategies for conquering the challenges of transitions—no matter where you are in your career. Watkins, a noted expert on leadership transitions and adviser to senior leaders in all types of organizations, also addresses today’s increasingly demanding professional landscape, where managers face not only more frequent transitions but also steeper expectations once they step into their new jobs."

* [The Essential Drucker](https://www.amazon.com/Essential-Drucker-Druckers-Management-Essentials-ebook/dp/B000FC11LK/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Essential+Drucker&qid=1575167204&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Peter F. Drucker  
  (annotated by [Geoffrey James](https://www.inc.com/geoffrey-james/the-12-leadership-books-every-boss-should-read.html)) Almost everything that's been written about management since the middle of the 20th century is based in one way or another upon Drucker's work. Reading these excerpts gives you a solid understanding of this seminal thinker.

* [Management and Machiavelli](https://www.amazon.com/Management-Machiavelli-Antony-Jay/dp/0553206591/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Antony+Jay&qid=1575167343&s=books&sr=1-1) by Antony Jay  
  (annotated by [Geoffrey James](https://www.inc.com/geoffrey-james/the-12-leadership-books-every-boss-should-read.html)) This "classic that you've never heard of" reframes corporate behavior in terms of medieval politics. While the book was written before the PC revolution and many of its corporate stories are hoary, there's a universality to the way Jay presents his arguments that's eye-opening. He later co-authored two classics of political humor, Yes, Minister and Yes, Prime Minister.

* [The No Asshole Rule](https://www.amazon.com/Asshole-Rule-Civilized-Workplace-Surviving/dp/0446698202/ref=sr_1_2?keywords=The+No+Asshole+Rule&qid=1575167371&s=books&sr=1-2) by Robert I. Sutton  
  (annotated by [Geoffrey James](https://www.inc.com/geoffrey-james/the-12-leadership-books-every-boss-should-read.html)) All too many bosses tolerate bullying and jerky behaviors, especially from their "star" performers. This book explains why jerks always create more problems than they're worth and suggests ways to either get rid of them or change their behaviors.

* [Crazy Bosses](https://www.amazon.com/Crazy-Bosses-Fully-Revised-Updated/dp/0060731575/ref=sr_1_2?keywords=crazy+bosses&qid=1575167399&s=books&sr=1-2) by Stanley Bing  
  (annotated by [Geoffrey James](https://www.inc.com/geoffrey-james/the-12-leadership-books-every-boss-should-read.html)) Not only is this book wildly entertaining, but after you've read it, you can truly say to yourself, "Well, I may not be the best boss in the world, but I'm certainly not as bad as these bozos."

* [Measure What Matters: How Google, Bono, and the Gates Foundation Rock the World with OKRs](https://www.amazon.com/gp/slredirect/picassoRedirect.html/ref=pa_sp_mtf_digital-text_sr_pg1_2?ie=UTF8&adId=A03180873DWD66PC5JSR4&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2FMeasure-What-Matters-Google-Foundation%2Fdp%2F0525536221%2Fref%3Dsr_1_6_sspa%3Fs%3Ddigital-text%26ie%3DUTF8%26qid%3D1534037269%26sr%3D1-6-spons%26keywords%3Dharvard%2Bbusiness%2Breview%2Bbuilding%2BTeams%26psc%3D1&qualifier=1534037270&id=1941661246425871&widgetName=sp_mtf) by John Doerr and Larry Page

* [Developing Management Skills](https://www.amazon.com/Developing-Management-Skills-David-Whetten/dp/0136121004/ref=pd_cp_14_1/134-5932411-3709530?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=0136121004&pd_rd_r=c4cd4ed1-1281-4de5-8e3d-8a648377f3e9&pd_rd_w=ZUx6z&pd_rd_wg=W3qIX&pf_rd_p=0e5324e1-c848-4872-bbd5-5be6baedf80e&pf_rd_r=4G6JYZYJW4EPT5YW1JFT&psc=1&refRID=4G6JYZYJW4EPT5YW1JFT) (8th Edition) by David A. Whetten, Kim S. Cameron

* [Managing Up: How to Move up, Win at Work, and Succeed with Any Type of Boss](https://tinyurl.com/y5vauw5j) by Mary Abbajay

## **Culture**  {#culture}

* ## [**Organizational Culture and Leadership**](https://www.amazon.com/Organizational-Leadership-Jossey-Bass-Business-Management/dp/1119212049/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1526235057&sr=8-2&keywords=schein+edgar) **by Edgar H. Schein, Peter Schein** 

* [The Culture Code: The Secrets of Highly Successful Groups](https://www.amazon.com/Culture-Code-Secrets-Highly-Successful/dp/0804176981/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1526234895&sr=8-1&keywords=culture+code) by Daniel Coyle 

* [The Advantage: Why Organizational Health Trumps Everything Else In Business](https://www.amazon.com/Advantage-Organizational-Health-Everything-Business/dp/0470941529/ref=pd_bxgy_14_2?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=0470941529&pd_rd_r=46SF2RF4Y06QT98WMT99&pd_rd_w=YwOX9&pd_rd_wg=mJXAn&psc=1&refRID=46SF2RF4Y06QT98WMT99) by Patrick M. Lencioni

* Article: [Lessons from 7 highly successful companies](https://techbeacon.com/lessons-7-highly-successful-software-engineering-cultures) ([pocket](https://getpocket.com/a/read/1586138233))
