## **Teams** {#teams}

### Well Regarded {#well-regarded}

* [Committed Teams: Three Steps to Inspiring Passion and Performance](https://www.amazon.com/Committed-Teams-Inspiring-Passion-Performance/dp/1119157404/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1539188130&sr=8-1&keywords=Committed+Teams) by Mario Moussa, Madeline Boyer, Derek Newberry

* [Creating Effective Teams: A Guide for Members and Leaders](https://www.amazon.com/dp/1483346129/?ref=idea_lv_dp_ov_d) by Susan A. Wheelan 

* [Team of Teams: New Rules of Engagement for a Complex World](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1591847486/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_bibl_vppi_i0) by Gen. Stanley McChrystal

* [The Five Dysfunctions of a Team: A Leadership Fable](https://www.amazon.com/Five-Dysfunctions-Team-Large-Print/dp/0470580461/ref=as_li_ss_tl?_encoding=UTF8&me=&linkCode=sl1&tag=takefl0d7-20&linkId=4e5347b7093a97298ec53a402c2a0beb) by Patrick Lencioni

* [Total Leadership: Be a Better Leader, Have a Richer Life](https://www.amazon.com/Total-Leadership-Better-Leader-Richer-ebook/dp/B001E95JD4/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1530304859&sr=8-2&keywords=total+leadership) by Stewart D. Friedman 

* [The 17 Indisputable Laws of Teamwork: Embrace Them and Empower Your Team](http://amzn.to/2swJ3nb) by John Maxwell 

* [A Team of Leaders: Empowering Every Member to Take Ownership, Demonstrate Initiative, and Deliver Results](http://amzn.to/2rdy1PY) by Paul Gustavson and Stewart Liff

* [The Culture Code: The Secrets of Highly Successful Groups](https://www.amazon.com/Culture-Code-Secrets-Highly-Successful/dp/0804176981/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1523629679&sr=8-1&keywords=culture+code) by Daniel Coyle   

* [Great at Work: How Top Performers Do Less, Work Better, and Achieve More](https://www.amazon.com/Great-Work-Performers-Better-Achieve/dp/1476765626/ref=pd_sim_14_3?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=1476765626&pd_rd_r=XX5M6NYZYTC5TYDZESRQ&pd_rd_w=xrPSZ&pd_rd_wg=VkDpR&psc=1&refRID=XX5M6NYZYTC5TYDZESRQ) by Morten Hansen

* [Powerful: Building a Culture of Freedom and Responsibility](https://www.amazon.com/Powerful-Building-Culture-Freedom-Responsibility/dp/1939714095/ref=pd_sim_14_5?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=1939714095&pd_rd_r=XX5M6NYZYTC5TYDZESRQ&pd_rd_w=xrPSZ&pd_rd_wg=VkDpR&psc=1&refRID=XX5M6NYZYTC5TYDZESRQ) by Patty McCord

* [Global Teams: How the best teams achieve high performance](https://www.amazon.co.uk/Global-Teams-teams-achieve-performance/dp/129217191X) by Jo Owen teams

* [When: The Scientific Secrets of Perfect Timing](https://www.amazon.com/When-Scientific-Secrets-Perfect-Timing/dp/0735210624/ref=pd_sim_14_2?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=0735210624&pd_rd_r=XX5M6NYZYTC5TYDZESRQ&pd_rd_w=xrPSZ&pd_rd_wg=VkDpR&psc=1&refRID=XX5M6NYZYTC5TYDZESRQ) by Daniel H. Pink

* [The Little Book of Talent: 52 Tips for Improving Your Skills](https://www.amazon.com/Little-Book-Talent-Improving-Skills/dp/034553025X/ref=pd_sim_14_4?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=034553025X&pd_rd_r=XX5M6NYZYTC5TYDZESRQ&pd_rd_w=xrPSZ&pd_rd_wg=VkDpR&psc=1&refRID=XX5M6NYZYTC5TYDZESRQ) by Daniel Coyle

* [Radical Inclusion: What the Post-9/11 World Should Have Taught Us About Leadership](https://www.amazon.com/Radical-Inclusion-Post-9-Should-Leadership-ebook/dp/B0798WBH53/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1523750943&sr=8-1&keywords=Radical+Inclusion%3A+What+the) by Martin Dempsey

* [The Motivation Myth: How High Achievers Really Set Themselves Up to Win](https://www.amazon.com/Motivation-Myth-Achievers-Really-Themselves-ebook/dp/B06ZYFR2CL/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1523750922&sr=8-1&keywords=The+Motivation+Myth%3A+How+High+Achievers+Really+Set) by Jeff Haden

* [Debugging Teams: Better Productivity through Collaboration](https://www.amazon.com/Debugging-Teams-Productivity-through-Collaboration/dp/1491932058/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1523906940&sr=8-1&keywords=debugging+teams) by Brian W. Fitzpatrick and Ben Collins-Sussman

* [The Manager's Path: A Guide for Tech Leaders Navigating Growth and Change](https://www.amazon.com/Managers-Path-Leaders-Navigating-Growth/dp/1491973897/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1523906940&sr=8-2&keywords=debugging+teams) by Camille Fournier

* [Start With Why: How Great Leaders Inspire Everyone to Take Action](https://www.amazon.com/Start-Why-Leaders-Inspire-Everyone-ebook/dp/B002Q6XUE4/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1533945387&sr=8-2&keywords=Start+With+Why+by+Simon+Sinek) by Simon Sinek.  
  Providing reasons for people to do what you'd like them to do.

* [The Four Toxins](https://www.beyondtheleadingedge.com/news/teams/the-four-team-toxins/) ([personal copy](https://getpocket.com/a/read/426866822)) 

### Recommended {#recommended}

By [Ready to Manage](http://blog.readytomanage.com/top-20-books-on-teams-and-teamwork/) (with annotations)

* [The Advantage: Why Organizational Health Trumps Everything Else In Business](https://www.amazon.com/Advantage-Organizational-Health-Everything-Business/dp/B007MIWCAY/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1534037161&sr=1-1&keywords=The+Advantage%3A+Why+Organizational+Health+Trumps+Everything+Else+In+Business) by Patrick Lencioni, 2012

* [Team Turnarounds: A Playbook for Transforming Underperforming Teams by Joe Frontiera](https://www.amazon.com/Team-Turnarounds-Playbook-Transforming-Underperforming-ebook/dp/B008K9AHHE/ref=sr_1_1?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1534037180&sr=1-1&keywords=Team+Turnarounds%3A+A+Playbook+for+Transforming+Underperforming+Teams%2C+by+Joe+Frontiera), Daniel Leidl, Jim Kouzes and Barry Posner, 2012

* [Help the Helper: Building a Culture of Extreme Teamwork](https://www.amazon.com/Help-Helper-Building-Culture-Teamwork-ebook/dp/B007X5ZVTK/ref=sr_1_1?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1534037197&sr=1-1&keywords=Help+the+Helper%3A+Building+a+Culture+of+Extreme+Teamwork) by Kevin Pritchard and John Eliot, 2012

* [Harvard Business Review on Building Better Teams](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1422162346/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=1422162346&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by Bob Frisch, 2011

* [Leading Project Teams: The Basics of Project Management and Team Leadership](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1412991706/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=1412991706&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by Anthony T. Cobb, 2011

* [Building Team Power: How to Unleash the Collaborative Genius of Teams for Increased Engagement, Productivity, and Results](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0071746749/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=0071746749&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by Thomas Kayser, 2010

* [Clear Leadership: Sustaining Real Collaboration and Partnership at Work](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/089106382X/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=089106382X&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by Gervase Bushe

* [Teamwork and Teamplay](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0787245321/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=0787245321&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by James Cain and Barry Jolliff, 2010

* [Leading Global Project Teams: The New Leadership Challenge](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1554890640/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=1554890640&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by Russ J. Martinelli, Tim J. Rahschulte and James M. Waddell, 2010

* [Virtual Team Success: A Practical Guide for Working and Leading from a Distance](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0470532963/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=0470532963&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by Richard Lepsinger and Darleen DeRosa, 2010

* [Leading with Emotional Intelligence: Hands-On Strategies for Building Confident and Collaborative Star Performers](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0071750959/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=0071750959&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by Reldan S. Nadler, 2010

* [Group Dynamics for Teams](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1412977622/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=1412977622&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by Daniel Levi, 2010

* [The Discipline of Teams (Harvard Business Review Classics)](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1422179753/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=1422179753&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by Jon R. Katzenbach and Douglas Smith, 2009

* [Teamwork 101: What Every Leader Needs to Know](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1400280257/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=1400280257&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by John Maxwell, 2009

* [Extraordinary Groups: How Ordinary Teams Achieve Amazing Results](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0470404817/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=0470404817&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by Geoffrey M. Bellman and Kathleen D. Ryan, 2009

* [Great Business Teams: Cracking the Code for Standout Performance](http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0470122439/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=0470122439&linkCode=as2&tag=reainc0a-20) by Howard M. Guttman, 2008

* HBR’s [On Strategy](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1zAKX43JxM1wl1tMfy9NdaIpscRvAAoCFzoxK4V_0x-s/edit#bookmark=kix.nji1b3gfopok) 

* [Good Strategy / Bad Strategy](https://www.amazon.com/Good-Strategy-Bad-Difference-Matters-ebook/dp/B004J4WKEC/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1520460138&sr=8-1&keywords=Good+Strategy+%2F+Bad+Strategy+by+Richard+Rumelt) by Richard Rumelt  
  "Developing and implementing a strategy is the central task of a leader, whether the CEO at a Fortune 100 company, an entrepreneur, a church pastor, the head of a school, or a government official. Richard Rumelt shows that there has been a growing and unfortunate tendency to equate Mom-and-apple-pie values, fluffy packages of buzzwords, motivational slogans, and financial goals with “strategy.” He debunks these elements of “bad strategy” and awakens an understanding of the power of a “good strategy.” 

* [Thinking in New Boxes: A New Paradigm for Business Creativity](https://www.amazon.com/Thinking-New-Boxes-Paradigm-Creativity-ebook/dp/B00BVJG4WM/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=thinking+in+boxes&qid=1559843637&s=gateway&sr=8-1) by Luc De Brabandere and Alan Iny 

* [Your Strategy Needs a Strategy: How to Choose and Execute the Right Approach](https://www.amazon.com/Your-Strategy-Needs-Execute-Approach/dp/1531836216) by Martin Reeves

## **Organizational Development** {#organizational-development}

**OD Papers**

* [The BART System](https://drive.google.com/open?id=1jqMb8M-Rj-wgumUXy8r5FUTNniw7S8Qu) by Zachary Gabriel Green and René J. Molenkamp 

* [White Women at Work](https://drive.google.com/open?id=1RWZQ3XBtwXXGWPkTARN5jXOWAPLX0Bbg) by Sarah Brazaitis

* [X-Ray Vision at Work: Seeing Inside Organizational Life](https://drive.google.com/open?id=1kNPO7fcMBMMPPcqhAPtmIuIqDszeGrOZ). D.A. Noumair, D.L. Pfaff, C.M. St. John, A.N Gipson, Sarah Brazaitis.

**Process Consultancy**

* [Process Consultation Revisited](https://www.amazon.com/Process-Consultation-Revisited-Relationship-Organizational/dp/020134596X/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1539014829&sr=8-1&keywords=Process+Consultation+Revisited) by Edgar Schein ([book review](https://www.dropbox.com/s/j3r5akqfu19k60x/Edgar%20Schein%20-%20Process%20Consultation%20overview.pdf?dl=0))

* [The  concept of “client” from a process consultation perspective](https://www.dropbox.com/s/sp3u8a631bghmby/The%20Concept%20of%20%E2%80%9CClient%E2%80%9D%20from%20a%20Process%20Consultation%20Perspective.pdf?dl=0) by Edgar Schein

* [Intervention Skills: Process Consultation for Small Groups and Teams](https://www.amazon.com/Intervention-Skills-Process-Consultation-Groups-ebook/dp/B0014EST3Q/ref=sr_1_3?keywords=intervention+skills&qid=1560457854&s=gateway&sr=8-3) by W. Brendan Reddy 

**Books**

* [Dialogic Organizational Development: the theory and practice of transformational change](https://www.amazon.com/Dialogic-Organization-Development-Practice-Transformational-ebook/dp/B00SGET4AO/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1527623605&sr=8-1&keywords=Dialogic+Organizational+Development) by Bushe and Marshak  
  * Purpose of intervention is not to solve problems but to equip system members to learn what they need to do and learn to continuously use those processes for self-renewal and continuous adaptation for the future.  
  * With complexity/chaos theory, the goal is to increase the system’s capacity to self-organize, and evolve ability to break out of social/cultural/psychologic/paradigm constraints to participate in continuous dev 

* [Organization Development](https://www.amazon.com/dp/0134818350/?ref=idea_lv_dp_ov_d) by W. Warner Burke and Debra A. Noumair 

* [Covert Processes at Work : Managing the Five Hidden Dimensions of Organizational Change](https://www.amazon.com/Covert-Processes-Work-Dimensions-Organizational/dp/1576754154/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1538411271&sr=1-1&keywords=covert+processes+at+work) by Robert J. Marshak

* [Organizational Learning: A Theory of Action Perspective](https://www.amazon.com/Organizational-Learning-Addison-Wesley-Organization-Development/dp/0201001748/ref=sr_1_1?crid=1EOKYNZERFM6Z&keywords=theory+of+action+perspective&qid=1576418361&sprefix=10%25%2Caps%2C156&sr=8-1) by Chris Argyris and Donald A. Schon

Institute of Organizational Development recommendations [blog](https://instituteod.com/iod-blog/)

* [Handbook for Strategic HR: Best Practices in Organization Development from the OD Network](http://www.amazon.com/Handbook-Strategic-Practices-Organization-Development/dp/0814432492/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1425309034&sr=8-1&keywords=1.%09Handbook+for+Strategic+HR%3A+Best+Practices+in+Organization+Development+from+the+OD+Network+by+ODNetwork)  by John Vogelsang, Maya Townsend   
  This book is a collection of 78 articles from a variety of OD Professionals. The main reason for reading this book is that it helps the reader learn a greater role of the HR professional as OD consultants which involve strategy development, work design and cultural change. You can also get HRCI credit.

* [Best Practices in Organization Development and Change: Culture, Leadership, Retention, Performance Coaching](http://www.amazon.com/Best-Practices-Organization-Development-Change/dp/0470604557) by Louis Carter, David Giber, Marshall Goldsmith, Richard F. Beckhard, W. Warner Burke, Edward E. Lawler III, Beverly L. Kaye, Jay Alden Conger, John Sullivan  
  This book is a compilation of what the most effective OD techniques individuals and organizations are using to become successful. If you want to learn about how these companies are using OD, Leadership Development, Talent Management, and Coaching to up their game, then this book is for you.

* [Flawless Consulting: Your Guide to Getting Your Expertise Used](http://www.amazon.com/Flawless-Consulting-Guide-Getting-Expertise/dp/0470620749/ref=sr_1_fkmr0_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425309767&sr=1-1-fkmr0&keywords=3.+Flawless+Consulting%3A+Your+Guide+to+Getting+Your+Expertise+Used+%28Peter+Block%29%3A+Process+Consultation+Revisited) by Peter Block  
  This book guides us on how to navigate a complex and changing world by addressing the challenges surround us as OD professionals. It also helps us use questions and implement other OD tools more effectively so that we are able to get the results we are looking for.

* [Images of Organization](http://www.amazon.com/Images-Organization-Gareth-Morgan/dp/1412939798/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425309847&sr=1-1&keywords=4.+Images+of+Organization+%28Gareth+Morgan%29) by Gareth Morgan  
  This book helps us understand the complexity of organizations and enables us to use the theories to design better practices.

* [Organizational Culture and Leadership](http://www.amazon.com/Organizational-Culture-Leadership-Edgar-Schein/dp/0470190604/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425310047&sr=1-1&keywords=5.+Organizational+Culture+and+Leadership) by Edgar Schein   
  This book talks about how culture can be used to bring change within an organization. Culture is regarded as a tool which can help in achieving organizational goals.

* [Diagnosing and Changing Organizational Culture: Based on the Competing Values Framework by Kim S. Cameron, Robert E. Quinn](http://www.amazon.com/Diagnosing-Changing-Organizational-Culture-Competing/dp/0470650265/ref=sr_1_fkmr0_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425310119&sr=1-1-fkmr0&keywords=6.+Diagnosing+and+Changing+Organizational+Culture%3A+Changing+Conversations+in+Organizations%3A+A+Complexity+Approach+to+Change+%28Patricia+Shaw%29%3A)  
  This book talks about the culture of an organization and helps the reader understand how to change it through the process of diagnosing the culture, understanding it in detail and implementing the change process.

* [Changing Conversations in Organizations: A Complexity Approach to Change](http://www.amazon.com/Changing-Conversations-Organizations-Complexity-Emergence/dp/0415249147/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425310235&sr=1-1&keywords=Changing+Conversations+in+Organizations%3A+A+Complexity+Approach+to+Change+%28Patricia+Shaw%29) by Patricia Shaw  
  This book helps us understand that often the tools, methods and understanding of organizational change are difficult to implement because the situation keeps on unfolding in real-time. The book talks about the importance to keep understanding and deciphering what is happening with change and be comfortable with the uncertainty element of it. The author talks about bringing about change as a discovery process.

* [Managing to Collaborate: The Theory and Practice of Collaborative Advantage](http://www.amazon.com/Managing-Collaborate-Practice-Collaborative-Advantage/dp/0415339200/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425310321&sr=1-1&keywords=managing+to+collaborate) by Chris Huxham & Siv Vangen  
  Collaboration can have far-reaching impacts on one’s environment and day-to-day life. This book talks about the different aspects of collaboration and helps us as students of collaboration develop a deeper understanding of it.

* [Mindsight: The New Science of Personal Transformation](http://www.amazon.com/Mindsight-New-Science-Personal-Transformation/dp/0553386395/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425309962&sr=1-1&keywords=mindsight) by Daniel Siegel, M.D.   
  This book helps us overcome our mental barriers and accomplish more. It is a good read for helping you reach your potential.

* [Organization Development & Change](http://www.amazon.com/Organization-Development-Change-Thomas-Cummings/dp/1133190456/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425310378&sr=1-1&keywords=10.+Organization+Development+%26+Change) by Thomas G. Cummings & Christopher Worley  
  This book discusses who behavioral science impacts organizational practices. It provides a very good theoretical basis for understanding how behavioral science works in this way.

* [Community: The Structure of Belonging by Peter Block](http://www.amazon.com/Community-Structure-Belonging-Peter-Block/dp/1605092770/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425310425&sr=1-1&keywords=community+and+the+structure+of+belonging)  
  This book helps us determine what healthy communities look like and how people can save their communities from fragmentation. A good read for developing a better world around us.

* [NTL Handbook of Organization Development and Change: Principles, Practices, and Perspectives](http://www.amazon.com/NTL-Handbook-Organization-Development-Change/dp/1118485815/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425310527&sr=1-1&keywords=13.+NTL+Handbook+of+Organization+Development+and+Change%3A) by Brenda B. Jones    
  A recently published book which contains contributions on many authors on how organization change is all about and how we should bring about change in a complex environment. Noted for its relevance to the current times.

* [The Fifth Discipline Fieldbook: Strategies and Tools for Building a Learning Organization](http://www.amazon.com/Fifth-Discipline-Fieldbook-Strategies-Organization/dp/0385472560/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425310580&sr=1-1&keywords=fieldbook+fifth+discipline) by Peter Senge  
  Learn how to develop your own learning organization in a systematic, step-wise manner.

* [The Change Champion’s Field Guide: Strategies and Tools for Leading Change in Your Organization](http://www.amazon.com/Change-Champions-Field-Guide-Organization/dp/1118136268/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1425310660&sr=1-1&keywords=The+Change+Champion%27s+Field+Guide%3A+Strategies+and+Tools+for+Leading+Change+in+Your+Organization+by+Louis+Carter+and+Roland+L.+Sullivan) by Louis Carter and Roland L. Sullivan  
  Gain tools and strategies to become an effective change leader. The focus is on helping bring about positive change where people are satisfied with the process and outcome of change. This is a collection of a variety of contributions from noted authors in the field of HR and OD.

* [Helping: How to Offer, Give, and Receive Help Paperback](http://www.amazon.com/Helping-Offer-Give-Receive-Help/dp/1605098566/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1425350434&sr=8-1&keywords=helping) by Edgar H. Schein  
  We all imagine helping to be a simple process of offering help. In fact, it is much more than that. This book guides you on how to build a helping relationship so that all the stakeholders in this process are able to have a more productive exchange.

* [Organization Development: A Practitioner's Guide for OD and HR](https://www.amazon.com/Organization-Development-Practitioners-Guide-OD/dp/0749470178/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1524159510&sr=8-1&keywords=Organization+Development%3A+A+Practitioner%27s+Guide+for+OD+and+HR) by Mee-Yan Cheung-Judge and Linda Holbeche

## **Intentionality and Acceptance** {#intentionality-and-acceptance}

**Intentionality**

* [The Power of Intention: Learning to Co-create Your World Your Way](https://www.amazon.com/Power-Intention-Learning-Co-create-World-ebook/dp/B000SEIJ6A/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=%E2%80%9CThe+Power+of+Intention%E2%80%9D+by&qid=1590711177&sr=8-1) by Wayne W. Dyer  
* [Authentic Leadership: Rediscovering the Secrets to Creating Lasting Value](https://www.amazon.com/Authentic-Leadership-Rediscovering-Secrets-Creating/dp/0787975281/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1517780248&sr=8-1&keywords=Authentic+Leadership%3A+Rediscovering+the+Secrets+to+Creating+Lasting+Value) by Bill George ([HBR paper)](https://drive.google.com/open?id=1Cbe3IKHM7KeZ_1olVGF3mDVi7mqJpFxN)

* [*Emotional Agility: Get Unstuck, Embrace Change, and Thrive in Work and Life*](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B016JPTPDW/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_hsch_vapi_tkin_p1_i0) by Susan David  
  The result of 20 years of research by Dr Susan David, a psychologist on the faculty of Harvard Medical School. She argues that learning to navigate our inner world (things like our thoughts and feelings) is the key to thriving in work and life. (list and review from [here](https://www.simplyfiercely.com/intentional-living-books/)). I discovered this book after watching her [TED talk about emotional courage](https://www.ted.com/talks/susan_david_the_gift_and_power_of_emotional_courage?language=en) and since then, I refer to it constantly for inspiration, guidance and practical advice.  If you want to embrace intentional living in 2020, then this is my top recommendation—a must-read for anyone who wants to live true to their self\! 

* [*Chasing Slow*](https://www.amazon.com/Chasing-Slow-Courage-Journey-Beaten/dp/0310345677/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=Chasing+Slow+by+Erin+Loechner&qid=1593956465&s=books&sr=1-1) by Erin Loechner  
  After rising to what some would consider the epitome of success in life before the age of 30, Erin found that despite her accomplishments, she felt lost. In *Chasing Slow*, she takes you on her journey of intense struggle from her husband’s brain tumour to bankruptcy and a public judgement. All of which led her to discover what really matters and makes a difference in life. If you’re looking to [slow down](https://www.simplyfiercely.com/slow-down-a-busy-day/) and [simplify your life](https://www.simplyfiercely.com/simplify-your-life/), this isn’t a step-by-step guide—but it is an inspiration. Read this if you’re looking for a personal story that will challenge your perspective. 

* [*When Less Becomes More*](https://www.amazon.com/When-Less-Becomes-More-Making/dp/140021128X/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=When+Less+Becomes+More+by+Emily+Ley&qid=1593956439&s=books&sr=1-1) by Emily Ley  
  *When Less Becomes More* presents the idea that we have more good in our lives when we let go of what doesn’t fulfil us. Emily guides her readers through discovering what “more” means for them—an essential but often overlooked question\!  I haven’t had a chance to read this yet but it’s been highly recommended to me by another mum with young children.

* [*Everything is Figureoutable*](https://www.amazon.com/Everything-Figureoutable-Marie-Forleo/dp/0525534997/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=Everything+is+Figureoutable+by+Marie+Forleo&qid=1593956406&s=books&sr=1-1) by Marie Forleo  
  If you don’t know where to begin with your big goals and dreams, then this is the book for you. Marie (who you probably know from [Marie TV](https://www.marieforleo.com/marietv/)) has put together an inspiring and practical step-by-step guide that will show you how everything really is “figureoutable”. It’s a perfect balance of entertainment, inspiration and practical advice. Highly recommended for anyone who needs a motivation boost\!

* [Present Over Perfect](https://www.amazon.com/Present-Over-Perfect-Leaving-Frantic/dp/0310342996/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=Present+Over+Perfect+by+Shauna+Niequist&qid=1593956422&s=books&sr=1-1) by Shauna Niequist  
  I’ve always believed that perfectionism is a natural enemy of simple and intentional living—which is why Iove this book. Shauna shares personal stories of her own transformation and encourages you to face the world as your most authentic self. If you struggle with the need to find perfection in life, this book will inspire you to separate the things you “should do” from the things that matter most.

* [Simply Tuesday](https://www.amazon.com/Simply-Tuesday-Emily-P-Freeman-audiobook/dp/B013FA6W30/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=Simply+Tuesday+by+Emily+P.+Freeman&qid=1593956344&s=audible&sr=1-1) by Emily P. Freeman  
  In her book, Simply Tuesday, Emily presents a series of essays exploring how to be present in today’s fast-paced world. Despite the expectations and outside pressures that are alive and abundant in our culture, she suggests that “real life happens in the small moments, the kind we find on Tuesdays.” This idea really resonates with me because I believe that intentional living is less about big, sweeping changes and more about the small things we do every day. If you’re looking for an invitation to step back and appreciate the little things, then give this book a try.

* [Essentialism: The Disciplined Pursuit of Less](https://www.amazon.com/Essentialism-Greg-McKeown-audiobook/dp/B00IWYP5NI/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=Essentialism%3A+The+Disciplined+Pursuit+of+Less+by+Greg+McKeown&qid=1593956326&s=books&sr=1-1) by Greg McKeown  
  Essentialism is a wonderful guide on how to live an intentional life. The author reminds us that everything is a choice and every choice has trade-offs. So many important lessons on choosing the “essential” over the non-essential. Note that this book is slightly more “business-y” than the others on the list but I still highly recommend it for everyone. The core concepts can be applied to all areas of your life, even if you’re not working in a corporate environment.

* [The Joy of Missing Out](https://www.amazon.com/Joy-Missing-Out-Live-Doing/dp/1400214335/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=The+Joy+of+Missing+Out+by+Tonya+Dalton&qid=1593956302&s=books&sr=1-1) by Tonya Dalton  
  Tonya Dalton is a productivity expert and CEO of her own company which focuses on helping women be more productive. In her book, she teaches you how to reject the social pressure to do it all and instead, figure out what to say yes to and how to create a system that’s best for you to handle it. Read this if you are looking for practical and applicable advice about setting priorities.

* [The Happiness Project](https://www.amazon.com/Happiness-Project-Tenth-Anniversary-Aristotle/dp/0062888749/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=The+Happiness+Project+by+Gretchen+Rubin&qid=1593956282&s=books&sr=1-1) by Gretchen Rubin  
  The Happiness Project was written after the author had a sudden realization that life goes by quickly and we often spend our days just trying to get by. She dedicated an entire year to true intentionality in a search for the things that brought happiness to her life. As silly as this might sound now, at the time it was a shock to realise how much control I had over my own joy.

* [The Art of Making Memories](https://www.amazon.com/Art-Making-Memories-Happiness-Institute/dp/0062943383/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&keywords=The+Art+of+Making+Memories&qid=1593956260&s=books&sr=1-1) by Miek Wiking  
  They say the only thing we’ll leave this life with is our memories but how often are we intentional about making ones we can cherish? Wiking writes all about how having positive memories serves us in life and can bring us more joy. The book contains plenty of data-rich info and stories on how to be intentional about making memories that will last a lifetime\!

* [The Millionaire Next Door by Thomas J. Stanley](https://www.amazon.ca/Millionaire-Next-Door-Surprising-Americas/dp/1589795474/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&keywords=millionaire+next+door&qid=1522857812&s=books&sr=1-1)  
  Do you feel pressure to buy the latest smartphone, level up your wardrobe, or lease a fancier car? This book is for you. Thomas shows you that most millionaires in the US aren’t driving fancy cars, living in mansions, or even working glamorous jobs. This book demonstrates, through several interviews with actual millionaires, that it’s entirely possible for average-wage earners to become millionaires as long as they exhibit patience and discipline. There’s no secret sauce to these millionaires’ accumulation of wealth — just plain ol’ hard work and frugal living. As Thomas writes in his book, “After twenty years of studying millionaires across a wide spectrum of industries, we have concluded that the character of the business owner is more important in predicting his level of wealth than the classification of his business.” (list and reviews from [here](https://medium.com/@jennifertchan/9-must-read-books-for-anyone-who-wants-to-start-living-an-intentional-life-e032e313555f))

* [The Obstacle is the Way by Ryan Holiday](https://www.amazon.ca/Obstacle-Way-Timeless-Turning-Triumph-ebook/dp/B00G3L1B8K/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&keywords=obstacle+is+the+way&qid=1522857768&s=books&sr=1-1)  
  Former Marketing Director of American Apparel, Ryan Holiday, has made stoicism fresh and relevant again. In this book, Ryan applies the timeless principles of stoicism through using historic examples of the most successful people in history confronting the biggest challenges of their lives. From John D. Rockefeller to Winston Churchill, Ryan discusses how these courageous leaders turned their obstacles into opportunities. This book is perfect for anyone stuck in a rut or facing a difficult situation.

* [The Year of Magical Thinking by Joan Didion](https://www.amazon.ca/Year-Magical-Thinking-Joan-Didion/dp/1400078431/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&keywords=joan+didion&qid=1522857754&s=books&sr=1-1)  
  Part and parcel of living a successful life is dealing with tragedy. In reading this memoir, you can actively see Joan analyzing her grief and attempting to explain away her pain. It’s a simultaneously easy and difficult read — easy in terms of readability and difficult in terms of the impact it leaves with you. If/when you experience the loss of a loved one and are looking to hear from someone who has gone through the same, pick up this book. She has the ability to put into words what you cannot.

* [Originals: How Non-Conformists Move the World by Adam Grant](https://www.amazon.ca/Originals-How-Non-Conformists-Move-World-ebook/dp/B00XIYGCDO/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&keywords=originals&qid=1522857739&s=books&sr=1-1)  
  The premise of this book is simple: Non-conformists aren’t risk-tasking superheroes — they are people who pumped out a lot of average-quality work and actually made risk-adverse decisions before producing superior work that really moved the needle. Early on in the book, Grant uses the example of Warby Parker: He mentions that he had the opportunity to become an early investor in the company but declined because the founders seemed reluctant to drop-out of school and commit to growing Warby Parker full-time. Grant assumed that they would never be successful, so long as Warby Parker wasn’t the entire priority of the founders. Well, he ended up being wrong. The company is now valued at over $1 billion. What was the secret? Working smarter, not necessarily harder and being deliberate every step of the way. This book is great for anyone who wants to pursue entrepreneurship but feels like that they must risk everything in order to be successful.


* [Deep Work: Rules for Success in a Distracted World by Cal Newport](https://www.amazon.ca/Deep-Work-Focused-Success-Distracted-ebook/dp/B00X47ZVXM/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&keywords=cal+newport&qid=1522857723&s=books&sr=1-1)  
  This book is full of concrete tactics to remove the distractions that are preventing you from accomplishing the cognitive-demanding tasks that are required of us. I won’t ruin the entire book, because I think it’s worth a complete read, but one tactic he suggests is to, ‘work deeply.’ There are four strategies that we can use to accomplish this: monastic (isolate yourself for long periods of time), bimodal (set aside a few consecutive days where you’ll be working like a monastic), rhythmic (work three to four hours each day on a single task), and journalistic (alternate your day between deep and shallow work). This is just the tip of the iceberg, but you can see how practical Cal’s suggestions truly are. I encourage anyone who considers themself an information worker to pick this up.

* [Grit: The Power of Passion and Perseverance by Angela Duckworth](https://www.amazon.ca/Grit-Angela-Duckworth/dp/1443442313/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&keywords=angela+duckworth&qid=1522857708&s=books&sr=1-1)  
  In this book, Angela Duckworth, a critically-acclaimed professor of psychology at the University of Pennsylvania, details how talent is hardly a guarantor of success. What really moves the needle is grit — the magical combination of passion and perseverance. It’s not necessarily how smart you are, but rather the willingness to finish what you started. Angela drives home the point that it doesn’t matter so much with what skills you’re born with, rather it’s the act of rising from setbacks and the undertaking of sustained action that is often difficult and pleasant that will enable you to achieve your goals. At its core, this book is about taking matters into your own hands and the significance of realizing your own agency.

* [Mastery by Robert Greene](https://www.amazon.ca/Mastery-Robert-Greene/dp/0670024961/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&keywords=mastery&qid=1522857693&s=books&sr=1-1)  
  “The conventional mind is passive — it consumes information and regurgitates it in familiar forms. The dimensional mind is active, transforming everything it digests into something new and original, creating instead of consuming.” This is just one of the many pieces of advice that is hidden in this book. Robert, a master in his own right of writing timeless books on strategy, is an inspiring yet intimidating writer. His words are blunt yet profound. His thoughts are straightforward but filled with wisdom. I would suggest Mastery to anyone who is serious about perfecting their craft. As Robert explains in his book, “In order to master a field, you must love the subject and feel a profound connection to it. Your interest must transcend the field itself and border on the religious.”

* [Thinking in Bets: Making Smarter Decisions When You Don’t Have all the Facts by Annie Duke](https://www.amazon.ca/Thinking-Bets-Making-Smarter-Decisions-ebook/dp/B074DG9LQF/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&keywords=thinking+in+bets&qid=1522857664&s=books&sr=1-1)  
  This is the newest book on the list. For those of you who are unfamiliar with the author, Annie is a former professional poker player and now teaches poker to professionals, provides consulting services to C-suite executives and Fortune 500 companies, as well as writes about effective decision-making. As a lawyer, I find her knowledge directly applicable to my work. Among the topics that she covers, my favourites include dealing with uncertainty, understanding probabilities, and divorcing our decision-making from the outcome itself.

* [But What if We’re Wrong? by Chuck Klosterman](https://www.amazon.ca/But-What-If-Were-Wrong/dp/0399184139/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&keywords=but+what+if+we%27re+wrong&qid=1522857633&s=books&sr=1-1)  
  What I love about Chuck is that he never ceases to surprise me. For those that have been following his career over the decades (decades\!), he’s evolved a lot as both a writer and critical thinker since Fargo Rock City. Although he’s primarily a pop culture critic, he’s always willing to dip his toe outside of rock music and collegiate sports and share his unconventional views on conventional topics (i.e. gravity). This book lends us some perspective that in a hundred years from now people are probably going to look at us and laugh at how truly wrong our assumptions about the world are. I don’t try to hide my affinity for Chuck. I encourage you to read his writing for no other reason than he is a colourful writer that somehow challenges you to think twice about things.


* [Organizing from the Inside Out by Julie Morgenstern](https://www.amazon.com/Organizing-Inside-Out-Second-Foolproof/dp/0805075895/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=upjourney-20&linkId=165c8c3a1c210c14a1f385574b676faf&language=en_US)  
  I consider this book the bible of organizing. *Organizing from the Inside Out* provides a framework on how to view any organizing project and create a system that works. Julie’s S.P.A.C.E. technique – Sort, Purge, Assign a home, Containerize, Equalize – is simple and straightforward and doesn’t require a lot of fancy organizing products. The other key to *Organizing from the Inside Out* is the emphasis on the intuitive nature of effective organizing. So many times, I’ve been asked: *“Can you organize me?”* No, but I can help you get organized. For organizing to be sustainable, it has to be intuitive to you and you have to do the work. Living an intentional life works the same way – you create it day by day, choice by choice. (list and review from [here](https://upjourney.com/best-books-on-intentional-living))

* [Soulful Simplicity, How Living with Less Can Lead to So Much More by Courtney Carver](https://www.amazon.com/Soulful-Simplicity-Living-Less-Lead/dp/0143130684/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=upjourney-20&linkId=726fda6f903f2514ee477e1965869142&language=en_US)  
  I first became acquainted with Courtney when she spoke at a women’s conference and I could not wait to read her book. What impressed me the most was the authentic voice Courtney uses throughout, offering tips and suggestions, while never falling into a “this way or the highway” tone. This book outlines the joys of living with less and ways to get there that are doable and actionable for anyone who wants or needs a change. For anyone who has struggled with a cluttered wardrobe, Courtney is a godsend. She created Project 33 – keeping the 33 most essential items and creating an entire wardrobe around them – be sure to check it out.

* [The Five Second Rule, Transform Your Life, Work and Confidence with Everyday Courage by Mel Robbins](https://www.amazon.com/Second-Rule-Transform-Confidence-Everyday/dp/B06W9M3QDJ/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=upjourney-20&linkId=6ae99109788be18228012758572695e9&language=en_US)  
  One of the biggest stumbling blocks to living intentionally and mindfully is getting started and staying motivated. Mel’s book really delves into the roadblocks we put in our own way and how we can change our thinking and our actions. It’s really our thinking that drives what we do so she starts with that – how changing how we look at situations changes everything. Mel doesn’t paint a rose-colored glasses kind of world where change is easy but change must happen if you want different. If you don’t change, nothing changes.

* [Better than Before, Mastering the Habits of our Everyday Lives by Gretchen Rubin](https://www.amazon.com/Better-Than-Before-Mastering-Everyday/dp/0804188955/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=upjourney-20&linkId=8718cc1fc2cda24f284d630f9712d766&language=en_US)  
  Reading Gretchen is like catching up with a girlfriend over a cup of coffee or a glass of wine – authentic, funny, and down to earth. *Better than Before* focuses on the power of positive habits to create the life we want to live and see how we’ve been sabotaging ourselves. The book focuses on the little, everyday habits – exercising a little, eating just a bit healthier, sleeping just a bit longer – than feel doable. This isn’t about creating a training regime to run a marathon or create a 10 step plan to retire when you’re 35 – it’s about focusing on the small stuff that impacts us daily.

* [Outer Order, Inner Calm by Gretchen Rubin](https://www.amazon.com/Outer-Order-Inner-Calm/dp/147369373X/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=upjourney-20&linkId=d78f8ed5f0040bc3acf2eaa56aad9965&language=en_US)  
  Gretchen’s newest book – *Outer Order, Inner Calm* – is a hallelujah for organizers\! What’s going on outside in your life – how your office looks, what’s piling up in your car, how finding something to wear in your closet is like an archeological dig – reflects what’s going on with you mentally and spiritually. Everything in the universe has energy and the energy of disorganization and clutter is negative and loud. It’s difficult to make our best choices and live intentionally with all that noise and negativity.

* [The Charge: Activating the 10 Human Drives that Make You Feel Alive by Brendon Burchard](https://www.amazon.com/Charge-Brendon-Burchard/dp/1849837015/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=upjourney-20&linkId=f3c3b676c66d7d939d6a4a12dd2f9f86&language=en_US)  
  Are you looking for more motivation and direction in getting started in living an intentional life? If so, I highly recommend Brendon Burchard’s *The Charge: Activating the 10 Human Drives that Make You Feel Alive*. Brendon is a dynamic speaker and a powerful writer and *The Charge* is written in a really approachable way. In the book, he focuses on control, competence, congruence (living into your values), caring, connection, change, challenge, creative expression, contribution, consciousness, and celebration. Living a fully intentional life means being mindful of what doesn’t move you forward in life and by focusing on the drives, you create the life you want to live. Listen to this book if you can – Brendon reads his own books and he has a wonderful voice.

* [How to Organize (Just About) Everything: More Than 500 Step-by-Step Instructions for Everything from Organizing Your Closets to Planning a Wedding to Creating a Flawless Filing System by Peter Walsh](https://www.amazon.com/Organize-About-Everything-Step-Step/dp/0743254945/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=upjourney-20&linkId=9c99e29acd7421c9567634971c9ef5c9&language=en_US)  
  When I started my organizing business, *How to Organize (Just About) Everything* was a great resource. Peter is funny and down to earth and sees disorganization and clutter as a problem to be solved, not a character flaw. For visual learners, the checklists and step by step instructions are really helpful and while the book covers a lot of ground, I skipped anything that did not pertain to my organizing work.

* [It's All Too Much: An Easy Plan for Living a Richer Life with Less Stuff by Peter Walsh](https://www.amazon.com/Its-All-Too-Much-Living/dp/0743292650/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=upjourney-20&linkId=6c74e7045cfee29cf8c0497cf213e19c&language=en_US)  
  *It’s All Too Much* remains a favorite of mine because it really taught me to get to the “why” of organizing and how the clutter and disorganization in our lives drain us of the potential to live our best life. We create roadblocks in our lives with our stuff and by eliminating anything that’s holding us back and holding us down, we can step more fully into our lives. This book, *It’s All Too Much*, was a catalyst for writing my own book.


* [The Four Agreements by Don Miguel Ruiz](https://www.amazon.com/Four-Agreements-Practical-Personal-Freedom/dp/1878424319/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=upjourney-20&linkId=9e593a8eec54e1a35596e2fa3434da0c&language=en_US)  
  Don Miguel Ruiz’ *The Four Agreements* is a masterful work reminding us that by being kind to ourselves and others, we create a more beautiful, peaceful and intentional world. The folklore that Ruiz uses in the book may not resonate with every reader – I have to admit that I struggled with it a bit – but his message is positive and powerful. In a nutshell, be impeccable with your word; don’t take anything personally; don’t make assumptions, and always do your best. The premise may seem simple but it’s in the execution that we struggle. Living an intentional life is based on kindness – to ourselves and others and the world around us; Ruiz gives us a roadmap to get there.

* [The 7 Habits of Highly Effective People by Stephen Covey](https://www.amazon.com/Habits-Highly-Effective-People-Powerful/dp/1451639619/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&linkCode=ll1&tag=upjourney-20&linkId=949d9c56cf3ba6baf651e8506de19ac8&language=en_US)  
  I can’t finish this list without adding Stephen Covey’s *The 7 Habits of Highly Effective People*. Covey emphasizes over and over (and over) that we create the life we have by the choices we make and the habits we continue. While this might not seem to be a book about living intentional, it’s actually really effective in outlining how we have to act in order to create our best, intentional life. Covey’s number-one principle is to be proactive and I couldn’t agree more. When we react to situations, we are usually fearful and defensive. Being proactive doesn’t mean we don’t have fear; it just means we choose to face the fear and act positively and decisively anyway. Some of the content feels a little dated but the message remains powerful and transformative.

## **Habits** {#habits}

* [The Power of Habit](https://www.amazon.com/Power-Habit-What-Life-Business/dp/081298160X/ref=sr_1_2?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1522450940&sr=1-2&keywords=the+power+of+habit+by+charles+duhigg) by Charles Duhigg  

* [Atomic Habits: An Easy & Proven Way to Build Good Habits & Break Bad Ones](https://www.amazon.com/Atomic-Habits-Proven-Build-Break-ebook/dp/B07D23CFGR/ref=pd_sim_351_3?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=B07D23CFGR&pd_rd_r=de99ba18-edb5-11e8-b5f3-4fa8805058f7&pd_rd_w=cmMQy&pd_rd_wg=u7Bnh&pf_rd_i=desktop-dp-sims&pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_p=18bb0b78-4200-49b9-ac91-f141d61a1780&pf_rd_r=K42XX8PK5NWW3R1V1RCN&pf_rd_s=desktop-dp-sims&pf_rd_t=40701&psc=1&refRID=K42XX8PK5NWW3R1V1RCN) by James Clear

* [The Checklist Manifesto](https://www.amazon.com/Checklist-Manifesto-How-Things-Right/dp/0312430000/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533944750&sr=8-1&keywords=The+Checklist+Manifesto+by+Atul+Gawande) by Atul Gawande

* [The Seven Habits of Highly Effective People](https://www.amazon.com/Habits-Highly-Effective-People-Powerful-ebook/dp/B01069X4H0/ref=sr_1_3?ie=UTF8&qid=1533944891&sr=8-3&keywords=The+Seven+Habits+of+Highly+Effective+People) by Steven R. Covey  
  * By changing your mindset to embrace an alternative perspective, Covey walks you through the self-mastery Paradigm Shift. This process is broken down into Independence, Interdependence, and Continual Improvement, resulting in meaningful and consistent growth.

* [The Compound Effect](https://www.amazon.com/Compound-Effect-Darren-Hardy/dp/159315724X/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1533944919&sr=8-1&keywords=The+Compound+Effect+by+Darren+Hardy) by Darren Hardy  
  * How was your day today? If not so good, you’re future isn’t looking so good either. What you do on a daily basis determines everything about your life. Small things become big things. The things you do every day — whether good or bad — compound over time. If you have good habits, your future will explode with exponential goodness. If bad, the opposite.

* [5 Habits That Let Emotionally Intelligent People Adapt To Anything](https://www.fastcompany.com/40514381/5-habits-that-help-emotionally-intelligent-people-adapt-to-change) by Harvey Deutschendorf 

* [Mindful Relationship Habits: 25 Practices for Couples to Enhance Intimacy, Nurture Closeness, and Grow a Deeper Connection](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B078HYGSRJ/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_hsch_vapi_tkin_p1_i1) by S.J. Scott, Barrie Davenport

* [10 Minute Mindfulness: 71 Habits for Living in the Present Moment](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B071HVMVVR/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_hsch_vapi_tkin_p1_i2) by S.J. Scott, Barrie Davenport

* [Habit Stacking: 127 Small Changes to Improve Your Health, Wealth, and Happiness](https://www.amazon.com/gp/slredirect/picassoRedirect.html/ref=pa_sp_atf_digital-text_sr_pg1_1?ie=UTF8&adId=A03272551MA9FHOSKJUAT&url=%2FHabit-Stacking-Changes-Improve-Happiness-ebook%2Fdp%2FB06XP2B5QC%2Fref%3Dsr_1_1_sspa%3Fkeywords%3Dhabit%2Bstacking%26qid%3D1575164061%26s%3Ddigital-text%26sr%3D1-1-spons%26psc%3D1&qualifier=1575164061&id=6510708512608636&widgetName=sp_atf) by S.J. Scott and J. Green  

* [Hooked: How to Build Habit-Forming Products](https://www.amazon.com/Hooked-How-Build-Habit-Forming-Products-ebook/dp/B00LMGLXTS/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Hooked%3A+How+to+Build+Habit-Forming+Products&qid=1575164155&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Nir Eyal and Ryan Hoover 

* [Breaking The Habit of Being Yourself: How to Lose Your Mind and Create a New One](https://www.amazon.com/Breaking-Habit-Being-Yourself-Dispenza-ebook/dp/B006M7A8JI/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Breaking+The+Habit+of+Being+Yourself%3A+How+to&qid=1575164176&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Dr. Joe Dispenza

* [Rewire: Change Your Brain to Break Bad Habits, Overcome Addictions, Conquer Self-Destructive Behavior](https://www.amazon.com/Rewire-Your-Brain-Negativity-Toughness-ebook/dp/B08235XC2Q/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=Rewire%3A+Change+Your+Brain+to+Break+Bad+Habits&qid=1575164232&s=digital-text&sr=1-1) by Richard O'Connor

———————————————————

## **Productivity and Success** {#productivity-and-success}

* [Smarter Faster Better: The Secrets of Being Productive in Life and Business](https://www.amazon.com/Smarter-Faster-Better-Productive-Business/dp/B017WRCV0A/ref=sr_1_2?keywords=Smarter+Faster+Better%3A+The+Secrets+of+Being+Productive+in+Life+and+Business&qid=1575173015&s=books&sr=1-2) By Charles Duhigg  
  (annotated by [Jo Ilfeld](http://twitter.com/joilfeld)) Duhigg combines the latest research in productivity and effectiveness to explain how to become “better” at work. Not only does Duhigg combine cutting-edge productivity and the neuroscience of how we learn, but he does it with incredibly engaging stories that make it a fun summer read as well.

* [The Slight Edge: Secret to a Successful Life](https://www.amazon.com/Slight-Edge-Secret-Successful-Life/dp/0967285550/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1534008902&sr=8-1&keywords=The+Slight+Edge%3A+Secret+to+a+Successful+Life) By Jeff Olson    
  (annotated by [Marlo Higgins](https://mobile.twitter.com/marlohiggins?p=s)) I read this three times last year. Olson shares that your philosophy creates your attitude, your actions and your results, which ultimately create your life. Olson shares that the keys to your success come from the habits of your daily activities compounded over time. Very powerful\!

* [The Road to Excellence: The Acquisition of Expert Performance in the Arts and Sciences, Sports and Games](https://www.amazon.com/Road-Excellence-Acquisition-Performance-Sciences/dp/0805822321/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=The+Road+to+Excellence%3A+The+Acquisition+of+Expert&qid=1575173052&s=books&sr=1-1) by [Anders Ericcson](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anders_Ericsson)

* [The 7 habits of highly effective people](https://www.amazon.com/Habits-Highly-Effective-People-Powerful/dp/1451639619/ref=sr_1_3?ie=UTF8&qid=1517743148&sr=8-3&keywords=The+7+habits+of+highly+effective+people) by Steven Covey (classic for personal effectiveness)

## **Bias** {#bias}

* [The Urgency of Intersectionality](https://www.ted.com/talks/kimberle_crenshaw_the_urgency_of_intersectionality)  
  Kimberlé Crenshaw uses the term "intersectionality" to describe this phenomenon; as she says, if you're standing in the path of multiple forms of exclusion, you're likely to get hit by both. In this moving talk, she calls on us to bear witness to this reality and speak up for victims of prejudice.

* [Re:Work \- Unbiasing](https://rework.withgoogle.com/subjects/unbiasing/)

* [Down Girl: The Logic of Misogyny](https://www.amazon.com/Down-Girl-Misogyny-Kate-Manne/dp/0190604980/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1541255657&sr=8-1&keywords=down+girl#customerReviews) by Kate Manne. An exploration of misogyny in public life and politics.

## **Humanity and Society**  {#humanity-and-society}

* [A Short History of Nearly Everything](https://www.amazon.com/Short-History-Nearly-Everything/dp/076790818X/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1523752396&sr=1-1&keywords=A+Short+History+of+Nearly+Everything) by Bill Bryson

* [Prometheus Rising](https://www.amazon.co.uk/gp/product/1561840564/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1634&creative=6738&creativeASIN=1561840564&linkCode=as2&tag=livleaevo-21) by Robert Anton Wilson    
* [Astrophysics for People in a Hurry](https://www.amazon.com/Astrophysics-People-Hurry-deGrasse-Tyson/dp/0393609391/ref=pd_sim_14_2?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=0393609391&pd_rd_r=PZX4JRPV7A60D7FE7QSQ&pd_rd_w=kAgZO&pd_rd_wg=oJVqC&psc=1&refRID=PZX4JRPV7A60D7FE7QSQ) by Neil deGrasse Tyson  
* [The Selfish Gene](https://www.amazon.com/Selfish-Gene-Anniversary-Landmark-Science/dp/0198788606/ref=sr_1_3?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1523752316&sr=1-3&keywords=gene) by Richard Dawkins  
* [The Gene: An Intimate History](https://www.amazon.com/Gene-Intimate-History-Siddhartha-Mukherjee/dp/1476733503/ref=pd_sim_14_7?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=1476733503&pd_rd_r=SBDZHYHAWVH1F25KQ4E6&pd_rd_w=CfBJy&pd_rd_wg=EULM6&psc=1&refRID=SBDZHYHAWVH1F25KQ4E6) by Siddhartha Mukherjee  
* [Sapiens: A Brief History of Humankind](https://www.amazon.com/Sapiens-Humankind-Yuval-Noah-Harari-ebook/dp/B00ICN066A/ref=sr_1_3?ie=UTF8&qid=1542821752&sr=8-3&keywords=Yuval+Noah+Harari) by Yuval Noah Harari  
* [Homo Deus: A Brief History of Tomorrow](https://www.amazon.com/Homo-Deus-Brief-History-Tomorrow-ebook/dp/B01BBQ33VE/ref=sr_1_4?ie=UTF8&qid=1542821752&sr=8-4&keywords=Yuval+Noah+Harari) by Yuval Noah Harari  
* [21 Lessons for the 21st Century](https://www.amazon.com/Lessons-21st-Century-Yuval-Harari/dp/0525512179/ref=pd_sim_14_10?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=0525512179&pd_rd_r=SBDZHYHAWVH1F25KQ4E6&pd_rd_w=CfBJy&pd_rd_wg=EULM6&psc=1&refRID=SBDZHYHAWVH1F25KQ4E6) by Yuval Noah Harari (Bill Gates [review](https://www.gatesnotes.com/Books/21-Lessons))  
* [The Laws of Human Nature](https://www.amazon.com/dp/B07BJLX414/ref=dp-kindle-redirect?_encoding=UTF8&btkr=1) by Robert Greene    
* [Origin Story: A Big History of Everything](https://www.amazon.com/Origin-Story-Big-History-Everything/dp/0316392006/ref=pd_sim_14_1?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=0316392006&pd_rd_r=f43daaf9-fe24-11e8-9f8f-c706d394337b&pd_rd_w=d54Qk&pd_rd_wg=TaQln&pf_rd_p=18bb0b78-4200-49b9-ac91-f141d61a1780&pf_rd_r=XH2NFEBMZTQMJ60GWT6N&psc=1&refRID=XH2NFEBMZTQMJ60GWT6N) by David Christian  
* [How Behavior Spreads: The Science of Complex Contagions](https://www.amazon.com/How-Behavior-Spreads-Contagions-Analytical/dp/0691175314/ref=sr_1_2?crid=3A3IIB3M7WJV5&keywords=How+behavior+spreads&qid=1569935020&sprefix=solid+st%2Caps%2C164&sr=8-2) by Damon Centola   ([summary](https://wilte.wordpress.com/2018/10/17/how-behavior-spreads-the-science-of-complex-contagions-damon-centola/))  
* [The Empathic Civilization](https://www.amazon.com/Empathic-Civilization-Global-Consciousness-Crisis/dp/1585427659) by Jeremy Rifkin  [TED talk](https://www.ted.com/talks/jeremy_rifkin_on_the_empathic_civilization)   
  For Rifkin, the central paradox of human existence is, and has always been, the conflict between empathy and entropy: while globalization brings together diverse people, the very good-a rise in "empathic awareness" \- is counterbalanced by the very bad \- "dramatic deterioration of the health of the planet," by way of the technology that drives progress. Though wordy, Rifkin provides a thorough, lucid overview of mankind's history along the "empathy/entropy" spectrum. The Empathic Civilization speaks to our despair when we confront the horrific effects of global warming, financial meltdown, and war. Rifkin says that our customary feeling, thinking, and acting are no longer relevant to the world we have created and that humanity is on the cusp of its greatest experiment: to refashion our consciousness in order to live and flourish in the new globalizing society.

* [Winners Take All: The Elite Charade of Changing the World](https://www.amazon.com/Winners-Take-All-Charade-Changing/dp/110197267X/ref=sr_1_1?crid=1EOKYNZERFM6Z&keywords=winners+take+all&qid=1575473821&sprefix=10%25%2Caps%2C156&sr=8-1) by Anand Giridharadas   [NYTimes review](https://www.nytimes.com/2018/08/20/books/review/winners-take-all-anand-giridharadas.html)  
  Groundbreaking investigation of how the global elite's efforts to "change the world" preserve the status quo and obscure their role in causing the problems they later seek to solve. An essential read for understanding some of the egregious abuses of power that dominate today’s news. Anand Giridharadas takes us into the inner sanctums of a new gilded age, where the rich and powerful fight for equality and justice any way they can—except ways that threaten the social order and their position atop it. They rebrand themselves as saviors of the poor; they lavishly reward “thought leaders” who redefine “change” in ways that preserve the status quo; and they constantly seek to do more good, but never less harm.  

* [The Master Switch](https://www.amazon.com/Master-Switch-Rise-Information-Empires/dp/0307390993) by Tim Wu. The Master Switch is for anyone who wants to understand the struggle for open communication, information control, freedom, and accountability of government and large institutions. Throughout history, controlling information subverted and corrupted the public good. Western Union controlled telegraphs and threw a presidential election. AT\&T invented magnetic tape (hard disks), but squashed it for decades because it threatened the core telephone business. After documenting this process throughout history, Tim Wu suggests we treat information infrastructure like we treat journalism: A necessary pillar of a healthy democracy that requires protection.

## **Economics   ([top 10 economics books](https://www.wallstreetmojo.com/top-best-economics-books/))** {#economics-(top-10-economics-books)}

* [The Green and the Black: The Complete Story of the Shale Revolution, the Fight over Fracking, and the Future of Energy](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1250080665) by Gary Sernovitz 

* [The Economists' Hour: False Prophets, Free Markets, and the Fracture of Society](https://www.amazon.com/Economists-Hour-Prophets-Markets-Fracture-ebook/dp/B07MFKR1VG/ref=sr_1_1?keywords=the+economist+hour&qid=1579443126&sr=8-1) by Binyamin Appelbaum

* [The Wealth of Nations: Annotated](https://www.amazon.com/Wealth-Nations-Annotated-Adam-Smith/dp/1611040485/ref=sr_1_1_sspa?crid=1N7N377H8L6XL&keywords=adam+smith+wealth+of+nations&qid=1566748202&s=gateway&sprefix=adam+smith%2Caps%2C155&sr=8-1-spons&psc=1&spLa=ZW5jcnlwdGVkUXVhbGlmaWVyPUEzUjVFRVhXOFNIRU5HJmVuY3J5cHRlZElkPUEwNjQ3Mzc4MVhEUllBSUQzUFBTQyZlbmNyeXB0ZWRBZElkPUEwNzAwNDkxMklTQkVVU0FUSVBDOSZ3aWRnZXROYW1lPXNwX2F0ZiZhY3Rpb249Y2xpY2tSZWRpcmVjdCZkb05vdExvZ0NsaWNrPXRydWU=) by Adam Smith  
* [The Big Short](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0393338827/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=mannyb-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=0393338827&linkId=c049964b0aabfe29115d5850a8131f0b) by Michael Lewis  
* [Fault Lines](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0691152632/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=mannyb-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=0691152632&linkId=5779b8340daeba4ad7cc52dd713500de) by Raghuram G. Rajan  
* [Too Big to Fail](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0143118242/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=mannyb-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=0143118242&linkId=fa1c989b49c9b5aa43a6827980176f20) by Andrew Ross Sorkin

* [The Most Important Thing](http://www.wisdomordata.com/books/#) by Howard Marks  
* [Free to Choose](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0156334607/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=mannyb-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=0156334607&linkId=924f6b3603fd5f9a19a182642197e75a) by Milton Friedman  
* [Reminiscences of a Stock Operator](https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0471770884/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=mannyb-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=0471770884&linkId=04930d8e08082d6df258a93df3a51044) by Edwin Lefevre  
* [Why Nations Fail: The Origins of Power, Prosperity, and Poverty](https://www.amazon.com/Why-Nations-Fail-Origins-Prosperity/dp/0307719219/ref=sr_1_3?gclid=CjwKCAjw44jrBRAHEiwAZ9igKPq0NSwFwBv0dQ0bVrY1nHgn16lILSYlS-2GwzyS_5bFVXOrzEW0PBoCqgkQAvD_BwE&hvadid=241631334693&hvdev=c&hvlocphy=1018127&hvnetw=g&hvpos=1t1&hvqmt=e&hvrand=8349721154710978702&hvtargid=kwd-36902240028&hydadcr=21875_10169765&keywords=why+nations+fail&qid=1566748330&s=gateway&sr=8-3) by Daron Acemoglu and James A. Robinson   
* [Misbehaving: The Making of Behavioral Economics](https://www.amazon.com/Misbehaving-Behavioral-Economics-Richard-Thaler/dp/039335279X/ref=sr_1_1?crid=2MQASTOPLZFI7&keywords=misbehaving+richard+thaler&qid=1566747919&s=gateway&sprefix=misbehaving%2Caps%2C143&sr=8-1) by Richard H. Thaler

  Nobel laureate Richard H. Thaler has spent his career studying the radical notion that the central agents in the economy are humans―predictable, error-prone individuals. Misbehaving is his arresting, frequently hilarious account of the struggle to bring an academic discipline back down to earth―and change the way we think about economics, ourselves, and our world.


* [Capital in the Twenty-First Century](https://www.amazon.com/Capital-Twenty-First-Century-Thomas-Piketty/dp/0674979850/ref=asc_df_0674979850/?tag=hyprod-20&linkCode=df0&hvadid=312065696873&hvpos=1o1&hvnetw=g&hvrand=10843984435910367053&hvpone=&hvptwo=&hvqmt=&hvdev=c&hvdvcmdl=&hvlocint=&hvlocphy=1018127&hvtargid=pla-347358723827&psc=1&tag=&ref=&adgrpid=61316180399&hvpone=&hvptwo=&hvadid=312065696873&hvpos=1o1&hvnetw=g&hvrand=10843984435910367053&hvqmt=&hvdev=c&hvdvcmdl=&hvlocint=&hvlocphy=1018127&hvtargid=pla-347358723827) by Thomas Piketty

  Piketty, arguably the world’s leading expert on income and wealth inequality, documents the growing concentration of income in the hands of a small economic elite. He makes a powerful case that we’re on the way back to ‘patrimonial capitalism,’ in which the commanding heights of the economy are dominated not just by wealth, but also by inherited wealth, in which birth matters more than effort and talent.

* [People, Power, and Profits: Progressive Capitalism for an Age of Discontent](https://www.amazon.com/People-Power-Profits-Progressive-Capitalism/dp/1324004215/ref=sr_1_1?crid=130D02JF5A5ES&keywords=people%2C+power+and+profits&qid=1577390051&sprefix=gift%2Caps%2C316&sr=8-1) by Joseph E. Stiglitz 

  Stiglitz identifies the true sources of wealth and of increases in standards of living, based on learning, advances in science and technology, and the rule of law. He shows that the assault on the judiciary, universities, and the media undermines the very institutions that have long been the foundation of America’s economic might and its democracy. An authoritative account of the predictable dangers of free market fundamentalism and the foundations of progressive capitalism.

* [Anti-Piketty: Capital for the 21st-Century](https://www.amazon.com/Anti-Piketty-Capital-21st-Century-Emmanuel-Martin/dp/1944424253/ref=pd_sbs_14_2/134-5932411-3709530?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=1944424253&pd_rd_r=02c6dc6e-9ccb-4a7d-ac50-07c1f2995e50&pd_rd_w=gKC66&pd_rd_wg=296Cz&pf_rd_p=5873ae95-9063-4a23-9b7e-eafa738c2269&pf_rd_r=E2PM9Y1B8TTJKHAZBAXT&psc=1&refRID=E2PM9Y1B8TTJKHAZBAXT) by Emmanuel Martin et al

  Collects the Piketty criticisms from twenty specialists―economists, historians and tax experts―who provide scientific and rigorous arguments against Piketty's central theses. These researchers, who come from many countries and many backgrounds, examine the notions of inequality, growth, wealth and capital that Piketty treated in his book. They show in new ways how inequality did not explode, the rich are not rentiers but rather entrepreneurs who take risks and create millions of jobs, that wealth can not indefinitely grow faster than economic growth, and that radical taxation does not solve problems but aggravates them.

## **Politics and American Society** {#politics-and-american-society}

* [The Populist Explosion: How the Great Recession Transformed American and European Politics](https://www.amazon.com/dp/0997126442/?coliid=I11MMMNJJM1KGD&colid=E2P2OAQS8S5Y&psc=0&ref_=lv_ov_lig_dp_it) by John B. Judis

* [The Clash of Civilizations and the Remaking of World Order](https://www.amazon.com/Clash-Civilizations-Remaking-World-Order/dp/1451628978/ref=pd_sim_14_5?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_i=1451628978&pd_rd_r=66fa3c65-0eac-11e9-976d-331c5380a38c&pd_rd_w=UNNXg&pd_rd_wg=YTeLK&pf_rd_p=18bb0b78-4200-49b9-ac91-f141d61a1780&pf_rd_r=SY3MZY7EQ1N6MX6WPH7V&psc=1&refRID=SY3MZY7EQ1N6MX6WPH7V) by Samuel P. # **The Future** {#the-future}

## **Machine Intelligence** {#machine-intelligence}

* [Superintelligence: Paths, Dangers, Strategies](https://amzn.to/348lzFo) by Nick Bostrom  
  It begs the questions about whether AI with save or destroy humanity. As it stands right now, nothing is more intelligent and powerful than the human brain. If machine superintelligence becomes more powerful than humans, what will happen next?

* [Our Final Invention](https://amzn.to/2Ree2Q9) by James Barrat  
  This book discusses how AI could become humanity’s competitors. Barrat begs the question of whether or not people can coexist with something that could become more powerful over time.
